Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Legal Stratagem for Wife of Absent Non-Maintaining Husband
Problem-solution format – hila for wife of absent non-maintaining husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct and apply the Hanafi-adopted Maliki hila to obtain judicial separation (tafriq) for a wife from an absent husband who fails to provide nafaqah.

Core Idea
When the absent husband provides no nafaqah, the qadi can separate the spouses after due process, following the Maliki hila.

This passage presents a practical legal stratagem (hila) from the Hanafi tradition, drawing on the Maliki school, for a wife whose husband is absent (gha'ib ghair mafqud) and fails to provide maintenance. It begins by describing her predicament and poses two questions: whether she can separate and remarry, and what happens if the husband returns. The answer outlines a stepwise procedure that begins with seeking khul' and patience, and only as a last resort employs a Maliki process involving the qadi. Our goal is to parse this procedure and understand its conditions and application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and legal constraints
The husband is absent but not missing (gha'ib ghair mafqud), does not provide nafaqah, does not divorce, and does not make any arrangement. The wife is distressed. Recognize that in Hanafi fiqh, tafriq for non-maintenance is not normally granted, hence a hila is needed.
The distinction between mafqud (missing) and gha'ib ghair mafqud (absent but known) is crucial; different rules apply.
2
Understand the hierarchy of recommended solutions
First, try to persuade the husband to agree to khul' (divorce initiated by wife with compensation). If that fails, patience is advised. Only when maintaining a chaste life becomes impossible does the Maliki hila become permissible.
The Hanafi default is patience; the hila is an exception due to dire necessity.
3
List the elements that must be proven before the qadi
The wife must file a case, prove the marriage through witnesses, prove that the husband left without providing maintenance and did not send any, prove she did not waive maintenance, and take an oath on these matters. This establishes the husband's obligation and negligence.
All these elements are required for the qadi to proceed.
4
Outline the qadi's warning and waiting period
If no one takes responsibility for her maintenance, the qadi sends a notice to the husband with three options: come and fulfill rights, arrange maintenance, or divorce. If none, the qadi orders a one-month wait. If still unresolved, the qadi effects separation (tafriq).
The one-month wait is from the Maliki narration.
5
Note the consequence and re-petition right
If someone takes maintenance responsibility but then abandons it, the woman can re-file. After tafriq, if the original husband returns and is willing to provide, she does not automatically revert; the passage implies she remains separated.
The hila results in a permanent separation, not a revocable divorce.

غائب غیر مفقود کی بیوی کیلئے ایک سہولت حضرات اللہ کے متفقہ فیصلہ کے ساتھ اس عورت کی رہائی کے لیے جو صورت صحیح ہے وہ تو یہ ہے کہ اس کے شوہر کو ضلع پر رضامند کیا جائے اگر شوہر خلع پر بھی رضامند نہ ہو تو پھر اگر یہ عورت مبر کے ساتھ با صمت زندگی گزار سکے تو بہتر ہے ورنہ جب نان و نفقہ اور گذر اوقات کے لیے کوئی صورت ممکن نہ ہو تو سخت مجبور نہیں یہ بھی گنجانش ہے کہ مذہب مالکیہ کے موافق مندرجہ ذیل صورت اختیار کر کے رہائی حاصل کرے؟
وہ صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت قاضی کے پاس مقدمہ پیش کر کے گواہان سے اُس غائب شخص کے ساتھ اپنا نکاح ہونا ثابت کرے پھر یہ ثابت کرے کہ وہ مجھ کو نفقہ دے کر نہیں گیا اور نہ وہاں سے اُس نے میرے لیے نفقہ بھیجا۔ نہ یہاں پر نفقہ کا کوئی انتظام کیا اور نہ میں نے نفقہ معاف کیا غرض نفقہ کا واجب ہونا بھی اس کے ذمہ ثابت کرے اور یہ بھی کہ وہ اس واجب کی ادائیگی میں کوتاہی کہ رہا ہے ان تمام امور پر حلف بھی کرے اس کے بعد اگر کوئی عزیز قریب یا اجنبی عورت کے نفقہ کی ذمہ داری لے تو بہتر ہے ور نہ قامتی اس شخص کے پاس حکم یعنی نوٹس بھیجے کہ یا تو تم حاضر ہو کر اپنی بیوی کے حقوق ادا کر دیا اُس کو بلالو (آباد کرو) یا وہیں ہی نان و نفقہ کا کوئی انتظام کرو ورنہ اس کو طلاق دے دو اگر تم نے ان باتوں میں سے کوئی بات نہ کی پھر ہم خود تم دونوں میں تفریق واقع کر دیں گے اگر اس بات پر بھی شوہر کوئی صورت قبول نہ کرے تو قامتی ایک مہینہ کے مزید انتظار کا حکم دے اس زمانہ میں بھی اگر اس کی شکایت ختم نہ ہوئی تو اس صورت کو اس غائب شخص کے نکاح سے علیحدہ کردے جیسا کہ روایت و ۱۲ و ۲۴ و ۲۶ سے ثابت ہے ۔ اور یہی ظاہر ہے کہ تفریق کے لیے کسی شخص نے اگر نفقہ کی ذمہ داری سے لی لیکن پھر چھوڑ دیا تو عورت کو دوبارہ قاضی کے یہاں مقدمہ پیش کرنے کا حق حاصل ہے ۔
کے یعنی دو معتبر افراد سے جس کی بحث آگے مذکور ہے۔
که قنادی مالکیہ کی روایت ۳ رت میں جس کا حوالہ آگے آرہا ہے یہ بات تو واضح ہے کہ یہ مات ، شہر قاضی کے سامنے دعوی کرنے کے بعد ہو گی لیکن اس روایت میں نائب کے پاس آدمی بھیجنے سے کوئی تعاری نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے یہ بھی معلوم نہ ہوسکا کہ یہ دنت آدمی بھیجے جانے کے بعد ہو گی یا پہلے سے، ہم نے آدمی بھیجے جانے کے بعد سمجھ کر اختیار دیا ہے۔
He neither comes himself nor calls his wife to him, nor makes any arrangement for her expenses, nor divorces her. Due to this, the woman is distressed and worried. So is there any way for her to separate herself from the marriage of that absent husband and marry elsewhere? (2) In the case of separation, if after separation, before another husband or after marrying another, that person returns and is ready to arrange food and maintenance, will the wife be returned to him? And if she is returned, under what conditions and with what detail does she return? The answer: For the wife of an absent but not missing (gha'ib ghair mafqud) husband, there is a facility with the agreed ruling of the scholars of Allah. The correct course for the release of this woman is that the husband be made to agree to divorce (khul'). If the husband does not agree even to khul', then if this woman can live a chaste life with patience, it is better. Otherwise, when there is no possible means for food, maintenance, and livelihood, then it is not severe constraint. It is also permissible that, according to the Maliki school, she adopt the following course to obtain release: That course is that the woman files a case before the qadi and, through witnesses, establishes her marriage with that absent person. Then she establishes that he did not leave maintenance for me, nor did he send maintenance from there, nor did he arrange any maintenance here, nor did I waive maintenance. In short, she proves the obligation of maintenance upon him and that he is negligent in paying this obligation. She also takes an oath on all these matters. After that, if any relative or stranger takes responsibility for the woman's maintenance, it is better. Otherwise, the qadi sends a notice (hukm) to that person: either you come and fulfill your wife's rights, call her (settle her), or arrange maintenance there, or divorce her. If you do not do any of these things, then we will ourselves effect separation between you. If even then the husband does not accept any course, then the qadi orders a further wait of one month. If during this time also her complaint does not end, then he separates her from that absent person's marriage, as is established from narrations 12, 24, and 26. And it is apparent that for separation, if someone took responsibility for maintenance but then abandoned it, the woman has the right to file a case again before the qadi. That is, from two reliable persons, the discussion of which will come later. Regarding the Maliki narration in which the reference will come later, it is clear that this (order) will be after filing the claim before the qadi, but in this narration, there is no mention of sending a person to the deputy (na'ib). Therefore, it could not be known whether this (order) will be after sending the person or before. We have given the choice assuming it is after sending the person.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) from the Hanafi tradition, drawing upon the Maliki school's ruling, for a wife whose husband is absent (gha'ib ghair mafqud) and fails to provide maintenance. The passage is a problem-and-solution format. It first describes the wife's predicament: the husband is absent, does not provide maintenance, does not divorce her, leaving her distressed. It then poses two questions: (1) Can she separate and remarry? (2) If she remarries and the original husband returns willing to provide, does she revert to him? The answer begins by noting that the preferred solution is to persuade the husband to agree to khul' (divorce initiated by wife with compensation). If that fails, patience is advised if possible. If the situation becomes unbearable (dire necessity), then it is permissible to adopt the Maliki procedure. The steps: (a) file a case before the qadi, (b) prove the marriage through witnesses, (c) prove that the husband left without providing maintenance and did not send any, and that she did not waive it, (d) she takes an oath on these matters, (e) if someone takes responsibility for her maintenance, good; otherwise, the qadi sends a notice to the husband with three options: come and fulfill rights, arrange maintenance, or divorce; if none, the qadi threatens to separate them, (f) after a month's wait, if the situation persists, the qadi separates them. The authority for this is based on certain narrations (12, 24, 26) from the Maliki school. The passage also notes that if someone takes responsibility for maintenance but then abandons it, the woman can re-petition. The text ends with a discussion about the timing of the order relative to sending a person to the husband, acknowledging ambiguity in the Maliki narration.

Key Terms
غائب غیر مفقود (gha'ib ghair mafqud): An absent husband whose whereabouts are known, as opposed to one who is missing (mafqud) with no news.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter owed by the husband to the wife.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation between spouses ordered by a qadi.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife, usually with compensation to the husband.
قاضی (qadi): Islamic judge who oversees the case and can effect tafriq.
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome without violating sacred law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first recommended step for the wife when her husband is absent and not providing maintenance?
A) Immediately seek judicial separation
B) Try to persuade the husband to agree to khul' (divorce initiated by wife)
C) File a case before the qadi
D) Marry another man

Key Takeaway
The wife of an absent non-maintaining husband can obtain judicial separation through a qadi-supervised procedure, but only after exhausting khul' and patience, and following the Maliki hila.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

Legal Stratagem for Wife's Maintenance Against Absent Husband
Legal stratagem for wife's maintenance against absent husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the legal stratagem (hila) for a wife to claim maintenance from an absent husband under Hanafi law, including the procedural steps, conditions, and exceptions for judicial separation.

Core Idea
A wife can obtain maintenance and judicial separation from an absent husband through a qadi-supervised process using two witnesses, not mere correspondence.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najiyah details the complete procedure for a wife whose husband has disappeared without providing maintenance. As a hila (legal stratagem), it allows her to secure her rights without falling into the prohibited. The lesson walks through the proof, the qadi's notice, the options, and the final separation. Understanding this process is essential for muftis dealing with modern cases of desertion.

Guided Path
1
Establish the wife's claim
The wife must prove four facts before the qadi: (1) the husband left without providing maintenance, (2) he did not send maintenance from elsewhere, (3) he did not arrange any maintenance locally, and (4) she did not waive maintenance. She must also take an oath that the husband is negligent in fulfilling this obligation. This establishes the burden of proof.
The oath is crucial; without it, the claim may be weakened.
2
Attempt voluntary maintenance
Before the qadi sends a notice, it is recommended (mustahab) that a relative or stranger voluntarily undertakes to pay the wife's maintenance. This can resolve the issue without formal legal action.
This step is not obligatory but is encouraged to avoid escalation.
3
Qadi sends notice via two witnesses
If no voluntary maintenance is arranged, the qadi sends a notice to the absent husband through two reliable witnesses. The notice gives three options: return and fulfill the wife's rights, arrange maintenance from afar, or divorce her. The witnesses must deliver the notice in person and testify to the husband's response. Sending by post or mail is insufficient.
This procedure is based on both Hanafi and Maliki practice, as cited in the text.
4
One-month waiting period
If the husband refuses all options or does not respond, the qadi orders a one-month waiting period. If the situation does not improve, the qadi can annul the marriage (tafriq) based on the husband's persistent neglect.
The waiting period gives the husband one final chance to comply.
5
Exceptional case: inaccessible husband
If the husband is in a location so remote that sending a notice is impossible despite all efforts, the qadi may proceed without sending a notice. The qadi investigates the matter and, after following the same essential procedure (proof, oath, one-month wait), can order separation. This exception is based on a narration from Ibn Abidin.
This exception applies only when all possible methods of communication have failed.

اگر غائب، غیر مک وغیرہ میں ہو ایسی جگہ پر ہو کہ جہاں پر پوری جدوجہد اور امکانی کوشش کے باوجو د بھی کسی کو بھیجنے کا امکان نہ ہو سکے تو مذکورہ بالا مجبوری کے وقت اس کی بھی گنجائش ہے کہ بغیر کسی کو بھیجے ہوئے حاکم (شرعی) یا اُس کے قائم مقام وغیرہ کے بغیر حاکم شرعی، واقعہ کی تحقیق کرکے حسب ضابطہ مذکورہ بالا کے بعد تفریق کا حکم کر دے جیسا کہ حضرت علامہ اعضا با شم کی دسویں الفا

That she should prove that he did not give her maintenance when leaving, nor did he send her maintenance from there, nor did he arrange any maintenance here, and she did not forgive the maintenance. In short, she should establish that maintenance is obligatory upon him, and that he is negligent in paying this obligation. She should also take an oath on all these matters. After that, if any relative or stranger takes responsibility for the woman's maintenance, it is better. Otherwise, the qadi should send a notice to that person (the husband) that either you come and fulfill your wife's rights, call her (settle her), or arrange food and maintenance there, or give her divorce. If you do none of these, then we ourselves will cause separation between you two. If even then the husband does not accept any option, then the qadi orders a further one-month wait. If during this time her complaint is not resolved, then he separates her from the marriage of that absent person, as is proven by narrations 12, 24, and 26. And it is apparent that for separation, if someone had taken responsibility for maintenance but then abandoned it, the woman has the right to present the case again to the qadi. Regarding two reliable witnesses, the discussion will come later. For the Maliki narration whose reference will come later, it is clear that this will be after making a claim before a qadi. But in that narration, there is no discussion about sending a person to the deputy (absentee), so it could not be determined whether this will be after sending a person or before. We have chosen to adopt it after sending a person. The demand is conditional upon receiving the answer. So if after the absent person's answer arrives, the woman abandons the demand, then separation will not be effected. Necessary note regarding sending notice: If the qadi sends a notice to that absent person via postal mail etc., it is not sufficient. Rather, the correct procedure is that the qadi should give the order (notice) to two reliable individuals to hear it and hand it to them, saying take it to the absent person. These two individuals should deliver the writing to the absent person, ask for his response (i.e., take his reply to the claim) so that they may return and testify on it, and if the person gives any response, they should testify to it. In summary, the qadi should make his decision based on the testimony of these two, and not consider mere correspondence sufficient. And this practice is clearly proven from the Maliki school and the Hanafi school, as is clear from the book Al-Qadi ila al-Qadi. And Allamah Dardir has stated that it is necessary for those two witnesses to testify that this is the writing of such-and-such qadi (or shari’a court) and that that qadi made them witnesses to this writing which they bring with them. If the absent husband is in a faraway land, if the absent is in an inaccessible place such that it is impossible to send anyone despite full effort and possible exertion, then in such a compulsion, there is also leeway that without sending anyone, the shari’a ruler (or his deputy etc.)—the shari’a ruler—may investigate the matter and after the above-mentioned procedure, order separation, as is found in the narration of Hazrat Allamah Ibn Abidin (tenth century?).
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents a complete hila (legal stratagem) from the Hanafi school for the problem of a wife whose husband has absconded without providing maintenance. The teacher (Ashraf Ali Thanwi) lays out the procedure step by step. First, the wife must prove three things in court: (1) that maintenance was obligatory on the husband, (2) that he failed to provide it either by leaving without giving, not sending from elsewhere, not arranging locally, and (3) that she did not waive it. She must also take an oath that he is negligent in fulfilling this obligation. Then, if no one voluntarily undertakes to pay her maintenance, the qadi sends a notice to the absent husband giving him three options: take her back and fulfill her rights, arrange for her maintenance at his location, or divorce her. If he does none, the qadi warns that he will separate them. If the husband still refuses, the qadi orders a one-month waiting period. If the situation does not improve, the qadi annuls the marriage. The passage also specifies procedural details: the notice must be delivered by two reliable witnesses, not by mail. This is based on both Maliki and Hanafi practice. However, if the husband is in an inaccessible place where sending messengers is impossible, the qadi may proceed without sending a notice, as per a narration from Ibn Abidin. This lesson is crucial for Hanafi muftis handling modern cases of missing husbands.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance and financial support owed by husband to wife, including food, clothing, and lodging.
غائب (gha'ib): A husband who is absent from the wife's location, not present to fulfill marital obligations.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation or annulment of marriage ordered by the qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required method for sending a qadi's notice to an absent husband regarding maintenance?
A) By registered post
B) By two reliable witnesses who deliver and testify
C) By the wife herself
D) By a single messenger

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi legal stratagem for an absent husband's maintenance requires proof, oath, and qadi notice delivered by two witnesses; only when the husband is unreachable may the qadi proceed without notice, based on Ibn Abidin.

Concluding Rulings on the Missing Husband (Mafqud)
Concluding rulings on 'iddah, mahr, and remarriage in the mafqud case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on 'iddah, mahr, and remarriage in the case of a missing husband (mafqud), identifying the condition of khulwah sahihah as decisive.

Core Idea
Khulwah sahihah with the second husband triggers full mahr and 'iddah, even without actual intercourse.

This final passage from Thanwi's Hila-e-Najija consolidates the key consequences when a wife of a missing husband remarries and then the first husband returns. The ruling hinges on whether there was valid seclusion (khulwah sahihah) with the second husband. If yes, full mahr is due and 'iddah must be observed in the first husband's home; if not, the mahr is dropped and 'iddah is not required. The 'iddah prohibits the first husband from intimacy until it ends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The wife of a missing husband (mafqud) remarries, then the first husband returns. The second marriage is annulled. Determine if valid seclusion (khulwah sahihah) occurred with the second husband.
Khulwah sahihah is private seclusion unimpeded by any barrier.
2
Apply the 'iddah ruling
If khulwah sahihah occurred, 'iddah is obligatory (wajib). During the 'iddah, the first husband cannot have intercourse with her. The 'iddah must be spent in the first husband's house.
Contrary to a common error, the 'iddah is not in the second husband's house.
3
Apply the mahr ruling
For the second husband, if khulwah sahihah occurred, full mahr is wajib; otherwise mahr is completely dropped.
This applies even if the second marriage was annulled before consummation.
4
Consider other annulments (sair al-fusukh)
The same detail applies to other annulments where a woman remarries and the first husband reappears. The condition of khulwah sahihah governs the obligations.
The passage references earlier narrations (29–34) for detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے خلوت صحیحہ ہو چکی ہو تو عدت واجب ہے۔ یعنی عدت گزرنے سے پیشتر شوہر اول کو جماع اور اُس کے دوائی کا اور نہ کاب جائز نہیں- كما في الرواية التاسعة والعشرين الى الرابعة والثلاثین ۔ اور شوہر ثانی کے ذمہ مہر واجب ہونے میں وہی تفصیل ہے جو مفقود کے بیان میں گذر چکی یعنی اگر اس سے خلوت صحیحہ ہو چکی ہے تو پورا واجب ہے ورنہ بالکل ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیا ھونکو سائر الفسوخ و نیز احکام مفقود میں یہ بھی گزر چکا ہے کہ عدت شوہر اول کے مکان میں گزارے گی ۔ فلنظر تو فقد او الله اعلم بالصواب واليه المرجع والماب وههنا تمت الرسالة -
If valid seclusion has occurred, then 'iddah is obligatory. That is, before the completion of 'iddah, it is not permissible for the first husband to have intercourse or to have medicine [؟] or anything else. As in the twenty-ninth to thirty-fourth narrations. And regarding the obligation of mahr on the second husband, the same detail has passed in the discussion of the missing husband: i.e., if valid seclusion has occurred with him, then the full mahr is obligatory; otherwise it is completely dropped. And similarly for other annulments. In the rulings of the missing husband, it has also passed that she will spend her 'iddah in the house of the first husband. So consider, then, or (wa) Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the abode. And here the treatise ends.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on the legal stratagem (hila) for the missing husband (mafqud). The author reiterates key rulings: If a woman remarries after her husband's disappearance and has valid seclusion (khulwah sahihah) with the second husband, she must observe an 'iddah after the second marriage is annulled (due to the first husband's return). During that 'iddah, the first husband cannot have marital relations with her. The mahr for the second husband depends on whether valid seclusion occurred: if yes, full mahr is due; if not, no mahr. The 'iddah is to be spent in the first husband's home, as per earlier discussion. The author then concludes the treatise with praise to Allah.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khulwah sahihah): Private seclusion between a married couple that is not impeded by any legal or physical barrier, considered a basis for certain legal effects.
عدت ('iddah): Waiting period a woman must observe after separation or death of her husband before remarrying.
مہر (mahr): Mandatory dower given by the husband to the wife upon marriage.
مفقود (mafqud): A person whose whereabouts are unknown and whose life status is uncertain, specifically a missing husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the first husband divorces her
B) If valid seclusion (khulwah sahihah) occurred with the second husband
C) If the marriage is annulled by a judge
D) If the second husband consummated the marriage

Key Takeaway
In the mafqud case, the condition of khulwah sahihah with the second husband determines both the obligation of 'iddah and full mahr.

Methodology of Faskh Nikah in the Absence of a Qadi: Taqlid and Collective Fatwa
Introduction explaining the need and methodology for additional faskh nikah cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological steps taken by the author of al-Hilah al-Najizah to resolve faskh nikah cases without a qadi, and identify the role of Maliki taqlid and collective decision-making in Hanafi iftaa.

Core Idea
In the absence of a qadi, a Muslim committee adopting the Maliki position can legitimately annul marriages — a pragmatic Hanafi fatwa methodology.

This passage introduces a supplement to the well-known treatise al-Hilah al-Najizah. The author explains why three additional faskh nikah cases are being added and, more importantly, the methodological basis: necessity-driven adoption of the Maliki madhhab and the formation of a substitute qadi committee. This lesson unpacks this methodology, showing how Hanafi muftis historically navigated legal voids.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
The text begins by stating that certain faskh nikah cases require a qadi, but in India (and similar contexts) a shari'i qadi and a Muslim ruler's court may be absent. Recognize this as the core problem necessitating a legal workaround.
This is a classic darurah (necessity) situation.
2
Unpack the Solution: Substitute Qadi
The unanimous decision was that a congregation of Muslims (jama'at muslimin) acting as a shari'i committee can serve as a substitute qadi. This is a departure from the standard Hanafi requirement of an individual qadi, justified by necessity.
The committee follows the Maliki madhhab on the substantive faskh rules.
3
Analyse the Process: Addition of New Cases
Three additional faskh cases were not presented to the full consultative body due to practical delays and because they were already based on the Maliki madhhab adopted earlier. This shows a pragmatic approach to updating fatwa collections.
The author prioritizes timely implementation over exhaustive consensus.
4
Evaluate the Methodology
This is a blend of cross-madhhab taqlid (taking the Maliki view on faskh), collective ijma (unanimity of the consulted scholars on the substitute qadi), and istihsan (juristic preference to meet necessity). It exemplifies the flexibility of Hanafi iftaa.
The method is not arbitrary but grounded in usul al-fiqh principles.

Source Text

Supplement to the treatise called al-Mukhtarat on important matters of separation and options. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. After praise and salutations, it is stated that for those issues where the need for annulment of marriage or separation by a qadi arises, and due to the absence of a qadi there is difficulty, the treatise al-Hilah al-Najizah li al-‘Ailah al-‘Ajizah was written with utmost investigation and precision, after consultation with many verified scholars. In it, it was unanimously decided that in India, wherever there is no shari‘i qadi and it is not possible to obtain a shari‘i ruling from any Muslim ruler’s court, then the congregation of Muslims—[i.e.] the shari‘i committee—following the Maliki madhhab shall be considered as a substitute qadi. After the completion of this treatise, it was felt necessary that besides the five issues included in the treatise, there are three more situations where the need for annulment of marriage arises and difficulties occur due to the absence of a qadi. These should also be included in this treatise so that all necessary issues are collected together. However, these three issues were not presented to all the aforementioned scholars, because besides the fact that presenting them to all would cause great delay, a greater need for these issues was not felt, since most of them were a decision by way of consultation from a part of the Muslim congregation, which was taken from the Maliki madhhab, and that is in the original treatise...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is the introductory section of a supplement to the risalah al-Mukhtarat, itself an appendix to al-Hilah al-Najizah. The author explains the background and methodology. The core ruling is that in the absence of a shari‘i qadi and a Muslim ruler's court, a committee of Muslims can act as a substitute qadi, following the Maliki madhhab. This was a unanimous decision. The supplement adds three more cases for faskh nikah that were not in the original five. These three were not reviewed by the full consultative body due to practical delays, and they are primarily based on the Maliki madhhab, which had already been adopted in the original treatise. The passage reflects the practical legal reasoning (istihsan and necessity) characteristic of Hanafi fatwa methodology when dealing with exigencies.

Key Terms
الحيلة الناجزة (al-hilat an-najizah): The effective legal stratagem, a treatise addressing solutions for marriage annulment when a qadi is absent.
جماعة مسلمين (jama'at muslimin): A committee of Muslims acting as a substitute qadi in the absence of a shari'i qadi, following the Maliki madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The local imam of the mosque
D) Any adult male Muslim

Key Takeaway
In the absence of a qadi, a Muslim committee adopting the Maliki madhhab can act as a substitute qadi for faskh nikah, justified by necessity and unanimous scholarly agreement.

Talfiq in Hurmah Musaharah and the Role of the Muslim Assembly
Explaining talfiq and the Muslim assembly's ruling on hurmah musaharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the permissibility of talfiq in the context of hurmah musaharah and identify the conditions under which a Muslim assembly's ruling is considered independent.

Core Idea
Talfiq is permissible only when actions are separate; the Muslim assembly's ruling is a single action, not talfiq.

This lesson explores the strategic use of talfiq—combining rulings from different madhhabs—to resolve a knotty issue in family law: whether zina creates hurmah musaharah. The author of Al-Hilat al-Najijah shows how the Muslim assembly can issue a ruling that avoids the drawback of talfiq by acting as a single authoritative body. We will dissect the legal reasoning behind this hila.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What legal problem is the hila designed to solve? The problem is whether zina (unlawful intercourse) creates hurmah musaharah (prohibition of marriage to certain relatives). The Hanafi school says yes, the Maliki school (relied-upon view) says no.
The difference creates a practical difficulty: if a man commits zina, he cannot marry the woman's daughter according to Hanafi, but Maliki allows it.
2
State the general principle of talfiq
Talfiq (combining rulings from multiple madhhabs) is permissible only when the actions being combined are separate (mutafarriq). It is not allowed if it violates ijma' or a clear text.
The governing qawida: If actions are separate, talfiq is permissible (إذا تعددت الأعمال جاز التلفيق).
3
Analyze the potential talfiq in the assembly's ruling
The Muslim assembly decides on hurmah musaharah using the Maliki view (that zina does not cause prohibition). This appears to combine a Hanafi procedure (assembly acting as qadi) with a Maliki substantive ruling. Why might this be considered talfiq?
Some might argue it combines two different madhhabs in one action.
4
Apply the author's resolution
The author clarifies that the assembly's judgment is a single independent action because the assembly acts as a qadi (judge). Thus, it is not combining multiple actions; it is one authoritative ruling.
The assembly's decision stands alone as a hila (legal stratagem), not as talfiq.
5
Evaluate the hila
What condition makes this valid? The assembly must be recognized as a single authority (like a qadi), and the ruling must not violate ijma' or a definitive text. Here, the Maliki view is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih), so no ijma' violation occurs.
The hila works precisely because the assembly's ruling is treated as unified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عہ اصل رسالہ کے دیباچہ میں حاشیہ پر یہ مضمون واضح ہو چکا ہے کہ جب در عمل جدا گانہ ہوں تو تلفیقی جائز ہے گر حضرت والا نے مزید اختیاط کے لیے اصل رسالہ میں ایسا کوئی مسئلہ نہیں لیا جس میں تلفیق فارق اجماع لازم آجانےسے اور تمہ کے تین سکوں میں سے بھی دوستوں میں اس کی رعایت موجود ہے جگر صرف اس ایک تمہ .... مسئلہ یعنی حرمت مصاہرت میں جماعت مسلمین کا فیصلہ ایسا ہے جس میں بظاہر تلفیق خارق اجماع لازم آتی ہے یعنی مذہب خفیہ میں تو جماعت مسلمین کا فیصلہ بہتر نہیں اور مالکیہ کے مشہور و مختار مذہب کی بنا پر بعض و کی خاص صورتوں میں مس بالشہوۃ وغیرہ سے حرمت مصاہرت تعلق نہیں ہوتی کو بعض صورتوں میں قول معتمد د مشہور کے موافق اور بعض میں قول غیر مشہورں کے موافق ان کے نزدیک بھی حرمت متعلق ہو جاتی ہے ۔ کہا في مختصر الخليل وشرحه للدردير و في نشر حرمة الزنا خلاف المعتمد منه عدم نشر الحومة ا إلى قوله ( وان حاول زوج تلمذ ذا بزوجية فالته بابنتها منه او من غيره ظانا انها زوجته بوطئه او مقدمة فتردد في تحريم زوجة عليه وهو المرتضى وعدها (م ۲۹ م ) عرض بعض صورتوں میں جماعت مسلمین کے ذریعہ بوجہ حرمت مصاہرت تفریق کرانے میں تلفیق کا شبہ ہو گا لیکن ہم ان کو عمل واحد خیال نہیں کرتے بلکہ جماعت مسلمین کو قاضی کے حکم میں سمجھنا ایک مستقل مسئلہ ہے اور حرمت .
This content has been made clear in the footnote of the preface of the original treatise: When the actions are separate, then talfiq is permissible. However, for extra precaution, the respected author did not include in the original treatise any issue that would necessitate talfiq that violates ijma'. And this precaution is observed in three schools, except in this one issue – namely, the issue of hurmah musaharah – the decision of the Muslim assembly is such that apparently it necessitates talfiq that violates ijma'. That is, in the hidden school, the decision of the Muslim assembly is not famous, and based on the well-known chosen Maliki school, in some specific cases, touching with desire etc. does not cause hurmah musaharah, [while] in some cases, according to the relied-upon opinion of the famous school and in some according to the non-famous opinion, the prohibition attaches. It is said in Mukhtasar al-Khalil and its commentary by al-Dardir: 'Regarding the spread of prohibition due to zina, the contrary of the relied-upon opinion is that it does not spread the prohibition...' up to his statement: 'And if a husband intended to approach his wife, then he had intercourse with her daughter from him or from someone else, thinking she was his wife, or by a preliminary touch, then he is uncertain about the prohibition of his wife upon him, and this is the approved view and its opposite. In some cases, by means of the Muslim assembly, due to hurmah musaharah, there would be suspicion of talfiq, but we do not consider them as a single action; rather, considering the Muslim assembly in the ruling of a qadi is an independent issue and the prohibition...'
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage addresses the concept of talfiq (combining rulings from different madhhabs) and its application to the issue of hurmah musaharah (prohibition due to marriage relationships). The author explains that in his original treatise, he avoided any issue that would require talfiq violating ijma'. However, the ruling of the Muslim assembly on hurmah musaharah appears to involve such talfiq. The author clarifies that this is not true talfiq because the Muslim assembly acts as a qadi, making its judgment a single independent action. The passage cites Maliki opinions on whether zina causes prohibition: the relied-upon view is that it does not, but there is a contrary view. The author concludes that the Muslim assembly's decision does not constitute talfiq of multiple actions but rather a single authoritative ruling. This is a hila (legal stratagem) to resolve practical difficulties without violating principles.

Key Terms
تلفیق (talfiq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs to form a single legal solution, often to avoid hardship.
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmah musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to marriage relationships, e.g., a man cannot marry his wife's mother or daughter.
جماعت مسلمین (jama'at muslimeen): An assembly of Muslims acting as a collective authority in legal matters when no qadi is available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's justification for the Muslim assembly's decision on hurmah musaharah not being considered talfiq?
A) Because it follows the Hanafi school.
B) Because the assembly's judgment is a single independent action, not a combination of multiple actions.
C) Because it only applies to non-consummated marriages.
D) Because it is based on ijma'.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is permissible only when combining separate actions; the Muslim assembly's single judgment is not talfiq.

8 min
Talfiq in Hurmat-e-Musaharat: A Hila for Divorce
Explains the permissibility of talfiq in divorce via hurmat-e-musaharat using a Muslim committee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for valid talfiq in a hurmat-e-musaharat case and apply the procedure using a Muslim committee as a substitute for a qadi.

Core Idea
Talfiq is permissible when actions are separate; the committee's decision and the ruling of hurmat are two independent actions.

This lesson examines a practical hila (legal stratagem) for obtaining a Shar'i separation when no qadi is available. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains how combining a Hanafi position (on the ineffectiveness of a Muslim committee) with the Maliki position (on the causes of hurmat-e-musaharat) can be permissible through talfiq, provided the two actions are treated as separate. We will walk through the procedure, the potential pitfall of breaking consensus, and the precautionary measures to take.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Problem
The scenario: a woman needs a Shar'i divorce but no qadi is present. The Hanafi school normally requires a qadi for such rulings. Identify the need for an alternative.
The author suggests first looking for a Muslim ruler appointed by the government; if none, then a Muslim committee (jamāʿat al-muslimīn) may be used, based on the Maliki school.
2
Recognize the Potential Talfiq Issue
Talfiq (combining rulings across madhhabs) can be problematic if it breaks consensus (ijmāʿ). Here, the Hanafi school does not accept the committee's authority, while the Maliki school does. Combining these seems to break consensus.
The author argues that the committee's authority and the ruling of hurmat-e-musaharat are separate actions; thus talfiq is not applied to a single action but to two independent processes.
3
Apply the Separation Principle
Understand the principle: talfiq is permissible when actions are separate. Here, one action is the committee acting as a qadi (a procedural matter), and the other is the establishment of hurmat (a substantive matter). They are independent; combining them does not break consensus.
Analogous to wudu and prayer being separate actions; one can take rulings from different madhhabs for each.
4
Evaluate the Maliki Position on Hurmat
Within the Maliki school, there is ikhtilāf on whether touching with lust or zina establishes hurmat-e-musaharat. The well-known (mashhūr) position is that it does not, but there is a non-renowned (ghayr mashhūr) view that it does. The committee can choose the appropriate opinion.
The author cites Mukhtasar al-Khalīl and its commentary to show the Maliki ikhtilāf.
5
Formulate the Procedure and Precautions
The procedure: present the case to the committee, stating the act (e.g., touching with lust) without explicitly claiming zina to avoid the risk of hadd al-qadhf if four witnesses cannot be produced. Then the committee declares separation based on the Maliki view. The precaution is to consult a qualified scholar before acting.
The author advises against explicitly mentioning zina in the claim; instead, describe the act euphemistically.

He should obtain the ruling of Shar'i separation, and in a place where there is no qadi, if there is a Muslim ruler appointed by the government who handles such matters, then the case should be presented before him. Otherwise, according to the Maliki school, one should refer to the Muslim community (Shar'i committee). The detailed explanation of the Muslim community (Shar'i committee) has already passed in another part of this book. It is apparent that the intent is not established except by the husband's statement, so there is no benefit of this difference for the woman in what I have counted, and if the difference appears as a benefit in a certain situation, then the more precautionary is to accept the statement of the one who requires separation by statement, especially in the case of supervening corruption. This subject has already been clarified in the margin of the preface of the original treatise, that when actions are separate, talfiq is permissible. However, the revered one, due to extra caution, did not include any such issue in the original treatise where talfiq would necessitate breaking consensus. And among the three schools, this is also observed in the other two, except for this one issue, namely the ruling of hurmat-e-musaharat. The decision of the Muslim community in this matter is such that apparently talfiq would necessitate breaking consensus. That is, in the Hanafi school, the decision of the Muslim community is not effective, and based on the well-known and chosen Maliki school, in some specific cases, such as touching with lust, hurmat-e-musaharat is not established; in some cases, according to the relied-upon statement, and in others, according to the non-renowned statement, according to them also hurmat is established. It is said in Mukhtasar al-Khalil and its commentary by al-Dardir: 'The spreading of prohibition due to zina, contrary to the relied-upon, from it is the non-spreading of prohibition... up to his saying: And if a husband attempts to touch a woman with the intention of marriage, then her daughter from him or from another, thinking she is his wife, through intercourse or foreplay, then he hesitates regarding the prohibition of his wife upon him, and that is the approved view and its count.' In some cases, through the Muslim community, due to hurmat-e-musaharat, there will be doubt of talfiq in effecting separation. But we do not consider them as a single action; rather, considering the Muslim community as the authority of a qadi is one independent issue, and calling hurmat-e-musaharat a cause for separation is another independent issue, just as wudu is a separate action and prayer is separate. And the shaykh has already mentioned this in the margin of the preface of the original treatise. So there will be a doubt of talfiq. Thus, this form of talfiq is permissible according to us, which is also supported by a narration of the fatwa of 'Allamah Muhammad ibn 'Ali Baydawi, the mufti of the Malikis. Nevertheless, at the time of action, the precaution is that the one who acts should refer to a verified scholar of his own conviction regarding the permissibility of talfiq and act upon his fatwa. And Allah knows best. One thing worth remembering is that if an act of zina has occurred, then in the claim, zina should not be explicitly mentioned, because if four witnesses cannot be produced for the claim of zina, then there is the fear of hadd of qadhf. Rather, only illicit contact etc. should be mentioned, such as saying that the private part was brought to the private part without a barrier.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage discusses a hila (legal stratagem) concerning talfiq (patchwork of rulings from different madhhabs) in the matter of hurmat-e-musaharat (prohibition due to marriage relations) and divorce. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains that in places where no qadi is present, if there is a Muslim ruler appointed by the government, the case should be presented to him. Otherwise, according to the Maliki school, one may refer to a Muslim committee (jamaat-e-muslimin). The author then clarifies that talfiq is permissible when the actions are separate; here, the decision of the committee and the ruling of hurmat are considered separate actions, so talfiq does not break consensus. He cites the Maliki view that hurmat does not always arise from zina or touching, but in some cases it does, and the Muslim committee's decision can be based on the appropriate Maliki opinion. The precaution is to consult a qualified scholar. Additionally, the author advises not to explicitly mention zina in the claim to avoid the risk of hadd al-qadhf (punishment for false accusation) if four witnesses are unavailable; instead, one should describe the act euphemistically. This is a practical hila to achieve a Shar'i separation while adhering to legal safeguards.

Key Terms
تلفیق (talfīq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs in a single case or action to produce a desired outcome.
حرمت مصاہرت (ḥurmat muṣāharat): Prohibition of marriage due to certain relationships arising from marriage or illicit contact (e.g., between a man and his wife's mother if he touched her with lust).
جماعت مسلمین (jamāʿat al-muslimīn): A collective body of Muslims (committee) acting in place of a qadi in matters of Shar'i separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why should zina not be explicitly mentioned when claiming hurmat-e-musaharat?
A) Because zina is not a valid ground for separation in Hanafi fiqh
B) Because if four witnesses are unavailable, the claimant risks punishment for qadhf
C) Because the Maliki school does not consider zina as a cause for prohibition
D) Because the Muslim committee cannot hear cases involving zina

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is a valid tool for resolving practical difficulties, provided the actions combined are separate and consensus is not broken; in hurmat-e-musaharat cases, a Muslim committee can effect divorce using the Maliki position.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
advanced
8 min
The Wife's Stratagem When the Husband Denies Prohibition by Affinity
Legal stratagem for wife when husband denies prohibition by affinity and swears falsely.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal stratagem (hila) when a wife's claim of prohibition by affinity is dismissed due to the husband's false oath, identifying the conditions and the role of a third witness.

Core Idea
A wife must not submit to a husband after a false oath; lawful separation is required even if the court dismisses her claim.

When a wife claims that a prohibited affinity (e.g., fosterage or illicit intercourse) has occurred, but she lacks evidence and the husband swears falsely, the court may dismiss her case. However, this does not mean the marriage is lawful. The Hanafi school provides a legal stratagem: the wife must not voluntarily cohabit and must seek separation through divorce or other lawful means. This lesson examines the ruling, the role of third-party witnesses, and the conditions of the hila.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Understand the scenario: the wife claims a prohibition by affinity (e.g., hurmat al-musaharah) due to an act like fosterage or touch. She has no evidence; the husband denies and takes a false oath.
The husband's belief: if he knows the truth, his denial is haram.
2
Analyze the court's ruling
The judge dismisses the claim because the husband's oath settles the case outwardly. But the judge does not order the wife to remain; he simply rejects her case.
The judge may or may not explicitly order cohabitation.
3
Apply the hila conditions
List the conditions for the wife's stratagem: her claim is true, no evidence, husband's false oath, lack of court order to stay. The wife must not willingly submit; she must seek a divorce or separate by lawful means.
If the judge orders her to stay, additional guidance is needed.
4
Examine the third party's status
A third person who knows the truth is a witness, not a defendant. His statement is testimony, not admission. His testimony is acceptable if he is just and does not confess to a disqualifying sin.
This distinction is based on the qawida: informing about another's right is not admission.
5
Implement the fatwa
The mufti advises the wife to avoid the husband and use lawful means for separation. The husband's false oath is a sin but binds the court outwardly. The wife should not take the law into her own hands.
This hila balances the wife's rights and the constraints of court procedure.

کے ساتھ یہ کم بھی کردیا کہ بدستور اس شو ہر کی زوجیت میں رہے تو اس صورت میں عورت کو نمککن جائز ہے یا نہیں اس کے متعلق نہ تو کوئی جزئیہ ملا اور نہ قواعد سے کچھ احقر کی فہیم ناقص میں آیا اور خود غور و تلاش کے بعد جب مولانا محمد شفیع صاحب مفتی دارالعلوم دیوبند سے مکالمت پر بھی مسئلہ حل نہ ہوا توحضرت حکیم الامت دامت برکاتہم سے مراجعت کی حضرت نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ قواعد سے صاف واضح ہے کہ اس صورت
Fosterage prohibition. As for the wording of the oath, it is taken from what is in al-Shamiyya from al-Fath, and the prohibition is established by touching it, conditioned that he believes her and it occurs in his predominant opinion that she is truthful. And on this, it should be said regarding his touching that it does not forbid his father and son unless they believe her or it is predominant in their opinion that she is truthful. Then I saw from Abu Yusuf something indicating that. End (Shami 25 vol.2). So it is apparent that in those incidents from which the prohibition of affinity is established, there is also the participation of another with one of the spouses, and that other knows the validity or invalidity of the incident and also the presence or absence of desire. But despite much searching, no instance has been found where his statement is taken in the case or not, and if his statement is taken, what status does it have? However, after reflection on the rules, the opinion is that he is not a defendant, therefore he should not be made a defendant and forced to give a statement, but rather he should be considered a witness. Because informing about a right of another against another is not an admission but a testimony, and an admission is imposing a right upon himself for another, as is clearly stated in the books of fiqh. And regarding whether his testimony is acceptable, the detail is that if that person is just in terms of his other actions and statements, and in this incident he does not admit to any act that nullifies his integrity, for example, if he gives a statement of intercourse by doubt etc., then there is no hesitation in his testimony being accepted. And if he describes an act that proves his transgression, then will his testimony be acceptable or not? There is hesitation due to multiple reasons. When necessary, research the books of the madhhab and the scholars. However, if he is a man, his testimony is an admission against himself: if he later marries a woman who is among the ascendants or descendants of that woman, or if he already has such a woman in his marriage, then the above ruling applies. As is not hidden. And Allah knows best what is correct. If the husband has a predominant belief that such an incident definitely occurred that necessitates the prohibition of affinity, then denying it is forbidden. If he made a false oath and the judge passed a decision upon it, then its detail will come shortly in the second issue. If the wife's claim was true but evidence could not be presented and the husband took an oath, so the judge dismissed the case, i.e., he did not separate them and did not order her to remain in marriage, then it is not permissible for the wife to give the husband power over her person by her own choice. Rather, she should strive to separate herself from him through divorce or other means. If no stratagem works, then as long as she can, she should not let the husband come near her. It is said clearly in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: 'Whoever heard from her husband the three divorces and did not believe her...' And if the judge, along with rejecting the wife's claim, also ruled that she remain in the husband's marriage as before, then in this case, is it permissible for the wife to remain with him? Regarding this, no specific case was found, nor did my poor understanding grasp anything from the rules. After personal reflection and discussion with Maulana Muhammad Shafi, Mufti of Darul Uloom Deoband, the issue was not resolved. So I consulted Hadrat Hakim al-Ummat (may his blessings endure). He said: 'From the rules, it is clearly evident that in this case...'
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a wife whose husband denies an event that would establish a prohibition of affinity (such as fosterage or illicit intercourse) and swears falsely, leading to a court dismissal of her claim. The passage begins by citing a ruling from Shami and Fath regarding the conditions of oaths and prohibition by touch. It then discusses the role of a third person who knows the truth: such a person is neither a defendant nor a forced witness; his statement is considered testimony, not admission. The text distinguishes between informing about another's right (testimony) and imposing a right on oneself (admission). The third person's testimony is acceptable if he is just and does not admit to a sinful act that would disqualify him. The core hila is that when the wife's claim is true but she lacks evidence and the husband swears falsely, the judge dismisses the case but does not order her to stay. In this situation, the wife must not willingly allow the husband access; she must strive to obtain a divorce or other lawful separation. If the judge additionally orders her to remain, then the author sought an opinion from senior scholars and Hakim al-Ummat, who indicated that per the rules, there is a clear ruling (though the text cuts off). The passage emphasizes that the husband's denial is haram if he believes the incident occurred, and his false oath is a grave sin, but the court's decision based on it is binding outwardly. The wife's stratagem is not to rebel against the court but to use lawful means to separate, such as seeking divorce or not cohabiting.

Key Terms
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmat al-musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to affinity, arising from valid or invalid intercourse or touch with desire.
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath taken in court, here false oath denying the event causing prohibition.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given by a witness about a right of another, not about his own right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To accept the court's ruling and continue married life.
B) To file an appeal with new evidence.
C) To avoid the husband and seek lawful separation.
D) To request a retrial based on her own testimony.

Key Takeaway
When a wife's claim of prohibition by affinity is dismissed due to the husband's false oath, she must not cohabit and must pursue lawful separation; third parties who know the truth are witnesses, not defendants.

The Effect of a Qadi's Ruling on Inner Reality: Tamkin After a False Oath
Fatwa on wife's duty to refuse tamkin after false oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a qadi's ruling based on false testimony does not change the internal hukm, and state the wife's duty in a case of alleged hurmat musaharah.

Core Idea
A qadi's ruling does not make the haram halal internally when based on falsehood.

This fatwa addresses a delicate family law scenario: a wife claims an incident that would create a permanent marital prohibition, but cannot prove it, while the husband denies and swears a false oath, leading the qadi to dismiss the case. The central question is whether the wife must then allow her husband sexual access. The answer reveals a fundamental principle in Hanafi jurisprudence: the qadi's ruling only affects the outward, not the inner reality when based on false evidence. We will parse this ruling step by step, identifying the governing qawida and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute and the cause
The wife alleges an incident that triggers hurmat musaharah (permanent prohibition due to marital relationship). The husband denies it and swears an oath. The qadi, lacking proof, dismisses the case. Determine what exactly is contested: the fact of the incident, not the ruling itself.
The husband's false oath is key; the qadi acts on apparent evidence.
2
Extract the primary ruling for the wife
The fatwa states that the wife must not permit tamkin. She should seek separation (talaq) and avoid the husband physically. Identify the direct ruling and its source (al-Durr al-Mukhtar).
This applies even if the qadi only dismissed the case without ordering continuation.
3
Analyze the complication: qadi orders continuation
The author considers a scenario where the qadi explicitly orders the wife to remain. This case lacked a direct precedent, so the author consulted other scholars. Note how the problem is refined.
The qadi's order does not change the wife's inner knowledge.
4
Uncover the underlying legal maxim (qawida)
Hakim al-Ummat (Ashraf Ali Thanwi) explains that the qadi's ruling on this matter is analogous to a ruling on property based on false testimony. Just as such a ruling does not make the property halal for the lying claimant, here the ruling does not make intercourse halal. Extract the qawida: 'Hukm al-qadi la yughayyir al-batin' (the qadi's ruling does not alter the inner reality).
This principle distinguishes between external and internal rulings.
5
Apply the qawida to derive the final fatwa
Since the wife knows the truth, she must act according to her inner knowledge. Tamkin remains haram. This is the mufta bihi position, affirmed by Shaykh Muhammad Shafi' and Hakim al-Ummat. The student should be able to articulate this application.
The final ruling relies on the consensus of later authorities.

There is hesitation due to multiple reasons. At the time of need, one should investigate from the books of the madhhab and scholars. However, if this is a man, then the testimony he gave is an acknowledgement in his own favor. If in the future he marries a woman who is among the ascendants or descendants of that woman, or if he already has such a woman in his marriage, then the ruling will be as taken from above. As is not hidden. And Allah knows best the correct. If the husband has a dominant presumption that such an incident definitely occurred which necessitates the prohibition of marriage relationship, then denying it is forbidden. If he swore a false oath and the qadi gave a ruling upon it, its detail will come soon in the second issue. If the wife's claim was true but she could not produce [؟] testimony, and the husband took an oath, therefore the qadi dismissed the case — meaning he did not separate them nor did he order them to continue in marriage — then it is not permissible for this wife to allow her husband power over herself by her own choice. Rather, she should strive to separate herself from him through talaq or the like, and if no measure is effective, she should not let this husband come near her as long as she can. It is stated explicitly in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: 'Whoever heard from her husband a threefold divorce but did not prove it [؟].' Rather, this order is like the ruling on mutlaq properties based on false testimony, and by this order, [؟] is not proven for anyone.' And he also said: 'I have full satisfaction in this; there is no hesitation.' And the aforementioned mufti also agreed, but this humble one did not attain satisfaction. Perhaps Allah will bring about something after this. In any case, it is apparent that as long as the permissibility of letting him have intercourse is not proven with satisfaction from a specific case or from the rules, acting upon the instruction of Hadhrat is obligatory. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fatwa ruling on a scenario where a wife claims an incident that would cause marital prohibition (hurmat musaharah), but the husband denies and swears an oath, leading the qadi to dismiss the case. The primary issue is whether the wife is then obliged to allow the husband sexual access (tamkin). The passage first addresses the husband's internal duty: if he is genuinely convinced the incident occurred, it is haram for him to deny it. If he swore falsely and the qadi ruled, details will come later. Then it addresses the wife's situation: she is not permitted to let him have intercourse; she must seek separation via talaq or other means, and if that fails, she must avoid him physically. This is based on texts from al-Durr al-Mukhtar. A further complication arises if the qadi explicitly orders the wife to remain in the marriage. The author consulted Mawlana Muhammad Shafi' and then Hakim al-Ummat (Ashraf Ali Thanwi), who ruled that even in that case, tamkin is not permissible because the qadi's order is not like a ruling on the contract itself; it is analogous to a ruling on property based on false testimony, which does not affect internal reality. Thus, the wife must act according to what she knows inwardly. This is the final relied-upon position.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmat musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to a relationship established through marriage (e.g., husband's sexual contact with wife's mother becomes prohibition).
تمکین (tamkin): The wife allowing her husband sexual access.
حكم القاضي لا يغير الباطن (hukm al-qadi la yughayyir al-batin): The qadi's ruling does not change the inner reality; it only affects the outward situation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) She can only avoid him if she has witnesses to the original incident.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a qadi's ruling based on false evidence does not alter the internal hukm; the wife who knows the truth must avoid tamkin and seek separation even if the qadi orders continuation.

Exercising Khiyar al-Bulugh: Conditions for Virgin and Non-Virgin
Explains the rules of khiyar al-bulugh for bikr and thayyib with conditions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for exercising khiyar al-bulugh for a virgin (bikr) and a non-virgin (thayyib) and apply the Hanafi rules to determine when the option is valid or lost.

Core Idea
A virgin must reject immediately upon knowledge; a non-virgin retains the option indefinitely until explicit or implicit consent.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah clarifies the procedural rules for exercising khiyar al-bulugh, the right of a minor married by a non-father guardian to annul upon puberty. Understanding the distinction between bikr and thayyib is crucial, as it determines whether immediate verbal rejection is required or whether silence preserves the option. This lesson examines the conditions, exceptions, and the role of consent, drawing directly from Hanafi relied-upon sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the party's status
Determine whether the minor is a bikr (virgin) or thayyib (non-virgin). This classification dictates the immediacy requirement and witness obligations.
Thayyib includes those who have had intercourse in valid marriage, shubha, void marriage, or widely known zina.
2
Establish the timing of knowledge
When did the minor learn of the marriage? If before puberty, the option arises at puberty. If after puberty, the option arises upon receiving news.
The immediacy rule is calculated from the moment of knowledge, not puberty per se.
3
Apply the immediacy rule for bikr
A bikr must verbally reject the marriage immediately upon knowledge, without delay, unless there is a valid excuse (e.g., coughing, forced silence). If she delays even slightly without excuse, the option is lost.
Verbal rejection must be explicit, e.g., 'I am not pleased with this marriage'.
4
Apply the rule for thayyib and ghulam (boy)
A thayyib (or a boy) does not need to reject immediately. Silence alone does not void the option. The option remains until explicit or implicit consent occurs (e.g., saying 'I accept', kissing with consent, intercourse).
Implicit consent must be proven; mere silence is not consent.
5
Consider witnesses and procedural requirements
A bikr should have two men or one man and two women witness her rejection for proof before a judge. A thayyib or boy does not need witnesses; their claim suffices.
Witnesses are for evidentiary purposes, not validity of the rejection itself.

Source Text

Immediately, without any delay, she must say with her tongue: 'I am not pleased with this marriage.' Whether someone is present with her or not, in every case, saying it immediately with the tongue is a condition. However, if due to coughing or sneezing etc., she was unable to speak immediately, or someone forcibly shut her mouth, then the delay caused by this constraint does not invalidate the option of annulment, provided that as soon as the constraint is removed, she says it immediately. And if without any constraint, there is even a slight delay in saying it with the tongue, the option becomes void, and it is no longer permissible to have it annulled. If she falsely represents and gets it annulled, she will be severely sinful. But if she resorts to a stratagem for annulment, the court's ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly according to Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). And Allah knows best. Also, for a virgin, it is also required that when she says it with her tongue, she makes at least two men or one man and two women witnesses, so that they may be useful when the matter is presented before a judge etc. The detailed ruling of making witnesses will come after the jurisprudential narrations under the title 'Faa'idah'; it must be looked at. And if that girl is a thayyib, then it is not necessary for her to say it immediately; rather, as long as she does not consent, the option to keep or not keep (the marriage) remains, even if much time passes. Merely remaining silent does not invalidate the thayyib's option of puberty. However, if after puberty she says with her tongue that she accepts this marriage, or does an action (that is, one by which intercourse has occurred, whether with this husband or another husband before him), and likewise, a woman who has been intercourse by shubha or through a void marriage, or one who has been flogged for zina or has committed it repeatedly and it is widely known among the people, is also considered thayyib; as in Durr al-Mukhtar, chapter on guardianship, section on the virgin. For example, if the husband, with her consent, takes a kiss etc., or has intercourse, and consent is found in such actions, the option becomes void. And then the thayyib does not need to make witnesses for her rejection. Rather, it is sufficient for her to merely claim: 'I am a thayyib, have attained puberty, and now I wish to annul this marriage.' And the same ruling applies to the boy, i.e., it is not necessary for him to speak immediately upon attaining puberty; rather, as long as he does not consent by word or action, the option remains. So if a boy or a thayyib girl, after puberty, even once says with the tongue that this marriage is accepted, then demanding annulment is forbidden, whether that consent was given in complete solitude or quietly so that no one else heard. Similarly, if after puberty, kissing etc. occurs, then also the option of annulment does not remain. Also, the case of a boy is the same as that of a thayyib which has just passed. And all this detail applies when they were informed of the marriage before puberty. And if someone had no knowledge of the marriage before puberty, then when they receive the news, the option of puberty is acquired. And for the girl and the boy, the consideration of whether the option remains or not, based on the detail that has passed, will be from the time of receiving the news. And all these issues are found in Durr al-Mukhtar with its marginalia by Allamah al-Shami (may Allah have mercy on him), where the author of Durr said: (And the marriage is binding and there is no gross disparity) due to reduction of her dower or increase of his dower? (He married her without compatibility? If the guardian married himself to a non-father or grandfather) and likewise the guardian and the son of a mad woman? (He is not known to have poor judgment? frivolous?)
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah outlines the hila (legal stratagem) for exercising khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) in Hanafi law. The key ruling is that a virgin (bikr) must verbally express her rejection immediately upon learning of the marriage, without any delay, unless she has a valid excuse like coughing or being forcibly silenced. If she delays even slightly without excuse, the option is lost. For a thayyib (a woman who has had sexual relations), immediate verbal rejection is not required; she retains the option as long as she does not explicitly or implicitly consent, even if much time passes. Similarly, a boy (ghulam) is treated like a thayyib. The passage also requires a virgin to have witnesses for her rejection, while a thayyib does not need witnesses—her mere claim suffices. Any act indicating consent, such as kissing or intercourse, voids the option. The time of knowledge matters: if she knew before puberty, the option starts at puberty; if she learns later, it starts at that time. The text references Durr al-Mukhtar and its marginalia, indicating that this is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The right of a minor married by a non-father guardian to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
باکرہ (bikr): A woman who has never had sexual intercourse (virgin).
ثیبہ (thayyib): A woman who has had sexual intercourse, whether in valid marriage, shubha, void marriage, or zina, if known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, what is the difference in exercising khiyar al-bulugh between a virgin (bikr) and a non-virgin (thayyib)?
A) Both must reject immediately upon attaining puberty.
B) The virgin must reject immediately; the thayyib retains the option until she consents.
C) The thayyib must reject immediately; the virgin retains the option until she consents.
D) Neither can reject after puberty.

Key Takeaway
The exercise of khiyar al-bulugh depends critically on whether the minor is a bikr or thayyib, dictating immediacy and witness requirements.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

The Legal Stratagem (Hila) for Khiyar al-Bulugh: Witness Requirement and Permissible Statement
Explaining the witness requirement and the permissible legal fiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal stratagem for khiyar al-bulugh when witnesses are absent, and explain the ruling that a statement technically untrue is permitted under the maxim 'al-kadhib li-ihqaq al-haqq'.

Core Idea
To exercise khiyar al-bulugh, announce repudiation immediately; a permissible lie allows saying 'just reached puberty' to secure witnesses.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najijah addresses a practical problem: a girl married as a minor reaches puberty and wants to annul the marriage (khiyar al-bulugh) but has no witnesses at that moment. Hanafi fiqh requires witnesses for the annulment to be effective. The author outlines a legal stratagem (hila) to resolve this, grounded in the maxim that a lie is permissible to establish a legitimate right (يجوز الكذب لإحقاق الحق). This lesson explains the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Khiyar al-bulugh requires immediate repudiation upon reaching puberty and witnesses to attest the repudiation. Without witnesses, the annulment may be ineffective.
The Hanafi school requires witnesses for khiyar al-bulugh to avoid disputes.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
First: if witnesses are present at the moment of puberty, she states repudiation to them immediately. Second: if no witnesses are present, she must still repudiate immediately verbally, then later find witnesses and formally declare before them.
Immediate verbal repudiation prevents silence from being interpreted as consent.
3
Analyze the hila (legal stratagem)
In the second scenario, when the girl later speaks to witnesses, she should say 'I have just reached puberty' even if she actually reached puberty earlier. She must not reveal the true time.
This statement is a legal fiction to establish her right without risking her annulment being rejected.
4
Evaluate the basis
The permissibility is based on the maxim 'al-kadhib li-ihqaq al-haqq' (lying is permissible to establish a legitimate right). This is a known principle in Hanafi fiqh for certain hiyal.
The author notes a lingering doubt but upholds the ruling from established fiqh works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ارہ کو نکاح نامنظور کرنے کیلئے گواہ ضرور ہیں بارہ لڑکی بالغ ہونے کے بعد جب نکاح نامنظور کرے تو اس کو نا منظوری پر گواہوں کی بھی ضرورت پڑتی ہے جیسا کہ اس سے پہلے گزر چکا ہے لیکن وہ مختصر تھا اس وجہ سے تفصیل لکھی جاتی ہے تفصیل یہ ہے کہ گواہ بنانے کی دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ لڑکی جس وقت بالغ ہوئی ہے اُس وقت اگر اس کے پاس گواہ موجود ہیں جب تو اُسی وقت اُسی کو کہہ دینا چاہیئے کہ ہمیں اب بالغ ہوتی ہوں اور اس نکاح کو فسخ کرانا چاہتی ہوں ۔ بالغہ کو نکاح، زد کرنے کیلئے اگر فورا نہ مل سکیں دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اس وقت گواہ موجود نہ ہوں اس صورت میں زبان سے فوراً نا منظور کر کے گواہوں کو بلایا جائے یا خود ان کے پاس چلی جائے اور گواہ جلدی مل جائیں یا دیہ سے ملیں بہر صورت ان کے سامنے یہی کہنا چاہیے کہ میں اب بالغ ہوئی ہوں اور نکاح فسخ کرانا چاہتی ہوں ہرگز یہ بات ظاہر نہ کرے کہ میں ابھی کچھ دیر ہوئی بالغ ہوتی ہوں ۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر گواہ واضح طور پر بھی معلوم کریں کہ تم کب بالغ ہوئی ہو ؟ جب بھی تفصیلی طور پر واقعہ بیان نہ کرے بلکہ یہی جواب ہے کہ میں اب بالغ ہوئی ہوں یا صرف اس قدر کہہ دے له ويجوز الكذب لا جاء الحق كا هو مصر فى هذا الباب من كتب الفقد وفى البواب أخر ولكن يختلج في القلب اما جوز والتفريق بعض قولها عند القاضي الي فسخت كما اتى
For a girl to reject marriage, witnesses are necessary. When a girl after reaching puberty rejects the marriage, she needs witnesses for the rejection, as has passed before, but it was brief; therefore detail is written. The detail is that there are two forms of having witnesses. The first form: if at the time the girl reached puberty, witnesses are present, then she should say immediately to them: 'I have now reached puberty and I want to annul this marriage.' The second form: if at that time witnesses are not present, then in this case she should immediately reject verbally and then call witnesses or go to them. Whether witnesses are found quickly or after a while, in any case she should say before them: 'I have just reached puberty and I want to annul the marriage.' She should never reveal that she reached puberty some time ago. Even if the witnesses explicitly ask, 'When did you reach puberty?', she should not relate the story in detail, but only answer: 'I have just reached puberty' or just say that much. And it is permissible to lie to establish the truth, as is established in this chapter from the books of fiqh. And in the chapters it is mentioned, but there is a doubt in the heart: how can it be permissible? And the distinction: some of her statements before the judge... until she annulled as came earlier.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a practical explanation of the hila (legal stratagem) for a girl who was married as a minor and wants to exercise her khiyar al-bulugh. The key issue is that the annulment must be witnessed. The author outlines two scenarios: (1) if witnesses are present at the moment she reaches puberty, she should state her repudiation immediately; (2) if no witnesses are present, she must still utter the repudiation immediately (to avoid being seen as consenting by silence) and then later find witnesses to formally attest. She should not disclose that she reached puberty earlier, but should simply say 'I have just reached puberty'—even if that is not strictly true—because it is permitted to use such a statement as a stratagem to establish her right. The passage supports this with the principle 'يجوز الكذب لإحقاق الحق' (lying is permissible to establish a right), though it notes a lingering doubt. This is a classic hila in Hanafi fiqh: using a permissible fiction to avoid harm.

Key Terms
گواہ (gawah): Witnesses required to attest the girl's repudiation of the minor marriage
الكذب لإحقاق الحق (al-kadhib li-ihqaq al-haqq): The principle that a lie is permissible to establish a legitimate right when no other means are available
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract through repudiation
حيلة (hila (plural: hiyal)): Legal stratagem or permissible fiction to achieve a legitimate end

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wait to have witnesses before saying anything
B) Immediately say 'I reject the marriage' and then later find witnesses and say 'I have just reached puberty'
C) Only tell the judge without witnesses
D) Remain silent and the marriage is automatically annulled

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a legal fiction (saying 'just reached puberty') when exercising khiyar al-bulugh without witnesses, based on the maxim of permissible falsehood to secure a right.
