Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
The Legal Stratagem for Exercising Khiyar al-Bulugh with Witnesses
Explains legal stratagem for a girl to reject marriage upon puberty with witness testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the legal stratagem (hila) for a girl to annul her marriage upon reaching puberty, identifying the two witness scenarios and the applicable time limits.

Core Idea
A girl must reject her marriage immediately upon puberty; any delay or silence implies consent.

The option of puberty (khiyār al-bulūgh) gives a minor girl the right to annul her marriage upon reaching majority. However, this right is delicate: silence or delay can be interpreted as consent. To safeguard the annulment, the Hanafi school prescribes a legal stratagem (hīla) involving immediate verbal rejection and proper witness testimony. This passage from Thanwi's work details the procedure, emphasizing the critical role of timing and the wording of the declaration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Option and Its Trigger
Recognize that the khiyār al-bulūgh arises when a girl married as a minor reaches puberty. The moment of puberty is the critical juncture; she must act then.
Puberty is determined by menstruation or age (typically 15 lunar years).
2
Determine Witness Presence at the Moment of Puberty
Assess whether trustworthy witnesses are physically present when she becomes aware of puberty. This determines the immediate action she must take.
If witnesses are present, she declares directly to them. If not, she must reject verbally immediately and then find witnesses.
3
Execute the Immediate Verbal Rejection
She must utter a clear statement of annulment (e.g., 'I have just reached puberty and I annul this marriage') without any delay. If witnesses were absent, she must still speak the rejection now.
She should not reveal that any time has passed since puberty; she must say 'just now' even if it involves a permissible approximation.
4
Secure Witness Testimony
If witnesses were not initially present, she must summon them or go to them and repeat the same declaration in their presence. They will then testify that she rejected upon puberty.
The witnesses should not have heard a detailed account; summary testimony is sufficient and required for validity.
5
File a Petition with the Judge Within the Time Limit
After the witnesses have testified, she has one month to submit her petition to the court. If she delays beyond that, the option is lost. If witnesses are not yet secured, she must act immediately with no fixed grace period.
The one-month limit after testimony is analogous to the right of pre-emption (shuf'a). In the absence of testimony, delay of 'a few days' may forfeit the option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لے واضح رہے کہ ان تین صورتوں میں سے بیعنی جب گواہان کی گواہی ہو چکی ہو تو اس کو ایک مہینے تک درخواست پیش کرنے کی مہلت ہے اگر ایک مہینہ گزر گیا تو خیار فسخ ختم ہو گیا کیونکہ یہ اختیار اختیار حق شفعہ جیسا ہے ہے اگر گزر ہوگیا اور حق شفعہ میں ایک مہینہ تک خاموش رہنے سے اختیار سا فظ ہو جاتا ہے رشاہی اور دوسری صورت میں حتی الوسع جلدی کرنا لازم ہے لیکن اس جلدی کرنے کی کتب فقہ میں خاص مد نہیں ہو سکی البتہ خلاصہ الھادی سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر چند روز تک مقدمہ پیش نہ ہوا تو خیار ساقط ہو جائے گا وہ روایت یہ ہے قال هشام سالت محمد عن صغيرة زوجها عمها فحاضت فبعث خارها ليدعمها شهود آفلم يقدر وال في موضع ينقطع عن الناس فكشت ايا ما قال الزجها النكاح خلاصه في خيار البلوغ و ۲۲۔ اور تیری صورت کا حکم بھی قواعد سے وہ ہی معلوم ہوتا ہے جو کہ دوسری صورت کا ہے لان الاعمال في الصورة الأولى كان لتقرر العق بالاشهاد و التقرر باله شها و مفقود في الثالثة وفى الثانيه والله اعلم بالصواب . ضروری گذارش: چونکہ اس حاشیہ کا یہ سب مضمون قواعد سے لکھا گیا ہے اس لیے عمل کے وقت کسی منتقد فيه عالم محقق سے بھی دریافت کر لینا ضروری ہے ۔
Regarding before consummation; but if he consummates before her puberty, then it is said that his not returning the dower after her puberty is consent because it is necessary... and similar is said regarding her accepting the dower after consummation or valid seclusion. This is stated in Durar, volume 2. For a girl to reject the marriage, witnesses are necessary. When the girl rejects the marriage after reaching puberty, she also requires witnesses for the rejection, as has passed earlier, but that was brief; therefore, details are written. The details are that there are two forms of making witnesses. First form: At the time the girl reaches puberty, if witnesses are present with her, then she should immediately say to them, 'I have just reached puberty and I want to annul this marriage.' If witnesses are not immediately available for the adult girl to reject the marriage, second form: At that time witnesses are not present; in that case, she should immediately verbally reject and summon witnesses, or go to them herself, and the witnesses quickly meet or meet from the village; in any case, she should say in front of them, 'I have just reached puberty and I want to annul the marriage.' She should never express that she reached puberty some time ago. Even if the witnesses clearly ask, 'When did you reach puberty?' she should not relate the detailed story, but rather answer, 'I have just reached puberty,' or only say this much: 'It is permissible to lie for achieving the truth, as is clear in this chapter from the fiqh books and in other chapters; but it disturbs the heart to permit distinguishing some of her words before the judge: 'I annulled it as soon as' she said, 'I have annulled the marriage upon reaching puberty.' Because if she reveals the detailed story to the witnesses, then it will not be permissible for them to testify in ambiguous words, and if they give detailed testimony, that testimony will not be in her favor; but hearing the incident in summary words and testifying is permissible for them; they neither need to nor have the right to know the details. Then, approaching the judge has three scenarios. If the adult girl performs the rejection in front of witnesses, if according to the prescribed procedure the witnesses [testimony] has been given, then in that case... It is clear that among these three scenarios, meaning when the testimony of the witnesses has been given, she has a grace period of one month to submit her petition. If one month passes, the option of annulment is lost, because this option is like the right of pre-emption (shuf'a); if the month passes and in shuf'a, keeping silent for a month forfeits the option. In the second scenario, it is obligatory to hurry as much as possible, but for this hurrying, no specific period is found in fiqh books; however, from Khulasat al-Hadi it appears that if the case is not brought for a few days, the option is forfeited. That narration is: Hisham said: I asked Muhammad about a minor girl whose paternal uncle married her, then she menstruated, and her guardian sent someone to find witnesses for her, but he could not find a place isolated from people, and she remained for days. He said: The marriage is annulled. Summary in Khiyar al-Bulugh. And the ruling of the third scenario is also, from the principles, the same as the second scenario, because the practice in the first scenario was to establish the contract through witnesses, and establishment through witnesses is absent in the third and second. And Allah knows best what is correct. Necessary request: Since all this content of this commentary is written from principles, therefore, at the time of practice, it is necessary to also inquire from a critic who is a realized scholar.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a legal stratagem (hīla) for a girl who has been married off as a minor to exercise her option of puberty (khiyār al-bulūgh) to annul the marriage upon reaching majority. The author explains two scenarios for establishing witness testimony. First, if witnesses are present at the moment she reaches puberty, she should immediately declare in front of them that she has just attained puberty and wishes to annul the marriage. Second, if no witnesses are present, she must verbally reject the marriage immediately and then find witnesses as soon as possible; when they arrive, she should make the same declaration without revealing that any time has passed. She should not answer detailed questions about the exact time of puberty; instead, she should only say 'I have just reached puberty' or 'I annulled it upon reaching puberty.' This is because if the witnesses hear a detailed account, they cannot testify in summary form, and detailed testimony may not be favorable. Summary testimony is sufficient and permissible. After securing witnesses, there are three scenarios when going to the judge. If the witnesses have already testified, she has one month to file a petition, analogous to the option of pre-emption (shuf'a) where silence for a month forfeits the right. In the second scenario, where witnesses are yet to be produced, she must act immediately; there is no fixed period, but if she delays for a few days, the option may be lost, as per a narration from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybānī. The third scenario is similar to the second. The author notes that since this stratagem is derived from general principles (qawā‘id), one should consult a qualified verifier before acting upon it to ensure its validity.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyār al-bulūgh): The option a minor girl has upon reaching puberty to annul her marriage contracted by her guardian.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract by the exercise of the option of puberty.
شہود (shuhūd): Witnesses who attest to the girl's rejection of the marriage upon her declaration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a girl reaches puberty but no witnesses are present, what should she do first?
A) Wait for witnesses to come to her before saying anything.
B) Immediately verbally reject the marriage, then find witnesses.
C) Go to the judge without any witnesses.
D) Consult her guardian before taking any action.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-bulugh requires immediate rejection; any delay or silence implies consent.

Hila for Khiyar al-Bulugh: Three Scenarios for Annulment Procedure
Hila for khiyar al-bulugh: three scenarios for annulment procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios for exercising khiyar al-bulugh and apply the appropriate procedure (witnesses, oath, or no proof) based on the woman's situation.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-bulugh can be proven by witnesses, oath, or immediate claim – the procedure depends on available proof.

This passage from Al-Hilat al-Najijah presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a woman who, upon attaining puberty, wishes to annul a marriage contract made during her minority. Ashraf Ali Thanwi outlines three scenarios based on the availability of witnesses and the timing of her claim. Understanding these scenarios is crucial for any mufti advising a woman seeking annulment under Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three distinct situations described: (1) reliable witnesses available, (2) no reliable witnesses or witnesses disqualified, (3) woman claims immediate puberty and rejection.
Look for key phrases like 'if she has witnesses', 'if she cannot find witnesses', and 'third form'.
2
Determine the proof requirement for each
For each scenario, note what constitutes valid proof: in scenario 1, witness testimony; in scenario 2, woman's oath when she cannot produce witnesses; in scenario 3, no proof needed beyond her statement.
Pay attention to the Shami quote summarizing the different statements and their proof requirements.
3
Note the time limits
Identify the time constraints: scenario 1 has a one-month deadline from testimony; scenario 2 requires immediate action (within a few days according to Khulasat al-Hadi); scenario 3 has no time limit as she claims immediate puberty.
The one-month limit is based on analogy with shuf'a (pre-emption).
4
Understand the rationale behind the third scenario
Analyze why the third scenario requires no evidence: the woman's claim of immediate puberty is plausible and cannot be easily disproven; the default presumption is that she would reject the marriage if she disapproves.
The passage notes that 'action in the first form was to confirm the contract by having witnesses, which is absent in the third.'
5
Apply to a hypothetical case
Given a case described by the teacher, select the correct scenario and outline the procedure the mufti should follow.
This step tests your ability to operationalize the ruling.

Did I annul the marriage immediately upon attaining puberty? Because if she reveals the detailed incident to the witnesses, then it will not be permissible for them to give testimony in vague words, and if they give detailed testimony, this testimony will not be in her favor. It is permissible to give testimony after hearing the incident in summary; they neither need to know the details nor have the right to do so. Then there are three forms of presenting the application to the judge.
If the woman recited the marriage contract before witnesses? If due to prescribed shar'i procedure, witnesses are present, then in that case...
Let it be clear that among these three forms, meaning when the testimony of witnesses has been given, she has a respite of one month to present the application. If one month passes, then the option of annulment is terminated, because this option is like the right of pre-emption (shuf'a); if [the month] passes, then in the right of pre-emption, remaining silent for one month extinguishes the option. In the second form, it is obligatory to hasten as much as possible, but no specific period has been found in the books of fiqh for this hastening. However, from Khulasat al-Hadi it appears that if the case is not presented for a few days, the option will lapse. That narration is: Hisham said: I asked Muhammad about a minor girl whose paternal uncle married her; then she menstruated, and her [guardian?] sent someone to bring witnesses, but he could not find a place separated from people, so he hid her? He said: the marriage is annulled? Khulasah fi Khiyar al-Bulugh. And the ruling of the third form is also known from the principles to be the same as that of the second form, because the action in the first form was to confirm the contract by having witnesses, and confirmation by witnesses is absent in the third form, and in the second? And Allah knows best what is correct.
Necessary request: Since all this content of this footnote has been written from principles, therefore at the time of action, it is necessary to also inquire from a scrutinizing verified scholar.
The woman should submit an application to the judge or his deputy (i.e., shari'i representative) etc. in this manner: 'On such and such day, after attaining puberty, I disapproved of the marriage, and such and such persons are witnesses to the disapproval. Therefore, my marriage should be annulled.' Upon this application of the woman, after testimony, separation will occur.
If she cannot find reliable witnesses, or she revealed such details to the witnesses that it is no longer permissible for them to give testimony, then the situation is that the woman should submit an application as soon as possible, and in the application she should not disclose when she attained puberty, but only say: 'I annulled the marriage immediately upon attaining puberty.' Therefore, the judge should order annulment. If the judge also inquires when she attained puberty, she should still not tell. If she does tell, then separation cannot occur. Upon such an application, only after taking an oath, the marriage will be annulled.
Third form of application: She clearly states: 'I have just attained puberty and I do not approve of this marriage; therefore, I want it annulled.' In this case, neither witnesses nor oath are needed. Rather, without testimony and oath, the judge accepts this application and annuls the marriage.
Al-Allamah al-Shami said after quoting the statement of al-Bazzaziyyah and others: I say, and from the collection of that, it is derived that if she says, 'I attained puberty now and annulled,' she is believed without [proof] and without oath. If she says, 'I annulled when I attained puberty,' she is believed with proof or oath. If she says, 'I attained puberty yesterday and annulled,' then evidence is necessary. (al-Hirmah, vol. 2)
If she has actually immediately upon attaining puberty verbally said that I annulled this marriage...
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilat al-Najijah presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a woman who has been married as a minor and upon attaining puberty wishes to exercise her khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) to annul the marriage. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, describes three scenarios for presenting the case to the judge, based on the availability and reliability of witnesses.

The first scenario: The woman has reliable witnesses who can testify that she annulled the marriage immediately after puberty. In this case, she must present her application within one month of the testimony; otherwise, the option lapses by analogy with the right of pre-emption (shuf'a). The witnesses need not know the exact details; they may testify based on a summary.

Second scenario: The woman cannot find reliable witnesses, or she inadvertently revealed such details to potential witnesses that they can no longer testify (e.g., they heard specifics that disqualify them). In this case, she must apply as soon as possible, without specifying the time of puberty. She should only state that she annulled immediately upon puberty. If the judge asks when she attained puberty, she must not answer. The judge then takes an oath from her and annuls the marriage.

Third scenario: The woman states that she has just now attained puberty and immediately rejects the marriage. Here, no witnesses or oath are needed; the judge accepts her statement and annuls the marriage immediately. This is supported by the quotation from Allamah al-Shami, summarizing the positions of al-Bazzaziyyah and others: if she says 'I attained puberty now and annulled,' she is believed without proof or oath; if she says 'I annulled when I attained puberty,' she needs proof or an oath; if she says 'I attained puberty yesterday and annulled,' she must bring evidence.

The passage ends with a cautionary note that since this commentary is based on general principles, one should consult a verified scholar before acting on it.

Key legal points: The khiyar al-bulugh must be exercised immediately upon knowledge of puberty. The method of proof varies: if there are witnesses, they must testify; if not, the woman's own statement supported by an oath suffices; if she claims immediate puberty, no proof at all is required. The one-month limit in the first scenario is based on qiyas (analogy) with shuf'a (pre-emption).

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option for a minor married to annul the marriage upon attaining puberty.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or dissolution of the marriage contract.
شہادت (shahadat): Testimony given by witnesses in court.
حلف (half): Oath taken by the claimant when no witnesses are available.
شفعہ (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption in property sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No time limit; she can apply anytime

Key Takeaway
The hila for khiyar al-bulugh provides three procedures depending on evidence: witnesses (one-month deadline), no witnesses (immediate action + oath), or immediate claim of puberty (no proof needed).

Hila for Khiyar al-Bulugh Without Witnesses
Legal stratagem for annulment without witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the legal stratagem (hila) for a woman seeking annulment of marriage upon puberty when witnesses are unavailable, and apply the Hanafi conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
When witnesses are unavailable, a woman's oath suffices to annul a marriage at puberty — the hila bypasses the requirement of testimony.

In Hanafi family law, a minor given in marriage has the khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) to annul the marriage upon reaching majority. Normally, this requires witnesses to prove that the annulment was declared immediately. But what if no reliable witnesses can be found? This lesson unpacks the legal stratagem (hila) provided by the Hanafi school to allow the woman to still obtain an annulment by her own oath, carefully avoiding the pitfalls that would require testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard requirement
Recognize that the normal rule requires witnesses to prove the woman rejected the marriage at the moment of puberty. Without them, the annulment cannot proceed.
2
Define the obstacle
The obstacle is the absence of credible witnesses or their disqualification due to revealing details that prevent their testimony.
3
Outline the stratagem's key elements
The woman files a request to the qadi stating she rejected the marriage immediately upon puberty, but avoids specifying the exact date. She must not reveal when she reached puberty even if the qadi asks.
Revealing the date would require witnesses to confirm it, defeating the purpose.
4
Apply the qadi's response
The qadi takes an oath from the woman and annuls the marriage based on her oath alone, without witnesses.
The oath substitutes for testimony in this hila.
5
Identify the conditions for validity
The hila requires: (1) the woman must file as soon as possible, (2) she must not specify the date of puberty, (3) she must swear an oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت قاضی، یا اس کے قائم مقام [شرعی قاضی] وغیرہ میں اس طریقہ سے درخواست پیش کرے کہ میں فلاں دن بالغ ہونے پر نکاح کو نامنظور کر چکی ہوں اور نامنظوری کے فلاں فلاں حضرات گواہ ہیں اس وجہ سے میرا نکاح فسخ کر دیا جائے۔ عورت کی اس درخواست پر [اس عرضی دعوی پر] شہادت کے بعد تفریق ہو جائے گی۔ اگر معتبر گواہ نہ مل سکیں یا گواہوں سے اس [قسم کی تفصیل] ظاہر کردی جس سے ان کو گواہی دینا جائز نہ رہا تو پھر یہ صورت ہے کہ عورت جہاں تک ہو سکے جلد از جلد درخواست دے اور درخواست میں یہ ظاہر نہ کرے کہ کب بالغ ہوتی ہے بلکہ صرف اتنا کہے کہ میں نے بالغ ہوتے ہی نکاح فسخ کر دیا ہے۔ لہذا قاضی [؟] حکم دے دیا جاوے۔ اگر قاضی دریافت بھی کرے کہ کب بالغ ہوئی ہے تب بھی نہ بتلا دے کیونکہ اگر بتلا دیا تو پھر تفریق نہ ہو سکے گی۔ اور ایسی درخواست پر صرف حلف لے کر نکاح فسخ کرا دیا جاوے گا۔
The woman should submit a request to the qadi or his deputy in this manner: 'On such-and-such day, upon reaching puberty, I rejected the marriage, and such-and-such persons are witnesses to the rejection. Therefore my marriage should be annulled.' After this petition [claim], upon testimony, separation will occur. If reliable witnesses cannot be found or the witnesses have revealed details that prevent them from testifying, then this is the case: the woman should file the request as soon as possible without stating when she reached puberty, but only say that she rejected the marriage immediately upon puberty. Hence the qadi should give the order. Even if the qadi asks when she reached puberty, she should not tell him, because if she tells, the separation will not take place. Upon such a request, the qadi will take an oath and annul the marriage.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a woman who has the khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) but cannot produce witnesses to prove she rejected the marriage at the time of attaining puberty. The standard procedure requires witnesses to confirm her rejection. However, if witnesses are unavailable or disqualified, the woman may still obtain an annulment by filing a request without specifying the exact date of puberty, claiming she rejected it immediately. She must avoid answering the qadi's inquiry about the date, as revealing the exact time would require witnesses. The qadi will accept her request on oath, and the marriage is annulled. This is based on Hanafi fiqh, allowing a hila to avoid the rigid requirement of testimony when it is impossible.

Key Terms
خیار فتح (khiyar al-faskh): The option of annulment; here specifically the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) given to a minor upon reaching majority.
حلف (half): Oath taken by the woman to confirm her claim of immediate rejection, used in lieu of witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key condition for the hila to be valid when witnesses are unavailable?
A) The woman must bring at least one witness.
B) The woman must not specify when she reached puberty.
C) The woman must wait one year before filing.
D) The woman must have a male guardian file the request.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses for khiyar al-bulugh are missing, a woman can annul her marriage by filing a timely request without stating the date of puberty, and the qadi will accept her oath as sufficient proof.

Hila for Immediate Annulment at Puberty: Conditions and Juristic Effect
Provides a hila for immediate annulment upon puberty with conditions and juristic effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hila for khiyar al-bulugh by distinguishing permissible immediate rejection from sinful deception, and evaluate the effect of a qadi's ruling when the option has lapsed.

Core Idea
A woman’s immediate annulment claim is believed without proof; if delayed, only a trick—but the qadi’s ruling still binds.

This passage from Al-Hilatun Najijah presents a third scenario for annulment upon puberty. It explains when a woman’s word is enough, when she needs evidence, and crucially, the boundary between a permissible hila and a sinful deception. The fatwa also highlights the Hanafi position that a qadi's ruling is effective even if based on a false claim—a critical point for muftis issuing guidance on remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three verbal formulations
Read the passage carefully to find the three different statements a woman might make regarding her annulment. For each, note what evidence (bina, yamin) the qadi requires.
The key words: 'بلغت الآن وفسخت' vs 'فسخت حين بلغت' vs 'بلغت أمس وفسخت'.
2
Determine when the hila is permissible vs sinful
Separate the scenario where the woman actually spoke immediately (halal to conceal) from the scenario where she delayed (haram to claim falsely). Mark the condition: immediate verbal utterance at the moment of puberty.
The text explicitly says: 'اگر حقیقہ بالغ ہوتے ہی فورا زبان سے کہہ دیا ہے' – if in reality she said it immediately, it is permissible to use the hila of saying 'بلغت الآن'.
3
Analyze the effect of the qadi's ruling under Abu Hanifa
Even if the woman lies and says 'بلغت الآن' after the option has expired, the qadi's annulment ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly. Understand the principle: the qadi's ruling cuts off dispute (al-qada' yuhrim al-khilaf).
The passage states: 'Because his ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly in contracts and annulments'. This is the Hanafi position, as opposed to some other schools.
4
Apply the madhhab dispute to practical fatwa scenarios
Consider a modern case: a woman married as a minor reaches puberty, delays a week, then falsely claims immediate annulment. The qadi annuls. Later she marries someone else. Is the second marriage valid? According to Abu Hanifa: yes. According to the opposing view: no.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether she must repeat the annulment. The Hanafi position is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالغہ ہوتے ہی نکاح کرنا [فسخ کرنا] سوم: ایک صورت درخواست کی یہ ہے کہ صاف کرے کہ میں ابھی بالغ ہوئی ہوں اور یہ نکاح مجھے منظور نہیں اس واسطے فسخ کرانا چاہتی ہوں۔ اس صورت میں نہ کسی گواہ کی حاجت ہے نہ حلف کی۔ بلکہ بدون شہادت اور حلف ہی قاضی اس درخواست کو قبول کرے اور نکاح کو فسخ کردے۔

Annulment immediately upon puberty: third case: one form of request is that she clearly says: 'I have just reached puberty and this marriage is not acceptable to me, so I want to annul it.' In this case, there is no need for witnesses nor an oath. Rather, without testimony and oath, the qadi accepts this request and annuls the marriage. Al-Allama al-Shami said after quoting the expression of al-Bazzaziyya and others: I say, from all that it is concluded that if she says 'I reached puberty now and annulled', she is believed without evidence or oath; if she says 'I annulled when I reached puberty', she is believed with evidence or oath; if she says 'I reached puberty yesterday and annulled', then evidence is necessary. (al-Khaniyya, vol. 2) If in reality she immediately said with her tongue upon reaching puberty 'I annul this marriage', then it is permissible for her to conceal the actual incident from witnesses or the qadi and say 'I have just reached puberty'. But if she delayed even a little in saying that after puberty, then the option of annulment is void, and it is absolutely not permissible for her to use a stratagem for the acceptance of testimony and request. If she does use a stratagem, she will be severely sinful. But if she uses a hila after the option has fallen, and the qadi rules for annulment, the marriage is annulled according to Imam Abu Hanifa because his ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly in contracts and annulments.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage outlines a second hila for khiyar al-bulugh. When a woman clearly states upon attaining puberty that she rejects the marriage, the qadi can annul it without any witnesses or oath, as she is believed on her word. Imam al-Shami summarizes that the ruling depends on phrasing: 'I reached puberty now and annulled' requires no evidence; 'I annulled when I reached puberty' requires evidence or oath; 'I reached puberty yesterday and annulled' requires evidence. However, the hila is only valid if the woman actually exercised the option immediately. If she delayed, the option is lost, and she cannot use a subterfuge to claim immediate rejection. Still, if the qadi unknowingly annuls the marriage based on her false claim, the annulment is effective according to Abu Hanifa, as his ruling operates both outwardly and inwardly. The passage highlights the strictness against lying but also the legal effect of a qadi's ruling.

Key Terms
خیار فسخ (khiyar al-faskh): Option of annulment; here specifically the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) for a woman who was married as a minor.
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem or indirect means to achieve a permissible result without violating the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a woman says 'I reached puberty now and annulled the marriage', what does the qadi require?
A) Two witnesses
B) An oath
C) Neither witnesses nor an oath
D) Either witnesses or an oath

Key Takeaway
Immediate verbal annulment at puberty is believed without proof; if delayed, the option is lost and using a hila is sinful, but the qadi's ruling still annuls the marriage according to Abu Hanifa.

Marriage Without Guardian: First Scenario Invalid
Introduces the first scenario of marriage without guardian to a non-kufw as completely invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first scenario of non-kufw marriage without guardian's permission and state the Hanafi fatwa that it is completely invalid (batil).

Core Idea
A mature woman's marriage to a non-kufw without her wali mujabbir's permission is completely invalid (batil), not merely voidable.

In the Hanafi school, the requirement of kafa'ah (equality) in marriage is taken seriously. When a woman marries a man who is not her equal (ghayr kufw) without the consent of her authoritative guardian (wali mujabbir), the ruling varies depending on circumstances. This passage introduces the first scenario: such a marriage is completely invalid. Let's examine the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a mature woman marrying a man who is not her kufw without the permission of her wali mujabbir. The ruling given is that the marriage is batil (completely invalid).
The text explicitly states 'fatwa is that the marriage does not occur; it is batil.'
2
Understand the basis
In Hanafi fiqh, the wali mujabbir's consent is a condition (shart) for the validity of marriage when the man is not a kufw. Without it, the marriage contract is defective ab initio.
The condition is specific to ghayr kufw; for a kufw marriage, a mature woman may marry without guardian.
3
Note the consequence
Because the marriage is batil, it has no legal effects. No faskh (annulment) is needed; the marriage is considered as if it never happened. However, if consummation occurred, some scholars may require iddah under shubha.
This is different from the third scenario where the marriage is valid but not binding, requiring faskh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ بالغ عورت بغیر اجازت ولی مجبّرہ [؟] بلا اجازت ولی نکاح غیر کفو میں نکاح کرے اس صورت میں فتویٰ اس پر ہے کہ نکاح میں نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بالکل باطل ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر نکاح کے بعد ولی مجبّر [؟]

In some, the marriage is completely invalid; in some, it is [valid and] binding, so the option of annulment does not remain; in some, it is valid but not binding, and the option remains. The main objective here is to explain only those forms in which there is an option of annulment, because the need for a qadi's ruling arises only in that case. But for public benefit, we list all forms and write the ruling for each separately. Their detail is as follows: First form: A mature woman marries without the permission of her guardian mujabbir [authoritative guardian] to a non-kufw. The fatwa in this case is that the marriage does not occur; rather, it is completely invalid, to the extent that if after the marriage the guardian mujabbir...

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on khiyar al-bulugh in cases of marriage without a guardian to a non-kufw (of unequal status). The author categorizes such marriages into three types: (1) completely invalid (batil), (2) valid and binding (lazim), (3) valid but not binding (ghayr lazim). The main focus is on the last type where the woman retains the option of annulment. However, for public benefit, all types are listed. The first scenario described here: a mature woman marries without the permission of her wali mujabbir (e.g., father or grandfather) to a non-kufw. According to the fatwa, such a marriage is completely invalid (batil); it does not even take effect. The text cuts off, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
ولی مجبّر (wali mujabbir): An authoritative guardian (typically father or grandfather) who has the right to compel the minor's marriage; here refers to the guardian whose permission is required for a mature woman's marriage to a non-kufw.
غیر کفو (ghayr kufw): A man who is not equal in status to the woman, e.g., in lineage, profession, or piety.
باطل (batil): Void ab initio; a contract that has no legal effect as if it never occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In Hanafi fiqh, a marriage to a non-kufw without the wali mujabbir's consent is not merely voidable but completely void (batil).

Legal Stratagem for Khiyar al-Bulugh After Loss
Explains a legal stratagem for claiming khiyar al-bulugh after it is lost, with a note on the judge's ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman may use a hila to claim khiyar al-bulugh after it is lost, and explain why the judge's annulment is binding both externally and internally according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A lost option of puberty can be reclaimed via a truthful claim of recent puberty, and the judge's ruling annuls the marriage both externally and internally.

In the Hanafi school, khiyar al-bulugh gives a minor married by a non-father guardian the right to annul upon puberty. But if she delays exercise, the option lapses. This lesson unpacks a hila (legal stratagem) that allows her to still annul by claiming she has just attained puberty, and examines the binding effect of the judge's ruling. The passage also warns against misuse and advises verification with a qualified scholar.

Guided Path
1
Understand khiyar al-bulugh and its loss
Recall that khiyar al-bulugh allows a minor married by a non-father guardian to annul upon puberty. If she delays claiming it even slightly after puberty, the option is lost and she cannot annul normally.
This is the established Hanafi ruling: loss is immediate after the first opportunity to claim.
2
Identify the hila: claim of recent puberty
The text presents a stratagem: she hides the fact that she previously attained puberty and claims before witnesses or a judge that she has just become baligha. This claim is true in substance (she is indeed baligha) but not about the timing.
The hila relies on a truthful core—she is really baligha—but omits the delay.
3
Analyze the conditions of the hila
The hila is only permissible if certain conditions are met: the claim must be true in substance (she has attained puberty), made before a judge or witnesses, and the judge must rule based on it. If any condition fails, the hila becomes sinful.
The passage warns that if she uses a false stratagem (e.g., lying about being baligha), she will be 'severely sinful'.
4
Evaluate the effect of the judge's ruling
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the judge rules to annul based on her claim, the annulment takes effect both externally (zahiran) and internally (batinan) in contracts and annulments. This differs from the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who hold it only external.
This internal effect means the marriage is fully dissolved in the sight of Allah, allowing remarriage without doubt.
5
Apply the ethical caution
The author notes that since this hila involves hiding the truth, it must be verified from a 'non-common person' (a qualified scholar) before acting. The mufti should assess each case individually to ensure no sin is committed.
This caution reflects the principle that hiyal must be used responsibly and not as a means to circumvent Shari'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کرتی ہوں تب تو اس کو جائز ہے کہ گواہوں سے یا قاضی سے اصل واقعہ چھپا کر یہ کہے سے
کہ میں ابھی بالغ ہوئی ہوں ۔
اور اگر بلوغ کے بعد اس کہنے میں ذرا بھی دیر کردی تھی تو خیار فتح باطل ہوگیا اب اس کو ہرگز جائز نہیں کہ شہادت اور درخواست کے قبول ہونے کا حیلہ کر سے اگر جلہ کرے گی تو سخت گنہگار ہوگی ۔
ولكن ان احتالت مع سقوط الخيار و حكم القاضي بالفخ الفساح النكاح عند الاماملان القضاء عند ه ينفذ ظاهرا وباطنا في العقود والفسوخ
ضروری گذارش : چونکہ اس حاشیہ کا یہ سب مضمون قواعد سے لکھا گیا ہے اس لیے عمل کے وقت کسی غیر عا م حق سے بھی دریافت کر لینا ضروری ہے ۔
[She says] that it is permissible for her to hide the real situation from the witnesses or the judge and say that she has just attained puberty. And if after puberty she delayed this saying even a little, then the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) is lost. Now it is absolutely not permissible for her to use any stratagem for the acceptance of testimony and request. If she does it, she will be severely sinful. But if she employs a stratagem after the option is lost and the judge rules to annul, he annuls the marriage according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Indeed, his ruling takes effect both externally and internally in contracts and annulments. Essential note: Since all the content of this marginal note is written from the principles, it is necessary to verify from a non-common person when acting upon it.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This is a hila (legal stratagem) passage dealing with khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty). The issue: a woman who married as a minor and attained puberty had the right to annul the marriage upon attaining puberty (khiyar al-bulugh). If she delayed claiming this right even slightly after puberty, the option is lost according to the Hanafi school. In that case she cannot annul the marriage legitimately. However, the author presents a stratagem: she may hide the fact that she previously attained puberty and claim before witnesses or the judge that she has just now become baligha. This claim, if accepted, would allow her to exercise the option. The Arabic quote clarifies that if she uses this stratagem after the option is lost, and the judge rules based on her claim to annul the marriage, the annulment is effective both externally and internally according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The nafs al-amr (internal reality) yields to the judge's ruling in matters of contracts and annulments. The note warns that although this is permissible as a stratagem, acting on it requires verification from a qualified scholar because it involves hiding the truth.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of puberty that allows a minor who was married by a non-father guardian to annul the marriage upon attaining puberty.
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding prohibited consequences, often by using a neutral or constructive claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The hila of claiming recent puberty is a valid Hanafi device to activate khiyar al-bulugh even after it is lost, but it requires a truthful claim and a judge's ruling, which is binding both externally and internally.

Khiyar al-Faskh for Non-Kafa'ah: When the Father's Assumption Alone is Insufficient
Discussing khiyar al-faskh when father mistakenly assumed kafa'ah in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a father has the right to annul his daughter's marriage based on non-kafa'ah, applying the Hanafi principle that absolute texts are restricted by qualified conditions.

Core Idea
Merely assuming kafa'ah does not grant annulment; the husband must have claimed compatibility.

In Hanafi marriage law, the right to annul (khiyar al-faskh) for lack of compatibility (kafa'ah) is a critical protection for the family. However, not every discovery of incompatibility triggers this right. This lesson explores a nuanced ikhtilaf: what if the father married his daughter based on his own assumption of the husband's compatibility, without any statement from the husband? Through an analysis of classical sources, Asraf Ali Thanwi refines the application of this khayar, emphasizing the distinction between absolute and restricted rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Distinguish between when the husband himself stated he is kufu (compatible) and when the father/grandfather merely assumed compatibility based on appearances. The ruling differs based on this distinction.
2
Locate the Ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi jurists hold that khiyar al-faskh is available absolutely whenever non-kafa'ah appears, while others restrict it to cases where the husband's statement induced the assumption. Understand the evidence each side uses.
3
Apply the Usul Principle: Al-Mutlaq Yuhmalu 'ala al-Muqayyad
Thanwi resolves the ikhtilaf by carrying the absolute texts (granting khiyar broadly) onto the restricted texts (requiring husband's statement). This is a core Hanafi usul method for harmonizing evidence.
This principle is key to understanding how later Hanafi jurists like Thanwi prefer rulings.
4
Examine the Parental Right Continues
Even after discovery, the father's silence does not forfeit the right; he retains the option, and the child upon puberty also acquires a separate right. The marriage becomes binding only with mutual consent after puberty.
This relates to khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) which interacts with khiyar al-faskh.
5
Synthesize the Fatwa Outcome
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) per Thanwi's preference: the right to annul for non-kafa'ah is not established unless the assumption was based on the husband's statement. Scholars at need may consult sources and decide.
This is a tarjih (preference) and not absolute; other views are acknowledged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Because of his statement it was understood, or the condition of being kufu was made, but later it became known that he is non-kufu. In this case, the detail is that before puberty only the father and grandfather have the option; if he annulled, it would become clear. And if after the truth became known he still consented to the marriage, it becomes binding. The remainder of the Hashiya of the previous page: neither the husband stated such kafa'ah, but rather the father and grandfather merely from their own assumption considered him kufu and married, then it became apparent that he is not. In this case, regarding whether the option of [annulment] is established or not, despite searching, nothing clear could be found. Some juristic cases indicate that in the case of marrying based on the assumption of kafa'ah and then the contrary appearing, the option of [annulment] is absolutely available, whether this assumption of kafa'ah arose from the husband's statement or the girl's family made this assumption themselves. And in some other cases, this option is restricted to the condition that the assumption of kafa'ah was made based on the husband's statement. Therefore, there is disagreement among scholars whether these two issues are separate and in both cases the option of [annulment] is available, or whether they are carried on the absolute unrestricted [ruling] and without the husband's statement, merely his apparent kafa'ah is not sufficient for the option of [annulment]. And from the principles, it seems to me that the absolute should be carried on the restricted, and the option of annulment should not be granted in the case of apparent kafa'ah without the husband's informing. These juristic cases [are from] Radd al-Mukhtar, Bab al-Awla, from his saying '...', and Bab al-Kafa'ah, from his saying '...', and Bab al-Ayn, from his saying '...', and Bahr al-Raiq, Bab al-Kafa'ah, and Khaniyyah, end of Bab al-Kafa'ah. Scholars at time of need should refer and give preference to one side themselves and act, not rely on our preference. And if the father and grandfather remained silent, then merely their silence does not void the option; rather, the father and grandfather retain the option, and upon puberty the boy and girl also acquire the option. Therefore, after puberty, for the marriage to be binding, the consent of both is a condition: both the father/grandfather and the boy/girl. After puberty, if any one of the boy/girl and father/grandfather wishes, the marriage can be annulled, even if the other consents to the continuation of the marriage. Because it is stated in Fatawa Qadikhan: 'A man married his minor daughter to a man who mentioned that he does not drink intoxicants, but he found him a drunkard. Then the daughter reached puberty and said: I am not pleased.' Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: If the girl's father does not drink intoxicants and most of the people of his town are righteous, then the marriage is invalid because the father would not be pleased with non-kafa'ah, and he only married her based on the assumption that he was kufu. This explicitly states that in the mentioned case, after puberty the girl has the option, and the boy in the matter of kafa'ah holds the same ruling as the girl, as mentioned in the chapter on khiyar al-bulugh. In this case, the binding effect by the father's consent is because he has the right to marry her to a non-kufu, as detailed in the chapter on khiyar al-bulugh. And from this mentioned case and from the words 'because her father...' it seems understood. Also in Khazinat al-Muftiyin, there is explicit mention of the father having the option. He said: When the father marries his minor daughter to a man assuming he is able to provide housing and maintenance, then his inability appears, the father has the right to annul because the condition of kafa'ah is not fulfilled, and his right is not lost because he married based on his capability. (Khazinat al-Muftiyin, vol. 2) And when he gets the option after the situation becomes apparent, then [it is not voided] by any cancellation.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical issue in Hanafi marriage law: the right (khiyar al-faskh) to annul a marriage when the husband is discovered to be non-kufu (not of compatible status). The author, Asraf Ali Thanwi, presents a nuanced discussion from classical Hanafi sources. He first distinguishes two scenarios: (1) the husband himself stated he is kufu, and (2) the father/grandfather merely assumed compatibility based on appearances. In the first scenario, the right to annul is clearly established. In the second, there is disagreement among the jurists: some hold that the right exists absolutely, while others restrict it to cases where the husband's statement induced the assumption. Thanwi, after examining the texts, prefers the restricted view: the absolute (mutlaq) should be qualified by the restricted (muqayyad), so the option is not granted when the father assumed without the husband's statement. He cites numerous authorities like Radd al-Mukhtar, Bahr al-Raiq, and Khaniyyah to show the ikhtilaf. He then clarifies that the father's silence after discovering the truth does not forfeit his right; both he and the child upon puberty retain the option. The marriage becomes binding only with the consent of both after puberty. Thanwi also quotes Fatawa Qadikhan and Khazinat al-Muftiyin to support the father's right to annul when the husband turns out to be incapable or non-kufu. The passage thus refines the application of khiyar al-faskh, emphasizing the importance of the husband's statement and the father's right to protect his daughter's interests.

Key Terms
کفاءت (kafa'ah): Compatibility in marriage (lineage, religion, profession, wealth, etc.) required for a valid marriage in Hanafi law.
خیار الفسخ (khiyar al-faskh): The option to annul a marriage contract due to a defect or failure of condition, such as non-kafa'ah.
ظن کفاوت (zann al-kafa'ah): The assumption or belief that a person is kufu (compatible) in marriage.
المطلق يحمل على المقيد (al-mutlaq yuhmalu 'ala al-muqayyad): A principle of usul al-fiqh: when conflicting texts exist, the absolute ruling is interpreted as qualified by the restricted one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, according to the preferred view presented in this passage, when does a father have the right to annul his minor daughter's marriage after discovering the husband is non-kufu?
A) In all cases where non-kafa'ah becomes apparent, regardless of how the assumption of kafa'ah arose.
B) Only if the husband himself stated or indicated that he is kufu, leading the father to marry in reliance on that statement.
C) Only if the daughter reaches puberty and rejects the marriage.
D) Only if the father had explicitly made a condition of kafa'ah in the marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
The right to annul for lack of compatibility is not automatic; it depends on whether the belief in compatibility was induced by the husband's own statement, per the preferred Hanafi view.

Apostasy of a Wife: Hanafi Ruling and Stratagem for Renewal
Ruling on apostate wife, with dispute and stratagem for renewal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy to resolve a conflict between Zahir al-Riwaya and Nawadir, and construct a hila (legal stratagem) for renewing a marriage after a wife's apostasy.

Core Idea
An apostate wife is not enslaved; the marriage is renewed with minimal mahr under the principle that hardship brings ease.

The apostasy of a married woman raises questions about the marriage bond and her status. Hanafi fiqh has multiple narrations: the relied-upon Zahir al-Riwaya holds that she remains free and must renew the marriage, while a Nawadir narration would enslave her. Later scholars preferred the easier ruling, invoking the maxim 'hardship brings ease'. This passage also provides a practical stratagem for judges to renew the marriage with minimal mahr, closing the door to mischief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting narrations
Find the two narrations in the passage: one in Zahir al-Riwaya (she is not enslaved) and one in Nawadir from Abu Hanifa (she is enslaved). Note that both are attributed to the Hanafi school.
Zahir al-Riwaya is the well-known transmission from Imam Muhammad's six books.
2
Determine the tarjih (preference)
Identify the opinion of the scholars of Balkh (Mashayikh Balkh): they give fatwa on the apparent narration, not the Nawadir. Understand why: to avoid hardship and close the door to mischief.
The fatwa is 'first' (أولى) according to Al-Haskafi and others.
3
Extract the hila (legal stratagem)
Find the practical steps: the judge compels her to Islam, renews the marriage with the smallest amount (even a dinar), and administers ta'zir of 75 lashes. She cannot marry anyone else.
The hila ensures the marriage can continue with minimal formality.
4
Apply the qawida 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir'
This principle justifies the easy renewal. Understand that hardship (mashaqqa) in forcing a full new marriage or enslavement is avoided by this facility.
The maxim is explicitly cited in the passage.
5
Evaluate the fatwa hierarchy
Assess why the Zahir al-Riwaya is preferred over the Nawadir. Note that later Hanafi masters (like Ibn Abidin) confirm this tarjih based on public interest and ease.
Students often assume Nawadir is stronger because it comes from Abu Hanifa directly, but the established fatwa is otherwise.

With her first husband because the resolution is achieved thereby, and every judge may renew the marriage with the least thing, even if with a dinar, and she is beaten and punished with seventy-five lashes, and the apostate woman is not enslaved as long as she is in the abode of Islam according to the apparent narration, and in the narration of the Nawadir from Abu Hanifa she is enslaved. [...] And from the principles: hardship brings ease. [...]
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage compiles rulings on the apostasy of a married woman in Hanafi fiqh. According to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), the woman does not become enslaved as long as she is in Dar al-Islam; rather, she is compelled to re-embrace Islam and to renew her marriage contract with her husband. The judge may renew the marriage with the smallest amount (even one dinar) to close the door to mischief. There is a conflicting narration from Abu Hanifa in the Nawadir that she becomes enslaved, but the fatwa is given on the opinion of the scholars of Balkh, who prefer the apparent narration. The principle of hardship (mashaqqa) is invoked to justify the ease of renewal. The passage also notes that in later times, due to the Mongol invasions, some regions became Dar al-Harb in appearance, which affects the ruling on enslavement.

Key Terms
ردة (ridda): Apostasy from Islam by a married woman.
تجديد النكاح (tajdid al-nikah): Renewal of the marriage contract after apostasy.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known and relied-upon transmissions of Imam Muhammad.

C) She is compelled to re-embrace Islam and renew the marriage contract.
D) She remains married without any action required.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa on a wife's apostasy is that she is compelled to Islam and must renew her marriage with a minimal mahr, based on the principle of hardship bringing ease.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate

The Invalid Stratagem of Using Apostasy to Annul Marriage
Exposes the invalid stratagem of using apostasy to separate spouses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why the stratagem of apostasy to annul a marriage is invalid in the Hanafi school and apply the fatwa that the woman must return to her first husband.

Core Idea
Apostasy cannot be used to escape marriage—the woman is compelled to return to her first husband.

Stratagems (hiyal) are sometimes employed to circumvent legal rulings. This passage exposes one such attempt: advising a woman to apostatize in order to separate from her husband. The Hanafi school unequivocally rejects this, clarifying that apostasy nullifies the marriage but does not grant freedom; the woman is compelled to return to Islam and to her original husband, and the separation is not considered a valid divorce. Understanding this ruling is essential for muftis to prevent misuse of legal loopholes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Stratagem
Read the passage and note the specific stratagem: a woman is given a fatwa to apostatize from Islam in order to separate from her husband. This is presented as a hila (legal trick).
The passage labels this as an invalid stratagem.
2
Trace the Legal Dispute
The passage records disagreement among early scholars. Abu Bakr and some others held that apostasy does not affect the marriage, while the majority of scholars of Bukhara held that it does nullify the marriage but the woman is compelled to return to her husband.
The relied-upon fatwa is from the Bukhara scholars.
3
Identify the Mufta Bihi Position
Determine which position is operative for fatwa. The passage states 'upon it is the fatwa' referring to the Bukhara position: apostasy nullifies the marriage, but the woman is forced back to her first husband.
The separation is without divorce (firqah bila talaq).
4
Understand the Consequences
Note the consequences for the woman: she is compelled to return to Islam, punished with seventy-five lashes, and forbidden to marry anyone except her first husband.
This closes the door to using apostasy as a divorce mechanism.
5
Recognize the Usul Principle
The fatwa implicitly applies the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil) by preventing the stratagem from achieving its desired effect.
The Hanafi school uses this principle to invalidate hiyal that lead to prohibited outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح الفقه الأكبر لملا على القاري وفي المضمرات لو افتي لامرأة بالكفر لتبين من زوجها فقد كفر قبلها وتحير المرأة على الاسلام وتضرب خمسة وسبعين سوطا وليس لها ان تتزوج الا بزوجها الأول هكذا قال ابو بكر وكان ابوجعفر يفتي بأنه لا يؤخذ بهذا وقال بعضهم ان روتها لا تؤثر في افادة النكاح ولا يؤمر بتجديد النكاح حسما لهذا الباب عليهن وعامة علماء بخارى يقولون كفرها يعمل في افساد النكاح لكنها تجبر على النكاح مع زوجها قطعا بهذا فرقة بغير طلاق بالاجماع وعليها الفتوى كذا في منهاج المصلين.
And in the commentary of al-Fiqh al-Akbar by Mulla Ali al-Qari: And in al-Mudmarat: If a woman is given a fatwa to apostatize to separate from her husband, then she has disbelieved before that, and the woman is compelled to Islam and is beaten seventy-five lashes, and she may not marry anyone except her first husband. Thus said Abu Bakr. And Abu Ja'far gave fatwa that this is not taken? And some said: Her apostasy does not affect the marriage and she is not ordered to renew the marriage, to close this door upon them. And the majority of the scholars of Bukhara say: Her apostasy works to nullify the marriage, but she is compelled to marry her husband, definitely; this separation is without divorce by consensus, and upon it is the fatwa. Thus in Minhaj al-Musallin.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (stratagem) case: attempting to use apostasy as a means to dissolve a marriage. The text clarifies that this stratagem is invalid. If a woman is given a fatwa to apostatize in order to separate from her husband, she actually becomes an apostate (and is punished), but the marriage is not severed. The predominant Hanafi position (from the scholars of Bukhara) is that apostasy does nullify the marriage, but the woman is compelled to return to Islam and to her husband, and the separation is not considered a valid divorce. The fatwa is against the stratagem, emphasizing that one cannot use apostasy to escape marriage.

Key Terms
الرِّدَّة (ar-riddah): Apostasy from Islam; leaving the religion.
حيلة (hīlah): A stratagem or legal trick to achieve a result that would otherwise be inaccessible.
الفتوى (al-fatwā): A formal legal opinion issued by a qualified mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a woman who apostatizes to separate from her husband?
A) She is free to marry someone else.
B) She is beaten and must return to her first husband.
C) The marriage is automatically dissolved with a valid divorce.
D) She is executed for apostasy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi ruling is that a woman who apostatizes to dissolve her marriage does not succeed; she is compelled to return to Islam and to her first husband, and the separation is not a divorce.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

Blocking the Apostasy Stratagem: Three Hanafi Positions
Three Hanafi opinions on the marriage of an apostate wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi positions on the marriage status of an apostate wife and apply the mufta bihi (Zahir al-Riwayah) to block the use of apostasy as a legal stratagem for divorce.

Core Idea
To block apostasy as a divorce stratagem, the Hanafi school forces remarriage to the same husband.

This lesson examines a classic hila case: a wife apostatizes intending to free herself from marriage. The Hanafi school internally differs on the legal effect, but all opinions aim to prevent apostasy from becoming a loophole. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) dissolves the marriage but compels her to remarry her husband, closing the door to abuse. Understanding these positions equips a mufti to handle a mufti with a fatwa that upholds Shariah objectives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hila scenario
Recognize that the wife's apostasy is often a deliberate stratagem to dissolve an unwanted marriage. The ruling must block this means (sadd al-dhara'i).
The passage explicitly mentions the intent to escape the husband.
2
List the three Hanafi positions
From the text: 1) Dissolution with forced remarriage (Zahir al-Riwayah). 2) No dissolution – marriage continues. 3) Wife becomes a slave-girl (narration from Abu Hanifa).
These are within the school, not cross-madhhab.
3
Understand the legal effect of each
Analyze the practical outcome: under (1) she must remarry same husband; (2) she remains married; (3) husband acquires her as property through purchase (Dar al-Islam) or freely (Dar al-Harb).
All three prevent her from marrying another man.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states Zahir al-Riwayah is the relied-upon position (المعتمد). Recognize that later fatwa manuals (Durr al-Mukhtar, Shami) adopt this view.
Authority: fatwa hierarchy – Zahir al-Riwayah over nawadir.
5
Apply sadd al-dhara'i in fatwa
The mufti must understand that forcing remarriage is a legal measure to block the hila, not a punishment. The wife is compelled regardless of her true intention.
Sadd al-dhara'i is applied here to preserve marriage stability.

(شامي باب النكاح) اور دوسرا قول مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند اور بعض مشائخ بخارا اور ابو النصر الدبوہی اور ابو القاسم صفار کا فتویٰ ہے کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونے کی صورت میں نکاح فسخ ہی نہیں ہوتا، بلکہ بدستور یہ عورت شوہر سابق کے نکاح میں رہتی ہے جیسا کہ عبارت فتح القدیر من و عبارت قاضی خاں نی ر دعبارت در مختار و عبارت شامی نمبر و عبارت فقیه نیشکر اور شرح فقہ اکبر نمبر میں اس کی تصریح ہے۔ تیسرا قول وہ تو اور کی روایت ہے امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ سے کہ یہ عورت دارالاسلام میں بھی کنیز بنا کر رکھی جائے گی اور اس کے خاوند کا قبضہ اس پر بدستور سابق باقی رہے گا۔ لیکن اس روایت میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر یہ مرتدہ دارالاسلام میں ہو تو اس کا خاوند اس کو امام المسلمین سے قیمت دے کر خریدے گا یا اگر امام المسلمین اس کو مصرف سمجھیں گے تو اس کو مفت بھی دے دیں گے بہرحال بغیر اجازت امام اس کو اپنے قبضہ میں لانا جائز نہ ہوگا اور اگر دارالحرب میں ہے، تو ازن امام کی حاجت نہیں بلکہ جب خاوند اس پر قبضہ پائے تو اس کی ملک ہو جاے گی۔ اجارت امام وغیرہ کی کچھ حاجت نہیں جیسا کہ عمارت قیر نشے میں اس کی تصریح ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ عورت اگر مرتد ہو جائے تو اُس کے نکاح کے بارے میں حنفیہ کے تین قول ہوئے: ایک یہ کہ نکاح فسخ ہو جاتا ہے لیکن بعد تجدید اسلام اس کو تجدید نکاح پر مجبور کیا جائے گا کسی دوسری جگہ نکاح کرنے کا اختیار نہ دیا جائے گا (وهو ظاهر الرواية) تفصیل اس مسئلہ کی یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت مرتد ہو کر دارالحرب میں چلی جائے یا دار الحرب میں ہی مرتد ہو تو اُس کو کنیز بنانے پر ظاہر الروایہ بھی متفق ہے۔ تو اور اور ماہر الروایہ کا اختلاف مروان این که در اسلام میں رہتے ہوئے بھی کنیز بن سکتی ہے یا نہیں جیسا کہ فتح القدیر اور تنبیہ کی عبارت مذکورہ سے واضح ہے۔
It became clear that these rulings are not general for our case, and the lack of generality is indicated by consensus as mentioned from Ibn al-Arabi. In the case of a wife's apostasy, there are three opinions in the Hanafi school: First, Zahir al-Riwayah: the marriage is dissolved, but she is imprisoned and forced to renew Islam and to renew the marriage with her first husband, as stated in Qadhi Khan, Alamgiri, Durr al-Mukhtar, and Shami. Even if she apostatized to escape him, they said this to block the door entirely, so that apostasy is not made a stratagem. Second, the opinion of the scholars of Balkh, Samarqand, and some scholars of Bukhara, Abu Nasr al-Dabusi, and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar: the marriage is not dissolved; she remains in wedlock. Third, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa: she is made a slave-girl even in Dar al-Islam, and her husband retains possession, but if in Dar al-Islam, the husband must purchase her from the Imam; if in Dar al-Harb, no permission needed. Summary: three opinions: (1) marriage dissolved but forced to remarry (Zahir al-Riwayah), (2) marriage remains, (3) she becomes a slave-girl (narration from Abu Hanifa). The difference between the second and third opinions is whether she can become a slave in Dar al-Islam or not.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) situation: a wife might apostatize to dissolve her marriage. The Hanafi school has three internal opinions to prevent this trick. The first (Zahir al-Riwayah) declares the marriage dissolved but forces her to remarry the same husband, blocking any benefit from apostasy. The second opinion keeps the marriage intact, denying any effect. The third opinion treats her as a slave, allowing the husband to reacquire her (through purchase in Dar al-Islam, freely in Dar al-Harb). All three aim to prevent apostasy from being a valid means to end a marriage. The commentary emphasizes that the wife is compelled to return to the same husband to close the door to hila.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted position from the six authoritative works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, representing the mainstream Hanafi view.
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem used to circumvent a prohibition; here, apostasy intended to dissolve marriage is blocked by compelling remarriage.
سد الذرائع (sadd al-dhara'i): Blocking the means to evil; the principle used to prevent apostasy from becoming a trick for divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah position in Hanafi fiqh, what happens to a wife who apostatizes and then returns to Islam?
A) The marriage is automatically dissolved and she may marry anyone she wishes.
B) She is forced to renew her marriage with her original husband.
C) She becomes a slave-girl and must be purchased by her husband.
D) She remains married without any change.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a wife's apostasy does not grant her freedom from her husband; the relied-upon position forces remarriage to the same husband to prevent a hila.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

The Hila for an Apostate Wife in a Non-Muslim State
Selecting the Mashayikh of Balkh's view as a hila for apostasy cases in British India

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a fatwa for the case of a wife's apostasy when the state cannot compel renewal, by applying the Hanafi hierarchy of authority and the principle of darurah.

Core Idea
When the ideal Hanafi ruling cannot be enforced, necessity permits adopting a weaker view — but the prohibition of intercourse remains.

Classical Hanafi law (Zahir al-Riwayah) rules that a wife's apostasy annuls the marriage and requires renewal of Islam and the nikah. However, in British India, there was no Muslim authority to compel such renewal. Ashraf Ali Thanwi, in his treatise Al-Hilatun Najijah, presents a legal stratagem (hila) by adopting the view of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand that the marriage remains valid despite apostasy. Crucially, he insists that even with this ruling, intercourse with the apostate wife remains prohibited until she returns to Islam, based on Quranic injunctions and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi views on apostasy and marriage
List the three positions: 1) Zahir al-Riwayah: marriage annulled, must renew Islam and marriage. 2) Nawadir: marriage not annulled. 3) Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand: marriage not annulled, but woman kept as slave? (The text is ambiguous but the operative view is that marriage continues.) Note that all three agree the woman cannot remarry another man.
This consensus prevents the woman from leaving her husband and marrying someone else.
2
Determine which view is mufta bihi under ideal conditions
Under normal circumstances, the fatwa is based on Zahir al-Riwayah (annulment). This is the strongest authority.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
3
Recognize the practical impossibility in a non-Muslim state
In British India, after giving a verdict of annulment, there was no Muslim government to compel the couple to renew Islam and marriage. Thus, adopting Zahir al-Riwayah would lead to an impasse: the marriage is declared void, but the woman cannot remarry (due to consensus), and there is no mechanism to restore the marriage. The Nawadir view is even more impractical (requires buying the wife as a slave).
The author notes that even where some Muslim authority exists, difficulties arise, as mentioned in Shami.
4
Apply necessity (darurah) to select the viable view
Since neither Zahir al-Riwayah nor Nawadir can be implemented, the only option is to adopt the view of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand: the marriage remains valid. This avoids the harm (darar) of leaving the woman in a legal limbo.
This is a classic case of taghayyur al-zaman (change of times) justifying a shift in fatwa.
5
Articulate the necessary caveat: prohibition of intercourse
Even though the marriage is considered valid, the husband cannot have intercourse with his apostate wife until she renews Islam. The Quran prohibits marrying polytheists (Q. 2:221), and there is ijma on the prohibition of intercourse with a non-Muslim. The exception for kitabiyyah does not apply to apostates. Fiqh precedents (such as a husband buying his own apostate wife as a slave) confirm that ownership or marital validity does not permit intercourse.
This preserves the Islamic prohibition while allowing the marriage to continue legally.
