مسلم مشائخ تجدید اسلام سے پہلے مرتد بیوی سے ہمبستری وغیرہ حرام ہے بلے کے قوال کے موافقی جبکہ بقا و نکاح کا فتوی دیا جائے تو ساتھ ہی اس امر کا لحاظ رکھنا ضروری ہے کہ تجدید اسلام سے قبل شوہر کے لیے اس پرندہ سے استمتاع لینی جماع اور اس کے دواعي مثل تقبيل ولس بالشهوة وغيرہ کو جائز نہ کہا جائے کیونکہ آیت کریمہ لا تنكحوا المشركات حتى يومن سے کافر عورتوں کے ساتھ نکاح اور استمتاع کا حرام ہونا ظاہر ہے اور اس پر اجماع بھی ہے اور کتابیہ کا انتنام جو آیت وا لحضت من الذین اوتوا الکتاب میں وارد ہوا ہے اس سے کتابیہ اصطبیہ بلیہ مراد ہے وہ مرتدہ اس میں داخل نہیں جس نے اہل کتاب کا مذہب اختیار کر لیا ہو اور قول مذکور پر تقاء نکاح سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ حالت کفر میں صحبت و جماع ودوائی بھی معائنہ رہیں ۔ فقہ میں ایسے نظائر موجود ہیں کہ باوجود صحت نکاح و بقا د نکاح کے جماع و
ائے اسی طرح روایت نو اور بیعنی استرقاق کی صورت میں بھی گو قبضہ مالکا نہ خاوند کا اس پڑھو جائے گا لیکن استماع جائز نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ انتہ مشرکہ سے باوجود قبضہ مالکانہ کے استمتاع جائز نہیں
Second: that the marriage will not be annulled at all, but both will remain husband and wife as before. Third: that the woman will be kept as a slave-girl. In these three statements, although there is some difference, but on this point all three agree: that the woman will not be given any right to separate from her first husband's marriage and marry elsewhere. Therefore it will be agreed that the woman will have absolutely no option to marry elsewhere. Now in India, in the present state, acting on this agreed ruling while adopting the first narration is impossible, because after giving the verdict of annulment of marriage, there is no power among Muslims to compel renewal of marriage. And where such power exists, difficulties are faced as mentioned in the passage from Shami. Therefore, adopting the first ruling, i.e., Zahir al-Riwayah, has become impossible in present-day India, because although acting on one part of it is within control, the second part, i.e., compelling renewal of Islam and renewal of marriage, is absolutely not within control. And acting on the Nawadir narration is even more difficult than Zahir al-Riwayah, rather impossible in the present state. Therefore, now there is no option except to adopt the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand and give fatwa accordingly. Although the author of al-Nahr did not face these difficulties that we are facing today, yet in his own time he advised giving fatwa on this narration and considered acting contrary to it as causing severe hardship, as quoted in the passage from Shami. However, along with giving fatwa on this narration, it is also necessary that before renewal of Islam and renewal of marriage, the husband should not be permitted to enjoy (istimta'), i.e., intercourse, etc., as will soon come in the text under 'Some Necessary Issues'. And Allamah Shami is not opposed to this fatwa, and whatever he said was said at a time when acting on the Nawadir narration was possible. When that is not possible, then according to him too, giving fatwa according to the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand is determined. Similarly, other jurists too have narrated this saying and do not reject it. Therefore, in present-day India, where the government is not Muslim, there is no way to act on the Hanafi madhhab except to give fatwa according to the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand that the marriage is not annulled by the woman's apostasy, but remains as it is. The Muslim Mashayikh: before renewal of Islam, intercourse with the apostate wife is prohibited. According to [unclear] saying, when fatwa is given for the continuation of marriage, it is necessary to observe that before renewal of Islam, for the husband, enjoyment (istimta') i.e., intercourse and its precursors like kissing, licking with desire, etc., should not be considered permissible, because from the noble verse 'Do not marry polytheist women until they believe', the prohibition of marriage and enjoyment with disbelieving women is clear, and there is consensus (ijma) on it. And the exception of kitabiyyah which occurs in the verse '...and the chaste among those who were given the Scripture...' refers to original kitabiyyah, not to an apostate who has adopted the religion of the People of the Book. And from the continuation of marriage according to the mentioned saying, it does not follow that intercourse, coitus, and its precursors remain permissible in the state of disbelief. Such examples exist in fiqh that despite the validity and continuity of marriage, intercourse is [unclear]. Similarly, in the case of the Nawadir narration and then buying [slave-girl], even though the husband gains ownership, enjoyment is not permissible, just as with a polytheist woman, despite ownership, enjoyment is not permissible.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) for the problematic case of a wife's apostasy when the Islamic state cannot enforce the ideal ruling. The author (Ashraf Ali Thanwi) presents three scholarly views on the effect of apostasy on marriage: (1) The ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah: marriage is annulled (faskh) and the couple must renew Islam and marriage to continue. (2) The Nawadir view: marriage is not annulled at all; the couple remain married. (3) The view of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand: marriage is not annulled, but the woman is treated as a slave-girl (umm walad?) in terms of ownership? Actually the text says 'عورت کو کنیز بنا کر رکھا جائے گا' meaning the woman will be kept as a slave. However, all three agree that the woman cannot remarry another man. In British India, where there is no Muslim authority to compel the couple to renew Islam and marriage, the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling is unenforceable because its second part (compelling renewal) is impossible. Acting on the Nawadir view is even more difficult. Therefore, the author adopts the view of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand as a hila: the marriage remains valid despite apostasy. However, he immediately qualifies that even though the marriage continues, the husband is not permitted to have intercourse with his apostate wife until she renews Islam. This is because the Quran prohibits marriage to polytheists (though this wife was originally Muslim, she is now an apostate), and ijma prohibits intercourse with a non-Muslim woman. The exception for kitabiyyah (Jewish/Christian women) does not apply to an apostate who adopted the People of the Book religion. The author cites fiqh precedents where marriage remains valid but intercourse is prohibited (e.g., when a man buys his own apostate wife as a slave). Thus, the hila solves the legal gridlock: the marriage is not dissolved, so the wife cannot remarry; but the husband cannot treat her as a wife sexually until she returns to Islam. This preserves the marital bond while discouraging apostasy and maintaining Islamic prohibitions.

Key Terms
ارتداد (irtidad): A Muslim's abandonment of Islam, which according to Hanafi fiqh has legal consequences including potential death penalty for men, and affects marriage contracts.
ظاہر الروایت (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authoritative narrations from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six books, generally the primary basis for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less authenticated narrations within the Hanafi school, often from Hasan ibn Ziyad or other disciples, which are not part of the six authoritative books.
مشائخ بلخ وسمرقند (Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand): Later Hanafi scholars from Central Asia who often adopted practical rulings (like the continuation of marriage upon a wife's apostasy) to avoid hardship.
استمتاع (istimta'): Sexual enjoyment, including intercourse and its preliminaries like kissing with desire, which is prohibited with an apostate woman even if the marriage remains valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the one point on which all three scholarly views (about the effect of a wife's apostasy on marriage) agree?
A) The marriage is annulled immediately and she can remarry.
B) The woman becomes a slave-girl and can be sold.
C) The woman is not permitted to remarry another man.
D) The husband must immediately divorce her.

Key Takeaway
In a non-Muslim state, a Hanafi mufti may adopt the view of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand that a wife's apostasy does not annul the marriage, but must strictly forbid intercourse until she returns to Islam.

Apostasy of Wife and Continuation of Marriage: A Hila
Hila case: ruling on the effect of wife's apostasy on marriage in a non-Muslim state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi fatwa for a wife's apostasy in a non-Muslim state and identify the authority hierarchy (Zahir al-Riwayah vs. Balkh scholars) that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
In necessity, marriage does not dissolve by wife's apostasy; the fatwa shifts from Zahir al-Riwayah to the Balkh ruling.

This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) that addresses the difficult situation of a wife's apostasy in a context where strict adherence to the original Hanafi position would cause hardship. The author, drawing on the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand, rules that the marriage continues, but with important restrictions. This lesson examines the ruling itself and the hierarchy of authority that justifies this departure from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Identify the two Hanafi positions on the effect of a wife's apostasy on marriage: Zahir al-Riwayah (marriage dissolves) and the scholars of Balkh (marriage continues).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the basis for adopting the Balkh position
Analyze why the author adopts the Balkh position: necessity (darura) due to the lack of a Muslim government, making it impossible to enforce dissolution.
The principle of darura allows adopting a weaker (marjuh) opinion.
3
Analyze the fatwa hierarchy
Examine the authority hierarchy: Zahir al-Riwayah is the standard, but when rare narrations (nawadir) become accessible due to necessity, later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) may give fatwa accordingly.
Allamah Shami is cited as not opposing this shift.
4
Apply the ruling to a contemporary scenario
Consider a Muslim couple in a non-Muslim country where the wife apostasizes. According to the Balkh fatwa, the marriage remains intact, but with restrictions.
The mufta bihi in this context is the Balkh position.

مسئلہ : صورت مذکورہ میں تجدید نکاح کے لیے انقضائے عدت ضروری نہیں (كما هو ظاهر) لیکن تھوڑا سا ہر جدید ضروری ہے جو دس درہم سے کم نہ ہو جیساکہ فتح جو دس سے القدر ہے اور مہر سابق کا بہتو واجب عد وغیرہ کی عبارات گذشتہ سے معلوم ہو جی فی الذمہ رہنا ظاہری ہے البتہ اگر قبل خلوت میرمرد ہوگئی ہو تو ہر سابق ساقط ہو جاتا ہے خلاصه فتونی

والله سبحانه وتعالى اعلم وهو المستعان وعليه التكلان والحمد الله الذي بعزته وجلاله تتم الصالحات
And Allamah Shami also does not oppose this fatwa, and what he said was said at a time when the rare narrations (nawadir) were accessible. When they are not accessible, then in his view as well, it is determined to give fatwa according to the saying of the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand. Similarly, other jurists also transmit this saying and do not reject it. Therefore, in India, in the present situation where there is no Muslim government, it is impossible to act upon the Hanafi school without giving fatwa according to the saying of the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand: that from the apostasy of a woman, the marriage is not dissolved but remains intact as before. It is certain that before the renewal of Islam, intercourse with the apostate wife is forbidden. According to the saying that rules for the continuation of marriage, it is necessary to keep in mind that before renewal of Islam, for the husband, taking pleasure from her—i.e., sexual intercourse and its preliminaries such as kissing, licking with desire, etc.—should not be considered permissible. Because the noble verse 'Do not marry polytheist women until they believe' shows the prohibition of marriage and pleasure with disbelieving women, and there is consensus upon it. And the exception of the People of the Book that occurs in the verse 'And the chaste women from those who were given the Book before you' refers to chaste women of the People of the Book, not including the apostate who has adopted the religion of the People of the Book. And from the mentioned saying of the continuation of marriage, it does not necessitate that during the state of disbelief, sexual intercourse and its preliminaries remain lawful. There are similar instances in fiqh where despite the validity of marriage and its continuation, intercourse and its preliminaries are forbidden. Similarly, in the case of a slave woman who is owned by force (istirqaq), although the husband will have ownership of her, taking pleasure will not be permissible, just as with a polytheist woman, despite ownership, taking pleasure is not permissible. Similarly, a woman who has been subjected to suspicious intercourse (muwatua' bi al-shubhah): her marriage remains intact, but until the expiration of the waiting period, intercourse with her is absolutely forbidden. Similarly, a woman pregnant from fornication, if she marries someone other than the fornicator, the marriage is valid, but the husband is not allowed to have intercourse. The matter of the condition of renewal of Islam for the permissibility of pleasure has been proven from the mentioned verse and consensus in the first issue. Then, after renewal of Islam, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, renewal of marriage is also necessary; without it, pleasure is not permissible. But according to the saying of the scholars of Balkh, renewal of marriage is not a condition, as has been clarified in the passage from Sharh Fiqh Akbar Nashr. However, in this particular case, there is no compelling need to abandon Zahir al-Riwayah, so renewal of marriage will also be declared necessary, for in this there is precaution. Issue: In the mentioned situation, for the renewal of marriage, the expiration of the waiting period is not necessary (as is apparent), but a new dower is necessary, which should not be less than ten dirhams, as is in Fath al-Qadir. And the previous dower remains a debt in the husband's liability, unless before seclusion (khalwa) the husband died; then the previous dower is dropped. Summary of this fatwa: The woman will remain in the possession of the same husband as before; it is never permissible for another person to marry her. But as long as she does not renew Islam and renew marriage, intercourse and its preliminaries will not be considered permissible with her. And Allah knows best, and He is the Helper, and upon Him is the reliance. And all praise is to Allah, by whose might and majesty good deeds are completed.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) case addressing the problem of a wife's apostasy in the context of a non-Muslim government (India under British rule). The author, following the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand (muta'akhkhirin), rules that the marriage does not dissolve upon apostasy, contrary to Zahir al-Riwayah (which holds that apostasy dissolves the marriage). This is adopted out of necessity to preserve the family and prevent greater harm. However, the author immediately adds the critical condition: despite the marriage's continuance, intercourse and its preliminaries are forbidden during the state of disbelief, based on Quranic prohibition and consensus. After the wife renews Islam, the author, opting for precaution (ihtiyat), requires both renewal of Islam and renewal of marriage (following Zahir al-Riwayah) before intercourse becomes permissible, even though the Balkh scholars only require renewal of Islam. The renewal of marriage does not require waiting for the waiting period, but a new dower (mahr) of at least ten dirhams is needed; the previous dower remains a debt unless the husband died before seclusion. This hila thus preserves the marital bond legally while maintaining the prohibition of intercourse until the wife returns to Islam and the marriage is renewed, balancing necessity with strict adherence to the texts.

Key Terms
مرتدہ (murtadda): A woman who has renounced Islam (apostate wife).
بقا نکاح (baqa al-nikah): The continuation of the marriage contract despite apostasy.
تجدید اسلام (tajdid al-islam): Renewal of Islam by the apostate wife, i.e., pronouncing shahada and returning to Islam.
تجدید نکاح (tajdid al-nikah): Renewal of the marriage contract after the wife's return to Islam.
ضرورت (darura): Necessity that permits shifting from the original ruling to a more lenient one.
اختیاط (ihtiyat): Precaution; adopting the stricter of two valid opinions to ensure compliance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hila presented in this passage, what must happen before a husband can lawfully have intercourse with his apostate wife in a non-Muslim state?
A) She must renew Islam only.
B) She must renew Islam and renew the marriage contract, and a new dower of at least ten dirhams must be given.
C) The husband must divorce her first and then remarry.
D) She must complete a waiting period of three months.

Key Takeaway
The marriage survives apostasy in necessity, but marital relations are suspended until full renewal.

Conditions for Permissibility After Apostate Wife's Return to Islam
Hila conditions: detailing the steps to restore marital relations after wife's apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions that must be fulfilled before a husband can lawfully have intercourse with his wife after her apostasy, according to the author's precautionary fatwa.

Core Idea
After the wife renews Islam, both renewal of marriage and a new dower are required for intercourse; the waiting period is not needed.

While the marriage continues despite apostasy, the husband cannot have marital relations until specific conditions are met. This lesson details the steps the wife and husband must take to restore full marital intimacy, following the author's precautionary approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition during apostasy
Recognize that the Quranic verse 'Do not marry polytheist women until they believe' and consensus forbid intercourse while the wife is an apostate.
The prohibition applies even though the marriage contract remains valid.
2
First condition: renewal of Islam
The wife must profess the shahada and return to Islam (tajdid al-islam) before any intimacy is considered.
This is agreed upon by all parties.
3
Second condition: renewal of marriage
Despite the Balkh scholars not requiring it, the author insists on renewal of the marriage contract (tajdid al-nikah) as a precaution (ihtiyat).
This aligns with Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Third condition: a new dower
A new dower (mahr) of at least ten dirhams must be given at the time of renewal. The previous dower remains a debt unless the husband died before seclusion.
Reference: Fath al-Qadir.
5
Note the non-requirement of waiting period
The renewal of marriage can take place immediately; no waiting period (iddah) is needed.
This is apparent from the text.

اور علامہ شامی بھی اس فتوے کے مخالف نہیں اور جو کچھ فرمایا ہے وہ روایت نوادر پر قدرت ہونے کے وقت فرمایا ہے اور جب اُس پر قدرت نہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک بھی مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند کے قول پر فتوئی دینا متعین ہے اسی طرح دوسرے فقہاء بھی اس قول کو نقل کر کے تردید نہیں کرتے۔ پس ہندوستان میں بحالت موجودہ کہ حکومت مسلمانوں کی نہیں اس کے سوا مذہب حنفی پر عمل کرنا غیرممکن ہے کہ مشائخ بلخ د سمرقند کے قول کے موافق یوں فتوی دیا جائے کہ عورت کے ارتداد سے نکاح فسخ ہی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بدستور باقی رہتا ہے.
مسلم مشائخ تجدید اسلام سے پہلے مرتد بیوی سے ہمبستری وغیرہ حرام ہے بلے کے قوال کے موافقی جبکہ بقا و نکاح کا فتوی دیا جائے تو ساتھ ہی اس امر کا لحاظ رکھنا ضروری ہے کہ تجدید اسلام سے قبل شوہر کے لیے اس پرندہ سے استمتاع لینی جماع اور اس کے دواعي مثل تقبيل ولس بالشهوة وغيرہ کو جائز نہ کہا جائے کیونکہ آیت کریمہ لا تنكحوا المشركات حتى يومن سے کافر عورتوں کے ساتھ نکاح اور استمتاع کا حرام ہونا ظاہر ہے اور اس پر اجماع بھی ہے اور کتابیہ کا انتنام جو آیت وا لحضت من الذین اوتوا الکتاب میں وارد ہوا ہے اس سے کتابیہ اصطبیہ بلیہ مراد ہے وہ مرتدہ اس میں داخل نہیں جس نے اہل کتاب کا مذہب اختیار کر لیا ہو اور قول مذکور پر تقاء نکاح سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ حالت کفر میں صحبت و جماع ودوائی بھی معائنہ رہیں ۔ فقہ میں ایسے نظائر موجود ہیں کہ باوجود صحت نکاح و بقا د نکاح کے جماع و ائے اسی طرح روایت نو اور بیعنی استرقاق کی صورت میں بھی گو قبضہ مالکا نہ خاوند کا اس پڑھو جائے گا لیکن استماع جائز نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ انتہ مشرکہ سے باوجود قبضہ مالکانہ کے استمتاع جائز نہیں

دوائی جماع حرام ہوتے ہیں جیسے موطوہ بالشہر کہ اس کا نکاح بدستور سابق قائم ہے۔ مگر انقضائے عدت تک اُس سے ہمبستری وغیرہ بالکل حرام ہے ۔ اسی طرح حاملہ من الزنا اگر غیر زانی سے نکاح کرلے تو گو نکاح صحیح ہو جاتا ہے مگر شوہر کو محبت جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ مسئلہ حلت استمتاع کے لیے تجدید اسلام کا شرط ہونا تو آیت مذکورہ اور اجماع وغیرہ سے مسئلہ اولیٰ میں ثابت ہو چکا ہے۔ پھر تجدید اسلام کے بعد ظاہر الروایہ کے موافق تجدید نکاح بھی ضروری ہے بغیر اس کے استمتاع جائز نہیں۔ مگر مشائخ بلخ کے قول پر تجدید نکاح شرط نہیں جیسا کہ عبارت شرح فقہ اکبر نشر میں اس کی تصریح گذری ہے لیکن اس خاص جزء میں ظاہر الروایہ کو ترک کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت داعی نہیں لہذا جند تجدید نکاح کو بھی ضروری کہا جائے گا کہ اسی میں اختیاط ہے۔
مسئلہ : صورت مذکورہ میں تجدید نکاح کے لیے انقضائے عدت ضروری نہیں (كما هو ظاهر) لیکن تھوڑا سا ہر جدید ضروری ہے جو دس درہم سے کم نہ ہو جیساکہ فتح جو دس سے القدر ہے اور مہر سابق کا بہتو واجب عد وغیرہ کی عبارات گذشتہ سے معلوم ہو جی فی الذمہ رہنا ظاہری ہے البتہ اگر قبل خلوت میرمرد ہوگئی ہو تو ہر سابق ساقط ہو جاتا ہے خلاصه فتونی
اس مجموعہ سے خلاصہ اس فتویٰ کا یہ حاصل ہوا کہ عورت بدستور سابق اسی خاوند کے قبضہ میں رہے گی کسی دوسرے شخص سے ہر گز نکاح جائز نہیں لیکن جب تک تجدید اسلام کر کے تجدید نکاح نہ کرے اُس وقت تک اُس کے ساتھ جماع اور دوائی جماع کو جائز نہ کہا جائے گا۔
والله سبحانه وتعالى اعلم وهو المستعان وعليه التكلان والحمد الله الذي بعزته وجلاله تتم الصالحات
And Allamah Shami also does not oppose this fatwa, and what he said was said at a time when the rare narrations (nawadir) were accessible. When they are not accessible, then in his view as well, it is determined to give fatwa according to the saying of the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand. Similarly, other jurists also transmit this saying and do not reject it. Therefore, in India, in the present situation where there is no Muslim government, it is impossible to act upon the Hanafi school without giving fatwa according to the saying of the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand: that from the apostasy of a woman, the marriage is not dissolved but remains intact as before. It is certain that before the renewal of Islam, intercourse with the apostate wife is forbidden. According to the saying that rules for the continuation of marriage, it is necessary to keep in mind that before renewal of Islam, for the husband, taking pleasure from her—i.e., sexual intercourse and its preliminaries such as kissing, licking with desire, etc.—should not be considered permissible. Because the noble verse 'Do not marry polytheist women until they believe' shows the prohibition of marriage and pleasure with disbelieving women, and there is consensus upon it. And the exception of the People of the Book that occurs in the verse 'And the chaste women from those who were given the Book before you' refers to chaste women of the People of the Book, not including the apostate who has adopted the religion of the People of the Book. And from the mentioned saying of the continuation of marriage, it does not necessitate that during the state of disbelief, sexual intercourse and its preliminaries remain lawful. There are similar instances in fiqh where despite the validity of marriage and its continuation, intercourse and its preliminaries are forbidden. Similarly, in the case of a slave woman who is owned by force (istirqaq), although the husband will have ownership of her, taking pleasure will not be permissible, just as with a polytheist woman, despite ownership, taking pleasure is not permissible. Similarly, a woman who has been subjected to suspicious intercourse (muwatua' bi al-shubhah): her marriage remains intact, but until the expiration of the waiting period, intercourse with her is absolutely forbidden. Similarly, a woman pregnant from fornication, if she marries someone other than the fornicator, the marriage is valid, but the husband is not allowed to have intercourse. The matter of the condition of renewal of Islam for the permissibility of pleasure has been proven from the mentioned verse and consensus in the first issue. Then, after renewal of Islam, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, renewal of marriage is also necessary; without it, pleasure is not permissible. But according to the saying of the scholars of Balkh, renewal of marriage is not a condition, as has been clarified in the passage from Sharh Fiqh Akbar Nashr. However, in this particular case, there is no compelling need to abandon Zahir al-Riwayah, so renewal of marriage will also be declared necessary, for in this there is precaution. Issue: In the mentioned situation, for the renewal of marriage, the expiration of the waiting period is not necessary (as is apparent), but a new dower is necessary, which should not be less than ten dirhams, as is in Fath al-Qadir. And the previous dower remains a debt in the husband's liability, unless before seclusion (khalwa) the husband died; then the previous dower is dropped. Summary of this fatwa: The woman will remain in the possession of the same husband as before; it is never permissible for another person to marry her. But as long as she does not renew Islam and renew marriage, intercourse and its preliminaries will not be considered permissible with her. And Allah knows best, and He is the Helper, and upon Him is the reliance. And all praise is to Allah, by whose might and majesty good deeds are completed.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) case addressing the problem of a wife's apostasy in the context of a non-Muslim government (India under British rule). The author, following the scholars of Balkh and Samarkand (muta'akhkhirin), rules that the marriage does not dissolve upon apostasy, contrary to Zahir al-Riwayah (which holds that apostasy dissolves the marriage). This is adopted out of necessity to preserve the family and prevent greater harm. However, the author immediately adds the critical condition: despite the marriage's continuance, intercourse and its preliminaries are forbidden during the state of disbelief, based on Quranic prohibition and consensus. After the wife renews Islam, the author, opting for precaution (ihtiyat), requires both renewal of Islam and renewal of marriage (following Zahir al-Riwayah) before intercourse becomes permissible, even though the Balkh scholars only require renewal of Islam. The renewal of marriage does not require waiting for the waiting period, but a new dower (mahr) of at least ten dirhams is needed; the previous dower remains a debt unless the husband died before seclusion. This hila thus preserves the marital bond legally while maintaining the prohibition of intercourse until the wife returns to Islam and the marriage is renewed, balancing necessity with strict adherence to the texts.

Key Terms
مرتدہ (murtadda): A woman who has renounced Islam (apostate wife).
بقا نکاح (baqa al-nikah): The continuation of the marriage contract despite apostasy.
تجدید اسلام (tajdid al-islam): Renewal of Islam by the apostate wife, i.e., pronouncing shahada and returning to Islam.
تجدید نکاح (tajdid al-nikah): Renewal of the marriage contract after the wife's return to Islam.
اختیاط (ihtiyat): Precaution; adopting the stricter of two valid opinions to ensure compliance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum new dower required for renewal of marriage after the wife's return to Islam, according to the passage?
A) One dirham
B) Ten dirhams
C) The same as the previous dower
D) No dower is needed

Key Takeaway
Restoration of marital intimacy requires three steps: renewal of Islam, renewal of marriage, and a new dower; no waiting period.

Parsing a Maliki Fatwa: The Case of the Missing Husband's Wife
Maliki mufti's answer on remarriage for a woman with a missing husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse a Maliki fatwa on the missing husband's wife, identify the three authorities (judge, governor, community of Muslims), and explain their hierarchy.

Core Idea
In the Maliki school, a woman with a missing husband can have her marriage dissolved by a judge, governor, or community of Muslims, in that order.

This lesson presents a fatwa from the Maliki mufti of Medina, Shaykh Sa'id bin Siddiq al-Fullati, responding to practical questions about a woman whose husband has disappeared. The fatwa provides a detailed procedure for dissolving the marriage and remarrying, based on Mukhtasar al-Khalil and other Maliki texts. Although this is a Maliki fatwa, understanding it is important for Hanafi muftis who may encounter such cases or need to respond to comparisons. The lesson guides you through parsing the fatwa's structure and its procedural rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the questions
Read the fatwa and list the three questions posed to the mufti: (0) whether the ruling applies to women in non-Muslim lands, (1) the procedure for remarrying when the husband left no maintenance, and (1) whether a judge's ruling is necessary and how to act in lands dominated by disbelievers.
The second question has two parts.
2
Locate the answer structure
The mufti begins by stating that the texts of the school are consistent that the missing person is of six types and that the wife must raise her case to the judge, governor, or community of Muslims. Then he details the hierarchy.
3
Extract the three authorities
Identify the three entities: al-qadi (judge), al-wali (governor), and jama'at al-Muslimin (community of Muslims). Note their roles.
The community of Muslims is defined as a group of righteous individuals.
4
Determine the hierarchy
If all three exist, the woman must go to the judge. If the judge is absent or oppressive, she may go to the governor or community. If the governor is present, going to the community is invalid.
5
Note the role of necessity
The fatwa also addresses rulings from judges appointed by non-Muslim rulers, stating that they are implemented out of necessity, even though the appointment is invalid.
This reflects the principle of 'necessity permits the prohibited'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(م) هل الصورة الثانية للمفقود المذكورة في مختصر الخليل تختص بامرأة كانت من سكان البلاد الاسلامية فذهب زوجها إلى البلاد الشركية فقد هناك امر تشتمل القاطنه بالبلاد التي استولى عليها الكفار وبالديار العربية الاصلية المكيف الامر (0) المفقود عنها زوجها سواء كانت من البلاد الاسلامية او الشركية اذ الم يترك زوجها عندها نفقة وهي في غاية عن الاحتياج والفافة اوات بحنت يخشى عليها الفساد بالغروبة كيف السبيل لها اذا ارادت التزوج او اراد اهلها ذلك - (1) المفقود عنها زوجها اذا المريكي عندها النفقة وهى محتاجة او يخشى عليها من الفساد هل يصح تطليقها او فسخ نكاحها من غير حكم الحاكم الشرعى ام لا بد من الحكم وعلى الثاني كيف يعمل بالبلاد الاسلامية اللتي تغلب عليها الاكفارا فيدونا الجزيل - الجواب من العلامة سعيد بن صديق الفلاتي دامت بركاته مفتى المالكيه بالمدينة المنورة زادها الله نور بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الجواب والله اعلم بالصواب ومن فضله نرتجي النواب هران نصوص المذهب مطبقة من ان المفقود على ستة إقامكما سفر مفصلة الاحكام وعلى ان زوجية لا بد لها من الرفع المقاضي او الوالي او من يقوم مقامهما عند عد مهما من والى لماء اوجماعة المسلمين لاتهه يقومون مقام الحاكم العدل عندندمه ولكن عند وجود الثلاثة لو ترفع الا للضافي خان رفعت لغيره مع التمكن من الرفع له حرم عليها ذلك وان مضى ما فعله از كان هو الوالي لجماعة المسلمين هذا ما يظهر من كلاما بن عرفة كما قاله الاجهوري راما لو رفقت الجماعة المسلميين مع وجود الوالى فالظاهر معنى فصلهم وفي السنهوري وتبعه اللقاني ان ظاهر کلاه خليل ان الثلاث في مرتبة واحدة الا ان القاضي اضبط ووجود القاضی اوغیره ممن ذكر مع كونه يحورا وياخذ المال الكثير بمنزلة علامہ فترفع لجماعة المسلمين من صالحي جيرانهار عد وليه وغيرهم لانهم كالامام عند عدمه وما يفهم من تعبير هم بجماعة المسلمين ان الواحد لا يكنى وكذالاثنان و به صرح الا جمهوری فعلم انها ان ارادت الفع في شان زوجها ووحدت الثلاثة وجب للقاضي فان رفعت الغيرة حرم وصح و ان رفعت الجماعة المسلمين لم يصح وان لم يكن قاض حيرت فيهمانان رفعت لجماعة المسلمين صح على الظاهر وإن لم يوجد واحد من الثلاثة رفعت لجماعة المسلمين واهلها منهم وكذا القضاة والحناء المولون للأحكام من الكفار المستولي على بلاد المسلمين لحجز الناس بعضهم عن بعض فتند ادعى بعض أهل الهلال انه راجب عقلاوان كان باطلا تولية الكافر لهواء القضاة اما بطلب الرعية له اواقامة لهم المضرورة لذلك فلا يطرح حكمهم بل يننذ كما لورروهم سلطان مسلم فتمضى احكامهم للضرورة العلويذ هذا الناس في قبول توليتهم فتطيع الحقوق وفي كتاب الايمان في مسالة الحالف ليقضينك حقك الى اجل أقام شيوخ المكان مقام السلطان عند فقده لما يخاف من فوات القضية وعن مطرف وابن الماجشون فيمن خرج
(M) Is the second situation of the missing person mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Khalil specific to a woman who was a resident of Islamic lands, then her husband went to the lands of shirk, and is lost there? Or does it include the resident of lands occupied by disbelievers and the original Arab lands? How is the matter? (0) The woman whose husband is missing, whether she is from Islamic lands or lands of shirk, since her husband left no maintenance for her and she is in extreme need and poverty, and it is feared she may fall into corruption due to being a stranger; what is the way for her if she wants to marry, or her family wants that? (1) The woman whose husband is missing, if he left no maintenance for her and she is in need, or it is feared she may fall into corruption, is it valid to divorce her or dissolve her marriage without the ruling of a legitimate judge, or must there be a ruling? And on the second, how to act in Islamic lands that are dominated by disbelievers? We request a detailed answer. The answer from al-Allamah Sa'id bin Siddiq al-Fullati, may his blessings continue, Mufti of the Malikis in Medina, may Allah increase its light. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The answer: And Allah knows best what is correct, and from His grace we hope for success. Indeed, the texts of the school are consistent that the missing person is of six types: residency and travel with detailed rulings, and that his wife must raise the matter to the judge or the governor or whoever takes their place when they are absent, from any governor or a group of Muslims, because they take the place of the just ruler when he is absent. But when the three exist, she should not raise it to anyone other than the judge. If she raised it to another while able to raise it to the judge, that is forbidden for her, though what she did takes effect if he was the governor of the community of Muslims. This is what appears from the words of Ibn 'Arafah as al-Ajhuri said. As for if she raised it to the community of Muslims while the governor was present, the apparent meaning is that it is invalid. In al-Sanhuri, followed by al-Laqqani, it is stated that the apparent meaning of Khalil is that the three are of one rank, except that the judge is more precise. And the presence of the judge or others mentioned, despite being oppressive and taking much wealth, is like him in some respect? So she raises to the community of Muslims from among the righteous neighbors, etc., because they are like the imam in his absence. What is understood from their expression 'community of Muslims' is that one is not sufficient, nor two, and al-Ajhuri explicitly stated that. So it is known that if she wants to take action concerning her husband and she finds the three, she must go to the judge. If she raises to another, it is forbidden but valid. If she raises to the community of Muslims, it is invalid. If there is no judge, she has choice between them? If she raises to the community of Muslims, it is valid according to the apparent opinion. If none of the three exist, she raises to the community of Muslims and her family from among them. Likewise, the judges and rulers appointed for rulings by the disbelievers who have taken over Muslim lands, due to people preventing each other, so some people of the city claim that it is rationally obligatory, even if the appointment of a disbeliever as a judge is invalid, whether by request of the subjects or due to necessity, their rulings are not discarded but are executed, just as if a Muslim sultan appointed them, so their rulings are implemented out of necessity because people have accepted their appointment regarding rights. And in the book of oaths, in the issue of one who swears 'I will surely give you your right' until a time, the local elders take the place of the sultan in his absence due to fear of losing the case. And from Mutarrif and Ibn al-Majishun regarding one who left ...
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a fatwa from a Maliki mufti (Sa'id bin Siddiq al-Fullati) responding to questions about a woman whose husband is missing (mafqud) and who has no maintenance. The fatwa outlines the Maliki procedure for dissolving the marriage and remarrying. The questions are three: (1) whether the ruling applies to women in non-Muslim lands, (2) the way for such a woman to remarry, and (3) whether a judge's ruling is necessary and how to proceed in lands dominated by non-Muslims. The mufti answers that according to the established texts of the Maliki school, the missing person is categorized into six types. The wife must raise her case to a judge (qadi), a governor (wali), or a community of Muslims (jama'at al-Muslimin), as they stand in for the just ruler. However, if all three are present, she must go to the judge; going to another is forbidden but valid if that person is the governor. If only the community is present, going to them is valid. If the judge is oppressive or takes bribes, she may go to the community. The mufti also addresses the validity of rulings from judges appointed by non-Muslim rulers out of necessity, stating that such rulings are implemented due to necessity, even if the appointment is invalid. This passage illustrates the Maliki perspective on a common procedural issue, which differs from the Hanafi school. In the Hanafi school, the wife of a missing husband must wait a certain period (e.g., 90 years according to some) or seek a judge's permission for dissolution based on specific conditions. This fatwa is included here as a comparative example.

Key Terms
المفقود (al-mafqud): A person whose whereabouts are unknown and whose life or death is uncertain.
جماعة المسلمين (jama'at al-Muslimin): The community of Muslims, specifically a group of righteous and trustworthy individuals who can act as representatives in the absence of a judge or governor.
الحاكم الشرعي (al-hakim al-shar'i): The legitimate Islamic judge authorized to issue binding rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this Maliki fatwa, to whom should a woman with a missing husband first raise her case if a judge, governor, and community of Muslims are all present?
A) The governor (wali)
B) The community of Muslims (jama'at al-Muslimin)
C) The judge (qadi)
D) Any of them, as they are all equal

Key Takeaway
In the Maliki school, the woman must raise her case to the highest available authority: judge, then governor, then community of Muslims, in that order.

Hanafi Mufti's Adab: Responding to the Missing Husband Case
Maliki mufti's answer on remarriage for a woman with a missing husband (used as comparative basis)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the missing husband's wife and apply the principles of mufti adab (including necessity-based exceptions) when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti must prioritize the judge's ruling and use legal stratagems (hiyal) in the absence of a judge, rather than delegating to a lay community.

This lesson builds on the Maliki fatwa from the previous lesson but shifts focus to the Hanafi perspective. The Hanafi school is more cautious about dissolving a marriage without a judge's ruling. However, in real-world situations where no Islamic judge exists, the mufti must apply the principles of mufti adab, including the use of legal stratagems (hiyal) and necessity-based exceptions. This lesson teaches you how a Hanafi mufti should respond to a woman in need.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi default
Recall: The Hanafi school requires a judge's ruling (hukm al-qadi) to dissolve a marriage based on a missing husband. The wife must wait until the husband would be presumed dead (e.g., 90 years from birth) unless a judge decrees otherwise.
This is based on the principle of 'certainty is not removed by doubt'.
2
Identify the evidence
Hanafis rely on the hadith 'There is no divorce before marriage' and qiyas to cases of death. The absence of a judge does not automatically permit remarriage.
3
Consider the absence of a judge
When no qualified Islamic judge exists, Hanafi scholars have recognized the need for a fatwa. The mufti may allow a hila (legal stratagem), such as appointing a trustworthy Muslim as a deputy judge (qadi na'ib) to issue the dissolution.
This is a departure from the default, based on necessity (darurah).
4
Apply hiyal and necessity
The mufti must ensure that all conditions for necessity are met: the husband's absence is prolonged, no maintenance, fear of corruption, and no hope of return. The hila must be executed properly to avoid invalid marriage.
For example, the woman may give a revocable divorce (talaq) to a proxy, then the proxy pronounces it on the husband's behalf, with the mufti supervising.
5
Compare with Maliki approach
Unlike the Maliki school which allows the community to act directly, the Hanafi method preserves the form of a judicial act while adapting to circumstances. The mufti must ensure the procedure is sound according to Hanafi usul.

If she raises to the community of Muslims, it is invalid. If there is no judge, she has choice between them? If she raises to the community of Muslims, it is valid according to the apparent opinion. If none of the three exist, she raises to the community of Muslims and her family from among them. Commentary
This passage is a fatwa from a Maliki mufti (Sa'id bin Siddiq al-Fullati) responding to questions about a woman whose husband is missing (mafqud) and who has no maintenance. The fatwa outlines the Maliki procedure for dissolving the marriage and remarrying. The questions are three: (1) whether the ruling applies to women in non-Muslim lands, (2) the way for such a woman to remarry, and (3) whether a judge's ruling is necessary and how to proceed in lands dominated by non-Muslims. The mufti answers that according to the established texts of the Maliki school, the missing person is categorized into six types. The wife must raise her case to a judge (qadi), a governor (wali), or a community of Muslims (jama'at al-Muslimin), as they stand in for the just ruler. However, if all three are present, she must go to the judge; going to another is forbidden but valid if that person is the governor. If only the community is present, going to them is valid. If the judge is oppressive or takes bribes, she may go to the community. The mufti also addresses the validity of rulings from judges appointed by non-Muslim rulers out of necessity, stating that such rulings are implemented due to necessity, even if the appointment is invalid. This passage illustrates the Maliki perspective on a common procedural issue, which differs from the Hanafi school. In the Hanafi school, the wife of a missing husband must wait a certain period (e.g., 90 years according to some) or seek a judge's permission for dissolution based on specific conditions. This fatwa is included here as a comparative example.

Key Terms
المفقود (al-mafqud): A person whose whereabouts are unknown and whose life or death is uncertain.
جماعة المسلمين (jama'at al-Muslimin): The community of Muslims, specifically a group of righteous and trustworthy individuals who can act as representatives in the absence of a judge or governor.
الحاكم الشرعي (al-hakim al-shar'i): The legitimate Islamic judge authorized to issue binding rulings.
الحيلة (al-hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible result while staying within the framework of the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The wife herself
B) The community of Muslims
C) A qualified judge (qadi) or a deputy acting under his authority
D) The local imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists on a judge's ruling for dissolving a marriage, but mufti adab allows necessity-based fatwas and hiyal in the judge's absence.

The Missing Husband Stratagem: Wife's Path to Annulment
Explains the legal stratagem for the missing husband case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the Hanafi legal stratagem (hila) for the wife of a missing husband to obtain annulment, identifying the conditions and the four-year waiting period based on 'Umar's practice.

Core Idea
A missing husband's wife may seek annulment after a four-year investigation, based on 'Umar's precedent and companion consensus.

This passage presents a classical Hanafi legal stratagem (hila) for a wife whose husband is missing (mafqud al-khabar). It shows how the authorities — the caliph or judge — conduct a thorough investigation before setting a four-year waiting period, after which the marriage may be annulled. This procedure balances the wife's need to remarry with the sanctity of the marital bond, and is grounded in the practice of Caliph 'Umar and the consensus of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Recognize the core issue: a wife's husband is missing, and she cannot bear indefinite waiting. The Hanafi hila provides a remedy.
The mafqud is defined as one whose news is cut off but investigation is possible.
2
List the conditions for initiating the procedure
Identify the prerequisites: no famine/plague, wife not satisfied to wait, proof of marriage and absence, feasibility of investigation, husband's property for maintenance (or wife dropping it), and no fear of adultery due to severe deprivation.
These conditions are derived from the text and the purpose of the hila.
3
Trace the investigation process
The wife raises the matter to the caliph/judge, who verifies her claims and sends a letter with husband's details to the governor of the suspected region. A messenger is dispatched at the wife's expense.
Ibn Naji considered the messenger's fee on the wife.
4
Understand the basis for the waiting period
After investigation, if the husband is not found, the judge sets a four-year period. This is based on the action of 'Umar and the Companions' consensus (dalil naqli).
This period is specific to the Hanafi school and is conditional on the husband having property.
5
Note the practical upshot
Once the four years elapse without news, the wife may obtain judicial annulment and remarry. The hila recognizes the wife's hardship while preserving the marriage bond carefully.
The text ends mid-sentence, implying further details about maintenance dropping.

The procedure for the annulment of the marriage of the wife of the lost-husband. And the missing person in the lands of Islam – Ibn 'Arafah defined it by saying: He is one whose news has been cut off but it is possible to investigate about him; otherwise, if they cannot investigate about him, it is called mafqud in the terminology of the jurists. The missing person in the lands of Islam when there is no famine or plague, if the wife is not satisfied to wait for his return, she may raise her matter to the caliph or the judge or whoever takes their place in their absence so that they may investigate about her husband after the wife establishes [proof of] marriage and the husband's absence and that she is still under his matrimonial authority. When that is established with them, they write a letter including his name, lineage, and description to the governor of the country where his existence is presumed; and if his existence is not presumed in a specific country, he writes to the encompassing country. Ibn Naji considered it preponderant that the fee of the messenger who investigates about the missing person is upon the wife. Then when the investigation ends and the messenger returns to him and informs him... after it is established upon inquiry, he said: it is obligatory to set for him a period of four years from the day [of the husband's disappearance]? This specification is based on the action of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, and the Companions agreed upon it. The place of the mentioned deferment is when the missing person has property from which the woman could spend; in addition, if there is no fear of her committing adultery without intercourse due to the severe harm of leaving intercourse which leads to adultery? Don't you see that if she dropped the maintenance from her husband...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This is a hila case from a Hanafi work on legal stratagems. The passage addresses the problem of a wife whose husband is missing (mafqud al-khabar). The Hanafi position, as derived from this text, provides a procedure for her to obtain judicial annulment of the marriage (faskh) after a thorough investigation and a waiting period. The text defines the mafqud as someone whose news is cut off but is potentially traceable. If the wife cannot bear to wait, she may raise the matter to the caliph, judge, or their deputies. The authorities then verify her marital status and the husband's absence, and send a letter with his details to the governor of the region where he is presumed to exist. If no specific region is known, a general search is conducted. Ibn Naji states that the cost of the messenger is borne by the wife. Upon completion of the investigation, if the husband is not found, the judge sets a period of four years, based on the practice of Caliph 'Umar and the consensus of the Companions. This waiting period applies if the husband has property to provide the wife's maintenance; additionally, it is conditioned that the wife does not fear committing adultery due to severe sexual deprivation. The passage ends mid-sentence discussing the wife dropping maintenance, indicating further details follow.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A missing person whose news is cut off but investigation about them is possible.
الكشف (al-kashf): The investigation process to locate the missing husband, involving correspondence with governors.
أجل اربع سنين (ajal arba' sinin): The four-year waiting period set by the judge for the missing husband's return, based on 'Umar's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila provides a structured path for a wife of a missing husband to obtain annulment after investigation and a four-year waiting period, conditional on the husband having property and other factors.

Ruling on Missing Person: Maliki Hila and Hanafi Comparison
Maliki ruling on missing person's death by preponderant conjecture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki ruling on declaring the death of a missing person by preponderant conjecture and compare it with the Hanafi position that requires a judge's decree.

Core Idea
Preponderant conjecture can legally determine death if circumstantial evidence is strong, but Hanafi requires a judge's ruling.

This passage from Al-Ajhuri, a Maliki scholar, presents a specific legal stratagem (hila) for the wife of a missing person. It identifies exceptional conditions where her husband can be declared dead by preponderant conjecture without a lengthy wait. For the Hanafi school, such a declaration requires a judge's formal decree. Understanding this difference is crucial when advising families of missing persons in modern contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
The passage distinguishes: (1) doubt about whether the person was lost in Muslim or non-Muslim lands, and (2) travel by sea with news cut off.
The first category requires caution (treat wife as missing person); the second has an exception.
2
Locate the exception
The exception: if the loss happened during a severe windstorm with ships at anchor and no news becomes known, then death is judged by preponderant conjecture.
This is the key hila: it allows early remarriage for the wife.
3
Contrast with Hanafi ruling
In the Hanafi school, a missing person's death is not accepted by mere conjecture; a judge must investigate and issue a decree after a sufficient period (often 90 years or when peers die).
The Maliki exception is a practical relief, but Hanafi requires more certainty.
4
Apply as a hila
The Maliki hila is a legal stratagem to prevent hardship for the wife. It permits remarriage based on strong circumstantial evidence.
Muftis must know these differences to advise correctly depending on the school followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقى من شك في حاله هل فقد في بلاد المسلمين والكفار ونص في حاله قال الاجهوري وينبغي العمل بالاحوط تعامل زوجة معاملة مفقود[؟] من الشرك بخلاص[؟] من سافر فى البحر فانقطع خبره[؟] نبيل[؟] سبيل المفقود الا ان يكون فقد في شدة ريح والمراكب في المرسى ولم يتبين له خبر فيحكم بموته غلبة الظن بعزوفه[؟] هذا ملخص احكام المفقود باقسام حررها فى جمادى الاولى سنة سعيد بن صديق
And what remains is one who is doubtful about his condition: whether he was lost in Muslim or non-Muslim lands, and a text about his condition. Al-Ajhuri said: it is proper to act with caution, treat the wife as a missing person from shirk... of one who traveled by sea and his news was cut off... the path of the missing person, unless he was lost in a severe wind and the ships were at anchor and his news did not become known, then his death is judged by preponderant conjecture... This is a summary of rulings on the missing person in categories, written in Jumada al-Ula, year Sa'id bin Siddiq.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Ajhuri, a Maliki scholar, regarding the missing person (mafqud). It summarizes categories: if there is doubt about whether the person was lost in Muslim or non-Muslim land, the wife is treated as a missing person. However, if the loss occurred under specific conditions (e.g., a storm at sea with ships at anchor and no news), then preponderant conjecture (ghalabat al-dhann) determines death. This ruling provides a legal stratagem for the wife to remarry.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A person whose whereabouts and status (dead or alive) are unknown.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-dhann): Preponderant conjecture used to determine death when strong circumstantial evidence exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Maliki hila allows early remarriage for a missing person's wife under specific storm-at-sea conditions, while the Hanafi school requires a judge's decree.

Maliki Ruling for Missing Husband in Dar al-Islam
Maliki fatwa on missing husband in Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki ruling for a missing husband's wife in Dar al-Islam and identify the conditions for its application.

Core Idea
A missing husband in Dar al-Islam: wait 4 years, then iddah 4 months 10 days, then remarry.

This lesson examines a Maliki fatwa that provides a clear legal procedure for a woman whose husband has gone missing. The ruling, attributed to Caliph Umar, specifies waiting periods and maintenance conditions. Understanding this ruling is valuable for any mufti dealing with cross-madhhab solutions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the ruling
The fatwa cites Umar ibn al-Khattab via Yahya ibn Sa'id, recorded in Muwatta and Mudawwanah. This establishes the authority.
The ruling is considered sound in Maliki school.
2
Extract the waiting periods
The wife waits four years (search period), then observes an iddah of four months and ten days.
Total minimum time: 4 years + 4 months + 10 days.
3
Note the maintenance condition
During the four years, the wife is maintained from the missing husband's wealth. No maintenance during the iddah.
This applies only if the husband has wealth.
4
Understand the consequence
After completing the iddah, the wife becomes permissible to remarry.
This is a definitive legal outcome.

تمة احسن الله إليه في الفانية والدائم. ومن عليه وعلى المسلمين بحسن الخال الجواب .. من العلامة الفأها ثم رحمہ الله تعالى مفتى المالكية بالمدينة المنورة زادها الله تعالى شرفا بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد المستحقة واتم الصلواة والتسليم على خير خلقه واله و صحبه وتابع ما وصى : أما السئوال الأول عن مسلمة فقدت زوجها سنين ويولغ في التفتيش عنه ليستبين قلم ينفع ذلك ولم يظهر اسالم هوام هالك نجوا به اذا كان الفقد فى ارض الاسلام وله مال ينفق منه على زوجة المتزوكة في المقام هو ما في الموطا والمدونة وغيرها عن مالك عن يحيى بن سعید ان عمر بن الخطاب قال ايما امرأة فقدت زوجها فلم تدر این هر فانها تنتظر اربع سنين ثم تعتد اربعة اشهر وعشر اثمرتحل و عن ابن وهب أن عمد عمل بذلك ورواه الأئمة مالك والشافيو احمد و ابن ابى شيبة والديمقى والدارقطني عن عمر وعثمان وعلى وابن عباس وابن الزبير رضى الله عنهم وقال مالك ينفق على امرأة المفقود من ماله في الاربع سنين لا في العدة وقال لا يقسم ميران هذا المفقود حتی پاتى موته او يبلغ من الزمان ما لا يحيي مثله وهو سبعون او خمس وسبعون اوثمانون ذكره الشيخ خليل وغيره وفى هذا قال الناظم محمد ابن عاصم في تحفة الاحكام ومن بارض المسلمين ينقد فاريع من السنين الحمد وباعتداد الزوجة الحكم جرى بتعرضا والمال فيه عمرا وقول السائل هل تعتد نفسها بعد الاربعة الاعوام عدة الحمام ام ترفع امرها للحكام او جماعة الاسلام نجوا به مافي مدونة سحنون قلت ارايت امرأة المفقود العتد لو ربع سنين في قول مالك بغير فيجث عنه وبعد الياس نضرب اربع سنين وفي مختصر الشيخ الخليل المالكي وشرح وحواشيه إن لزوجة المفقود الرفع للقاضى والوالي او والى الماءاى جالي الزكاة والا فلجماعة للمسلمين قبل اقلهم ثلاثة من الصلحا او واحد عدل عارف يرجع اليه في المهمات واليرحاء اما مفقود ارض الشرك والاسير فلا يورث مالهما ولا تنكح زوجهما الا بعد التعمير وفي حاشية العدوى على الرسالة ان زوجة مفقود ارض الشرك وزوجة الاسبوء تقيان مدة التعمير لتعذر الكشف عن زوجهما ان دامت نفقتهما والافلهما التطليق كما اذا خشيت على انفسهما الزنا ومثله في شروح المختصر وفيها اعتاق امر ولده بعد مها النفقة اينا دفعا للضررا و تزوج بمن ينفق عليها وفي هذا قال الناظم محمد بن عاصم
Completion: May Allah improve his condition in this world and the next. And may He be pleased with him and with the Muslims for their good character. The answer... from the scholar al-Fa'ha (?), then may Allah have mercy on him, the Mufti of the Malikiyyah in Medina... In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. ... The first question about a Muslim woman who lost her husband for years and they searched but nothing became clear... If the loss was in the land of Islam and he had wealth to spend on his wife, the ruling is as in al-Muwatta and al-Mudawwanah from Malik from Yahya ibn Sa'id that Umar ibn al-Khattab said: Any woman who loses her husband and does not know where he is, she waits four years, then observes iddah of four months and ten days, then she becomes permissible (to remarry). And it was narrated from Ibn Wahb that Umar acted upon that... Imam Malik said: The wife of the missing person is maintained from his wealth during the four years, not during the iddah. And he said: The inheritance of this missing person is not divided until his death comes or he reaches an age after which one does not live, which is seventy, seventy-five, or eighty... As for the missing person in the land of shirk and the captive, their wealth is not inherited and their wives cannot marry except after 'ta'mir' (the waiting period of 70-80 years). And in the commentary of al-'Adawi on al-Risalah: The wife of the missing person in the land of shirk and the captive's wife wait the period of ta'mir, but if their maintenance ceases, they may be divorced, especially if they fear falling into sin...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This is a fatwa from a Maliki mufti answering a question about a woman whose husband has been missing for years. The fatwa cites the well-known Maliki ruling from Umar ibn al-Khattab: wait four years, then observe iddah of four months and ten days, then she may remarry. During the four years, the wife is maintained from his wealth. After that, inheritance is delayed until proof of death or until the husband reaches an age beyond which he cannot be alive (70-80 years). For missing in the land of shirk (non-Muslim territory) or captive, the wife must wait the full ta'mir period unless maintenance stops, in which case divorce may be sought. This provides a legal stratagem for the wife.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period after dissolution of marriage, here four months and ten days for a missing husband.
مفقود (mafqud): A missing person whose whereabouts are unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Maliki fatwa, what must a wife do after waiting four years for her missing husband?
A) She may remarry immediately.
B) She must observe an iddah of four months and ten days.
C) She must seek a divorce from a judge.
D) She must wait another four years.

Key Takeaway
The Maliki ruling provides a clear path: 4 years waiting + 4 months 10 days iddah, then remarriage.

Ta'mir and the Stricter Rule for Missing in Dar al-Shirk
Maliki rule for missing in Dar al-Shirk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ta'mir and explain the stricter Maliki rule for a missing husband in Dar al-Shirk, including the exception when maintenance ceases.

Core Idea
Missing in enemy territory: wait until maximum lifespan (70-80 years) unless maintenance ceases.

The Maliki fatwa distinguishes between missing in Muslim lands and in non-Muslim territories. For the latter, the wife must wait the full ta'mir period unless her maintenance stops, in which case she may seek annulment. This lesson unpacks that distinction and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The fatwa distinguishes between missing in Dar al-Islam and missing in Dar al-Shirk (or captive). Different rules apply to each.
Dar al-Shirk includes enemy territory or captivity.
2
Define ta'mir
Ta'mir is the maximum lifespan estimate, set at 70, 75, or 80 years by Maliki scholars.
It is used as the outer limit for presuming death.
3
State the default rule
The wife of a missing captive or one in Dar al-Shirk cannot remarry until ta'mir is reached, and his wealth is not inherited.
This is stricter than the rule for Dar al-Islam.
4
Identify the exception
If the wife's maintenance ceases, she may seek divorce, especially if she fears falling into sin (zina).
The judge can grant divorce to prevent hardship.

Case of a Woman in Muslim Land Occupied by Non-Muslims
Answers how a woman can remarry when her husband is missing in occupied land with no Muslim judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hila for a woman whose husband is missing in occupied land with no Muslim judge, and identify the conditions under which a single just Muslim can issue a ruling.

Core Idea
When hardship prevents access to a judge, a single just Muslim can issue the ruling needed for remarriage.

When a Muslim woman's husband goes missing in territory overrun by non-Muslims and no Muslim judge exists, Islamic law does not leave her trapped. This lesson explores the hila (legal stratagem) derived from the Maliki text Sharh Aqrab al-Masalik, as endorsed by the Hanafi school, which allows a just and knowledgeable member of the community to act as a quasi-judge.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
The woman's husband is missing in a Muslim land that has been conquered by non-Muslims. There is no Muslim judge available. She needs to remarry but cannot proceed without a ruling.
2
Identify the solution from the text
The solution is from al-Dardir's commentary: she raises her matter to the judges (if any) or to the jama'at al-muslimeen (the general body of Muslims). If no judge, a single just and knowledgeable Muslim suffices.
This is a hila based on the qawida 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir'.
3
Note the conditions for the single person
That person must be just (adil), knowledgeable (arif), and someone to whom people refer in important matters (not just any Muslim).
The text specifies these conditions to prevent abuse.
4
Compare with the Hanbali position
The Hanbali school does not require any judge's ruling at all. This is a valid ikhtilaf. The Hanafi view uses a single person as a necessity.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi requires a ruling; Hanbali does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السوال الثالث عن مسلمة فقرت زوجها في بلاد اسلامية استولى الكافر عليها وحازها وليس هناك حاكم اسلامي كيف تحمل اذا ارادت زواجها فجوابه مافي شرح اقرب المسالك للدرديران زوجه المفقود في ارض الاسلام تعتد عدة وفاة ان رفعت امرها للحاكمات كان تم حاكم او لجماعة المسلمين عند عدمه ولو حكما قال كما في زماننا عصر اذلا حاكم فيها عربى فيكفى الواحد من جماعة المسلمين ان كان عدلك عار ناشانه ان يرجع اليه فى مهمات الامور بين الناس لا مطلق واحد وعند الحنابلة لا تفتقرا مراة المفقود الى حكم حاكم البلدة كما في كشاق القناع وشرح المنتهى للشيخ مصور الحنبلي في قول السائل وفى اى قسم للمفقود يكون هذا جوابيه انه من الفقد في بلاد الإسلام
And as for the third question about a Muslim woman whose husband she lost in an Islamic land that the non-Muslim conquered and possessed, and there is no Muslim judge there, how can she proceed if she wants to remarry? Its answer is in Sharh Aqrab al-Masalik by al-Dardir: The wife of a missing person in the land of Islam observes the widow's waiting period if she raises her matter to the judges, whether a judge, or the group of Muslims if none exists. Even if a single person rules, as he said: as in our time, an era in which there is no Arab judge, a single individual from the group of Muslims suffices if he is just, knowledgeable, and one to whom people refer in important matters, not any absolute person. And according to the Hanbalis, the wife of a missing person does not need a ruling of the town's judge, as in Kashshaf al-Qina' and Sharh al-Muntaha by Shaykh Mansur al-Hanbali. In the statement of the questioner: 'In which category of the missing person is this?' Its answer: It is from [the category of] the missing person in the land of Islam.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific hila (legal stratagem) for a Muslim woman whose husband is missing in Muslim territory that has been conquered by non-Muslims, such that no Muslim judge remains. The question is how she can lawfully remarry. The answer is taken from al-Dardir's commentary on Aqrab al-Masalik. She may observe the widow's waiting period (iddat al-wafat) after raising her matter to the available authorities. If there is a Muslim judge, she goes to him. If no judge exists, she may go to the general body of Muslims (jama'at al-muslimeen). However, in times where there is no 'Arab judge' (perhaps meaning a fully qualified judge), even a single upright Muslim who is just, knowledgeable, and is looked upon for important matters among the people suffices to give a ruling (hukm) for her case. This is a practical solution (hila) for women in such dire circumstances. The passage also notes that the Hanbali school does not require a judge's ruling at all, citing Kashshaf al-Qina' and Sharh al-Muntaha. The questioner asks which category this case falls under; the answer is that it is from the category of missing persons in the land of Islam.

Key Terms
جماعة المسلمين (jama'at al-muslimeen): The general assembly of Muslims in a locality, which can act as a quasi-judicial body in absence of a formal judge.
عدة وفاة (iddat wafat): The widow's waiting period of four months and ten days observed after the death or presumed death of a husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi-based solution for a woman whose husband is missing in Muslim land occupied by non-Muslims with no Muslim judge?
A) She must wait until the land is recaptured by Muslims.
B) She can remarry after a single just and knowledgeable Muslim issues a ruling.
C) She can remarry only after a Hanbali qadi from elsewhere comes.
D) She can remarry immediately without any waiting period.

Key Takeaway
In cases of extreme hardship, the Hanafi school allows a single just Muslim to act as a judge for a missing husband's wife, based on the qawida 'mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir'.

Wife of a Missing Husband: Madhhab Positions and Fatwa Procedure
Fatwa on the wife of a missing husband with multiple madhhab views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which the wife of a missing husband may obtain a divorce, compare the Maliki, Hanbali, and Shafi'i positions, and apply the fatwa hierarchy to determine the operative ruling.

Core Idea
The wife of a missing husband cannot remarry without judicial or communal authority, even after a waiting period.

This lesson examines a complex family law scenario: the wife of a missing husband (al-mafqud 'anha zawjaha). The source presents a question about divorce without a judge and responses from multiple madhhabs. As a mufti, you must navigate the conditions, the varying waiting periods, and the role of community leaders when no judge is available. We will parse the text to extract the operative rulings for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problem
The passage addresses two questions: Can the wife obtain a divorce without a judge? What is the waiting period? Recognize that the issue is about valid exit from marriage when the husband is missing.
This is a hila (legal stratagem) case where the wife needs practical steps to remarry.
2
List the conditions for divorce
The text mentions two triggers: lack of maintenance (nafaqa) and fear of fornication (khawf al-zina) due to absence of intimate relations. Under each, different waiting periods and procedures apply.
Distinguish between maintenance-based and intimacy-based grounds.
3
Extract the Maliki position
The Maliki school, represented in the fatwa, initially allows iddah of four years plus four months ten days without judge's order, but then requires raising the matter to a judge or community leaders. Note the apparent contradiction and the preferred view from Mudawwana.
According to the text, Malik's final view requires a judge or a righteous group of Muslims.
4
Compare with Hanbali and Shafi'i positions
Hanbalis allow immediate or delayed divorce; Shafi'is require a three-day wait and a judge's ruling. The text also mentions a one-year or six-month wait for intimacy-based fear according to some Malikis and Hanbalis.
This comparison shows the practical differences (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Determine the fatwa procedure
The fatwa from Muhammad Tayyib al-Ansari emphasizes that the wife must raise her case to a judge, governor, water officer, or congregation of upright Muslims. She cannot act alone. This establishes the procedural rule for the mufti to apply.
In the absence of a judge, the community leaders act as substitute authorities.

واله اما بعد فالجواب عن المسئلة الاولى هوما فهمتم لازلتم من اهل الفهم من المدونة ومختصر الشيخ خليل من ان المفقود عنها زوجها لانها من احد امرین اما ان ترضى المقام مع زوجها المفقود او تريد المفارقه فان The missing husband if her maintenance continues from his wealth and she does not fear sin and fornication, otherwise she may divorce due to lack of maintenance or fear of fornication? As for the sixth question: Is her divorce valid without a sharia judge and how to act? It was said to Malik: 'She observes iddah after four years, four months and ten days, the iddah of death, without the ruler ordering her?' He said: 'Yes, she has that right.' And for the ruler in the four months and ten days which is iddah? The text of Mukhtasar: 'And the wife of a missing person.' Explanation: 'He who is absent in the lands of Islam, news interrupted, and it is possible to inquire about him, she should refer to the judge, and the authorities, and the governor of the desert, and the water officer who collects zakat, and the congregation of Muslims from the righteous of her town. And she may choose not to refer and remain in his bond until his matter becomes clear. So he is given a term of four years if his maintenance is ongoing. If his maintenance is cut off, she may divorce without delay. And likewise if she fears harm to herself from the day of inability due to lack of maintenance, then the wife proves with two witnesses that so-and-so is her husband and he is absent from her and left her no maintenance nor agent for her nor anything from him, and she swears on that, then the judge says: 'I have annulled her marriage' or 'I have divorced you from him' or orders her to do so, then judges accordingly. And this is after waiting about a month and by his ijtihad according to the Malikis; immediate or delayed according to the Hanbalis; after three days according to the Shafi'is. And if it is due to her fear of fornication from lack of intercourse and care despite availability of maintenance and wealth, then after waiting a year or more according to some Malikis, and after six months according to the Hanbalis. May Allah grant us righteous deeds. The poor servant Muhammad al-Fahasham. [PAGE_207] The answer from Allama Muhammad Tayyib bin Ishaq al-Ansari, may his blessings continue, the Maliki teacher at the Prophet's Mosque, may prayers and peace be upon its owner. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah and prayers and peace upon His Messenger and his family. To proceed: The answer to the first question is what you understood, may you remain among people of understanding, from al-Mudawwana and Mukhtasar al-Shaykh Khalil, that the woman whose husband is missing is in one of two matters: either she is satisfied to remain with her missing husband, or she wants separation. If she wants it, she must raise her matter to the judge, or the governor, or the water officer, and if none exists, to the congregation of Muslims from the righteous of her town and neighbors. And as for her observing iddah and marrying another man without raising to the judge or someone who permits its legality and permissibility, due to what it contains of evident corruption. The text of al-Mudawwana: I said - meaning Abu al-Qasim - I saw the wife of a missing person observe iddah for four years according to Malik's saying without the ruler's order. He said: Malik said: No. Malik said: If she stays twenty years then raises her matter to the ruler, he considers it and writes to the place he went, and if he finds nothing from him, he sets for her from that time four years. The closest paths. And the Shafi'i books: Annulment due to lack of maintenance and the like must be by the judgment of the judge and the one being judged. And if there is no judge, a group of upright Muslims stand in his place in that and in every matter where access to the just judge is difficult. And if one of them is such that he is relied upon in important matters... May Allah do good to him in life and after death, and may Allah bless and grant peace to the owner.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents a legal problem and answer regarding the wife of a missing husband (al-mafqud 'anha zawjaha). The text begins with the question: if the wife's maintenance is provided and she does not fear sin, she may not seek divorce; but if she fears fornication or lacks maintenance, she may seek divorce. The central issue is whether she can obtain a divorce without a sharia judge, and how to proceed. The text then narrates a dialogue with Imam Malik regarding the iddah of four years and four months and ten days (iddah of death) without the ruler's order. Malik initially permits it but later seems to require the ruler's involvement. The text then outlines various madhhab positions: According to the Malikis, after waiting about a month and by ijtihad; Hanbalis allow immediate or delayed divorce; Shafi'is require a three-day wait. If the fear is due to lack of intercourse despite maintenance, Malikis require waiting a year or more, Hanbalis six months. The second part is a fatwa from the Maliki scholar Muhammad Tayyib al-Ansari, explaining the ruling from the Mudawwana and Mukhtasar Khalil. He states the wife has two options: remain or seek separation. If she wants separation, she must raise the matter to a judge, governor, or community leaders. He emphasizes that she cannot simply observe iddah and remarry without authorization, as that leads to corruption. He also mentions the Shafi'i position that annulment due to lack of maintenance requires a judge's ruling, but if no judge exists, upright Muslims can stand in. This passage is important for understanding legal stratagems (hiyal) in family law for a missing husband, particularly the conditions under which a wife can exit the marriage without a formal court.

Key Terms
المفقود عنها زوجها (al-mafqud 'anha zawjaha): A woman whose husband is missing with no known location or death confirmation.
التطليق (al-tatliq): Divorce initiated by the wife through judicial decree due to harm or absence of the husband.
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Maliki fatwa in the passage, what must the wife of a missing husband do before she can marry another man?
A) Wait four years and then remarry without any permission.
B) Raise her matter to a judge, governor, or a group of upright Muslims.
C) Obtain a fatwa from a mufti only.
D) Seek permission from her missing husband's family.

Key Takeaway
The wife of a missing husband must seek dissolution through a legitimate authority; independent remarriage is invalid and sinful.
