Waiting Period for the Wife of a Missing Husband in Occupied Lands
Hila ruling for missing husband in colonized lands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the waiting period for a woman whose husband is missing in occupied Muslim lands and distinguish between the two categories of missing persons.

Core Idea
A missing husband in occupied lands with Muslim authorities is treated as missing in Islamic lands: wait 4 years, not indefinitely.

This passage addresses a critical issue faced by Muslim women in territories that have fallen under non-Muslim control, such as Egypt and Syria during colonial times. The Hanafi school provides a specific waiting period of four years followed by the iddah of death (four months ten days), rather than requiring the woman to wait indefinitely. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between two categories of missing persons and the role of Muslim judicial presence in the land.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of the missing (mafqud)
The text divides the missing into: (1) one whose news is cut off but investigation is possible, and (2) one lost in enemy territory where investigation is impossible. Determine which category applies to the woman's husband in an occupied land.
The first category includes those missing in lands with Muslim judges and governors.
2
Determine the applicable waiting period
For a woman whose husband falls into the first category (possible investigation), she waits four years, then observes the iddah of death (four months ten days). This is a legal stratagem (hila) to prevent indefinite waiting.
She does not wait muddah al-ta'mir (the period after which a missing person is presumed dead).
3
Distinguish occupied lands from pure war zones
Even if the land is under non-Muslim rule, if Muslim judges and authorities exist and investigation is possible, it is treated as Islamic lands. If the land is a war zone (dar al-harb) where Muslims cannot enter and investigation is impossible, different rules apply (including ransom by the imam).
The term 'polytheistic lands' in the text refers specifically to war zones, not all non-Muslim lands.
4
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a Muslim woman in a territory that was colonized but retained Islamic courts (e.g., parts of British India). She waits four years, then performs iddat al-wafat. If the territory had no Muslim judges and was inaccessible, the imam would ransom her.
This ruling is based on the possibility of investigation, not the political ruler's religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اما المسئلة الأولى والثانية نجربهما والله اعلم ان المرأة المسلمة التي فقدت زوجها في بلاد استرات عليها الكفار مدة مديدة كما في مصر والشام وبقية الامصار تعتد اربع سنين ثم تعتد عدة الوفاة اربعة اشهر وعشرا وزوجها يكون في عداد القسم الاول من اقسام المفقو لا نهم عرفوه باب من غاب وانقطع خبره وامكن الكشف عنه وعرفوا القسم الثانى وهو المفقود فى ارض الحرب بارض خاب و انقطع خيره ولم يمكن الكشف عنه لانه فقد في ارض الحرب فالبلاد المذكورة وان كان حاکمھا كانوا لا تكون كارض الحرب من كل وجه لوجود قضاة المسلمين فيها وولاتهم وامكان الكشف فاتضح بهذا ان حكمها حكم من فقدت زوجها ببلاد الاسلام فلا تنتظر مدة التعمير فلا تختص الصورة الثانية المذكورة في المختصر بالمسلمة الكائنة في بلاد الاسلام بل تشمل من كانت فى البلاء المستعمرة الكفارات المراد بالشركية البلاد الحربية التي لا يمكن المسلم الوصول اليهاوره تتمكن القضاة من التفتيش فيها لا مطلق البلاد الكفرية لانها ربما تكون سلمية أو زعية وأما القاطنة في البلاد الشركية العربية فحكمها هي وزوجها حكم المسليين فيفديهما الامام من بيت المال ان كان والا فمن ماله بالغا ما بلغ والا فعلى جميع المسلمين.
As for the first and second issues, we will try them, and Allah knows best. Indeed, the Muslim woman whose husband has been lost in lands over which the disbelievers have taken control for a long period, as in Egypt, Syria, and other regions, performs iddah for four years, then performs the iddah of death: four months and ten days. Her husband is counted among the first category of the missing, because they defined it as someone who disappeared and his news was cut off, and investigation about him was possible. They defined the second category as the one lost in the land of war, in a hostile territory, and his news was cut off and investigation about him was not possible, because he was lost in the land of war. The aforementioned lands, even if their rulers were [non-Muslims], are not like the land of war in every respect, due to the presence of Muslim judges and governors and the possibility of investigation. So it becomes clear that her ruling is the ruling of one whose husband was lost in the lands of Islam. So she does not wait for the period of ta'mir. So the second scenario mentioned in al-Mukhtasar is not specific to the Muslim woman living in the lands of Islam; rather it includes those who were in the colonized lands [؟]. The intent by 'polytheistic lands' is the war lands that a Muslim cannot reach and the judges cannot investigate in them, not all disbelieving lands, because they might be peaceful or [؟]. As for the woman residing in the Arab polytheistic lands, her and her husband's ruling is the ruling of Muslims. The imam ransoms them from the treasury if it exists, otherwise from his own wealth, whatever the amount; otherwise, it is upon all Muslims.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for the first two issues concerning a Muslim woman whose husband has gone missing in territories that have fallen under non-Muslim control. The text classifies the missing person into two categories: the first is someone who disappeared with possible investigation, and the second is one lost in enemy territory with no possibility of investigation. The woman in an occupied land like Egypt or Syria is treated as if her husband is lost in Islamic lands, so she must wait four years and then observe the iddah of death. She does not wait indefinitely (muddah al-ta'mir). The author clarifies that this ruling applies even if the land is under non-Muslim rule as long as Muslim courts and authorities exist, making investigation possible. The scenario of the wife of a missing husband in a polytheistic war zone where Muslims cannot enter is different, and the imam must ransom them from the treasury.

Key Terms
المفقود (al-mafqud): A person whose whereabouts are unknown and whose news has been cut off.
عدة الوفاة (iddat al-wafat): The waiting period after the husband's death: four months and ten days.
مدة التعمير (muddah al-ta'mir): The period after which a missing person is presumed dead, typically 9 years in some schools, but in this context, the Hanafi ruling for the first category replaces it with 4 years.
البلاد الشركية الحربية (al-bilad al-shirkiyyah al-harbiyyah): Polytheistic war lands: territories under hostile non-Muslim control where Muslims cannot enter and Muslim judges cannot investigate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a woman whose husband is missing in lands with Muslim judicial presence to remarry after waiting 4 years and then fulfilling the iddah of death, preventing indefinite waiting.

Maliki Hila: Returning to First Husband After a Second Marriage
Stating Maliki rulings for two subcases of a remarried woman returning to her first husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a Maliki hila that returns a remarried woman to her first husband, and apply these conditions to evaluate similar cases.

Core Idea
Second marriage does not dissolve the first if the divorce was based on false information.

This passage from Thanwi's work presents two Maliki subcases where a woman, after remarrying due to a defective separation, is returned to her first husband. The rulings function as a legal stratagem (hila) to preserve the original marriage, provided specific conditions are met. Understanding these conditions helps a mufti recognize when a second marriage can be annulled without a new contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two subcases
First, the woman divorced for non-maintenance who later learns maintenance was provided. Second, the woman who remarries on the basis of a death report from non-just witnesses, then the husband returns.
Both involve a first husband who reappears after she has remarried.
2
Extract the triggering condition
For the first subcase, the condition is that the woman dropped her claim (isqat) after proof that maintenance was sent or left with her. For the second, the death report must not be from two just witnesses.
The key is that the divorce or remarriage was based on faulty information.
3
Determine the consequence
In both subcases, she is returned to the first husband without a new marriage contract or dower, but she must observe istibra' (three menses, or pregnancy, or three months).
The second marriage is not considered valid for dissolving the first.
4
Recognize the hila element
The ruling allows the woman to return to the first husband even after the second marriage, provided the conditions are met. This is a hila to preserve the original marriage and avoid the need for a new contract.
The second husband pays the dower and lineage of any children is attributed to him.
5
Contrast with Hanafi position
In the Hanafi school, a valid second marriage would dissolve the first completely. This Maliki ruling is a specific exception based on the hila principle.
Understanding the madhhab difference is crucial for comparative fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما المثلة الثالثة فالحكم عند المالكية كما ذكرتم انها ترد إلى زوجها الأول فاما الغائب المطلق عليه بعدم النفقة فقال عبد الباقي على مختصر خليل والمطلقة لعدم النفقة تتنروج ويدخل بها ثم ظهر اسقاطهاعي المطلق عليه بان اقام بنية انه كان يرسلها اليها وانها وصلتها اوانه تركها عندها فلا يفتيها دخول الثاني واما المنعى لها زوجها bo فقال عبد الباقي ايضا اذا اخبرت من غير عدلين بموته فاعتملات و اعتدت و تزوجت ثم قدم فلا تفوت عليه بدخول الثاني ولو ولدت منه اولاد اسواء جگريه الحاكم ام رو على المشهور وترد اليه في الصورتين من غير تجديد عقد ولا مهر و يجب عليها الاستبراء بثلاث حيض ان كانت ممن يحیض اور ضع حمل ان كانت حاملا او ثلاثة اشهران كانت صغيرة او ايستو يجب على الثاني جميع الصداق المسح ان كان والا نصداق المثل القول الشيخ خليل رو تقرر بوطأ وان حرم ) قال الدرديرو تقرى جميع الصداق الشرعى السمى وصداق المثل في التفويض بوطا المطيقة من بالغ وان حرم ذلك الوطأ و يلحق نسب الاولاد بالثانى وهذا مها لا خلاف فيه في مذهب المالكية
As for the third issue, the ruling according to the Malikis is as you mentioned: she is returned to her first husband. Regarding the absentee who is ruled against for lack of maintenance, Abd al-Baqi said in his commentary on Mukhtasar Khalil: 'The woman divorced for non-maintenance marries and he (the second husband) enters her, then it appears that she dropped the claim against the absentee by him (the absentee) proving that he was sending it to her and she received it, or that he left it with her, then the entry of the second does not make her forbidden to the first.' And regarding the one whose husband's death is reported to her, Abd al-Baqi also said: 'When she is informed of his death by someone other than two just witnesses, so she performs iddah and marries, then the (first) husband arrives, then the entry of the second does not invalidate her marriage to the first, even if she gives birth to children from him, whether the judge executed it or not according to the well-known opinion. And she is returned to him in both cases without renewing the contract or dower. And she must perform istibra' with three menses if she menstruates, or with a pregnancy if she is pregnant, or three months if she is a minor or menopausal. The second is liable for the full dower agreed upon if one was set, otherwise the dower of the like.' Sheikh Khalil said: 'It is determined by intercourse, even if forbidden.' Al-Dardir said: 'She determines the full specified sharia dower, and the dower of the like in a delegation [of marriage] by intercourse, and the divorced woman (is) an adult, even if that intercourse is forbidden. The lineage of the children is established to the second. And there is no disagreement on this in the Maliki school.'
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents the Maliki rulings for two subcases within the third issue. The first subcase: a woman divorced for lack of maintenance remarries, but if it later becomes clear that the husband was actually providing maintenance or had left it with her, the second marriage does not dissolve the first. The second subcase: a woman informed of her husband's death by unreliable sources performs iddah and remarries; if the first husband returns, she is returned to him without a new contract or dower, provided she observes istibra'. The second husband must pay the dower, and lineage of children from the second marriage is attributed to him. The text quotes Abd al-Baqi, Khalil, and Dardir, confirming this as the Maliki position.

Key Terms
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): A waiting period to ensure the womb is free from pregnancy before remarriage or return.
المطلق عليه (al-mutlaq 'alayhi): The person ruled against, here the husband who failed to provide maintenance.
الحيلة (al-hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding a prohibition or difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Maliki hila allows a woman to return to her first husband after a faulty second marriage, provided she observes istibra' and the second husband pays the dower.

Maliki Ruling on the Missing Husband's Divorce as a Hila
Maliki ruling on missing husband's divorce conditioned on second marriage consummation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki ruling on the missing husband's divorce, explain the condition of the second husband's entry, and evaluate its use as a legal stratagem (hila) in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
The missing husband's divorce is confirmed only upon the second husband's entry — a conditional ruling with strategic application.

In this passage, the Hanafi scholar Ashraf Ali Thanwi presents the Maliki position on a delicate marital issue: when a husband is missing and his divorce is pronounced, its validity hinges on the wife's subsequent marriage and consummation. This ruling, though Maliki, offers a potential hila (legal stratagem) that a Hanafi mufti may consider in issuing fatwa. Understanding the precise condition — actual entry or valid seclusion — is crucial for accurate application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The fourth issue (al-mas'ala al-rabi'a) concerning the missing husband (mafqud) and the effect of a second marriage.
2
State the Maliki ruling per Dardir
The divorce takes effect only upon the second husband's entry (dukhul).
3
Understand the condition of entry
If the first husband returns before entry, he retains rights; after entry, divorce is confirmed and she is separated from the first.
4
Contrast with the insolvent husband case
For a missing husband who is insolvent or fails to pay maintenance, the ruling differs; entry does not separate her.
5
Recognize the hila potential
How this Maliki ruling can be used as a hila in Hanafi iftaa: by having the wife marry another, consummate, then the first marriage dissolves permanently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما المسئلة الرابعة فقال الدردير رحمة الله تعالی و قدر طلاق من المفقود حسين الشروع في العدة يفتيها عليه يتحقق وقوعه بدخول الزوج الثاني عليها حتى لو جاء الأول قبل دخول الثاني كان احق بها وبعد الدخول بانت من الاول وتاخذ منه جميع المهروان لم يكن قد دخل بها فلم ينض الاعلى امرأة المفقود واما المعسر القائم، والمطلق عليه بعدم النفقة فلا يفتيها دخول الثاني ولو ولدت منه اولاد اكما تقدم ذكره في المسئلة الثالثة واذا اختلى بها خلوة اهتداء فقد دخل بها وقال
As for the fourth issue, Al-Dardir, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The divorce of the missing person, [؟] commencing the iddah, is issued against her. Its occurrence is confirmed by the entry of the second husband upon her. So if the first husband comes before the entry of the second, he has more right to her. After entry, she becomes separated from the first and takes all the dower from him (the one who entered). If he had not entered her, then [؟] pertains only to the wife of the missing person. As for the insolvent who is established [as such], and the one ruled against for lack of maintenance, the entry of the second does not make her forbidden [to the first], even if she gives birth to children from him, as was mentioned in the third issue. And if he secludes himself with her in a [valid] seclusion, then he has entered her.' And he said: ...
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage gives the Maliki ruling for the fourth issue regarding the missing husband's divorce. According to Dardir, the divorce pronounced by the missing husband (or on his behalf) becomes effective only when the second husband actually consummates the marriage with the wife. If the first husband returns before consummation, he retains his right to her. After consummation, she is irrevocably separated from the first and must receive the full dower from the second. This ruling is contrasted with the case of an insolvent or non-maintaining husband: their divorce does not become effective upon the second husband's entry, as previously stated. The text also notes that valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) is equivalent to actual intercourse for this purpose.

Key Terms
الخلوة الصحيحة (al-khalwa al-sahiha): A valid seclusion between a married couple where no legal impediment prevents intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Maliki ruling in this passage, what condition must be met for the missing husband's divorce to be confirmed?
A) The first husband fails to return within one year
B) The wife observes iddah completely
C) The second husband enters or has valid seclusion
D) The qadi issues a final decree

Key Takeaway
The Maliki condition for the missing husband's divorce to take effect is actual entry or valid seclusion by the second husband — a ruling that serves as a hila in Hanafi fatwa.

The Prohibition of Talfiq and Madhhab Consistency in Fatwa
Fatwa on talfiq and community deputization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify talfiq and explain why a mufti must issue fatwa according to a single madhhab without mixing rulings.

Core Idea
Talfiq is forbidden by consensus — a fatwa must follow a coherent madhhab without patching.

This lesson addresses a critical principle in ifta': the prohibition of talfiq. The source passage warns that when the Muslim community acts in place of a judge, their decisions must be according to their own madhhab, because combining rulings from different schools to produce a new ruling not recognized by any is forbidden. Understanding this principle is essential for avoiding invalid fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of talfiq
The fatwa is responding to a question about the mafqud case where the Hanafi school's procedure might be mixed with Maliki rules. Note that the author insists on consistency.
2
Define talfiq and its prohibition
Talfiq is the act of combining rulings from different madhhabs in a way that results in a ruling not accepted by any single madhhab. The passage states it is haram bi al-ittifaq (forbidden by consensus).
This applies even if each component ruling is valid in its own school.
3
Apply the principle to the mafqud case
The Hanafi query wanted to use the Maliki rule of community authorization while possibly retaining Hanafi rulings. The Maliki scholar rejects this as talfiq.
A mufti must consistently follow one madhhab throughout a case.
4
Recognize the practical implication
If a mufti issues a fatwa mixing madhhabs without proper taqlid, the fatwa is invalid. The mufti must either give the ruling of his own school or switch madhhab entirely for that case, but not mix.
Talfiq differs from takhayyur (selecting from multiple schools) which is permissible under certain conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في حاشية العدوى على مجموع الامير عند قوله وقدر طلاق يتحقق عند دخول الثانی ای خلوته بهاران انكر التلذذ بها لان الخلوة مظنة وقائمة مقامها كما في التوضيح - واما المسئلة الخامسة فالجواب ان المسائل التي تنوب فيها جماعة المسلمين عن القاضي كثيرة ومنها مسئلة المفقود فان امرأته لابد لها من احد امرين اما ان ترضى المقام مع زوجها المفقود او تريد المفارقة فان ارادتها فلابد لها من رفع امرها اما الى القاضي او الوالي او والى الماء وان لم يوجد فالى جماعة المسلمين من صالحي بلدها وجيرانها واما انها تعتد و تتزوج برجل اخر من غير رفع امرها الى القاضي فلا قائل بحليته وجوازه لما فيه من الفساد - واما المسئلة السادسة فجوابها ان القضايا التي يرجع فيها الى جماعة المسلمين يجب ان تكون موافقة لمذهبهم لان التلفيق حرام باتفاق والله سبحانه وتعالى اعلم امريكانت محمد الطيب بن اسحق الانصاري المدني خادم العلم في المسجد البدرى الجواب من العلامة الصالح التونسي المالكي المدرس بالمسجد الشريقي بالمدينة المنورة بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله والصلوة والسلام على رسول الله وعلى اله وصحبه ومن والاه وبعد فقد وردت على مسئلة متفرعة عن مسئلة المفقود وهي هذه - (1) ازاردت زوجة المفقود ونحوة إلى الزوج الاول بعد دخول الثاني فهل يجدد الاول النكاح ام لا (۲) وهل يجدد لها المهر ام لا (۳) وهل تجب عليها العدة للزوج الثاني اولا وكم عدتها (۳) وهل لها المهر على الثاني اولا (۵) نسب اولادها من الثاني بمن يلحق و (4) هل الخلوة الصحيحة المعتبر بها العدة ونحوها تقوم مقام الدخول لله القضايا التي يكون المرجع فيها و نظرها الى القاضي فان عدم حسا او اعتبار فجماعة المسلمين فهل يكون تلفيفا ممنوعا ان كان اصلها على المذهب الحنفى واريد جعل النظر فيها الجماعة المسلمين على المقرر عند المالكية بشرط المذكور الجواب بعون الله على المذهب المالكي حسب المقرر والمحرر في كتبهم المتداولة المعمول بها في الحكم و الفتوى . فعلى السئلة الاولى ان رجوع الزوجها الأول بعد دخول الثاني لاي متاج لتجديد النكاح وعلى الثالى انه لا مهر لها من جديد - وعلى الثالث وجوب العدة وتسمى استبراء وهو ثلاث حيض - وعلى الرابع بوجوب المهر كاملا لها على الثاني للقاعدة المجمع عليها وهو تكميل بالوطاً. و على الخامس يلحق نسب اولادها من الثاني به القاعدة وان كلما سقط الحد لحق الوليد .
In the marginalia of al-‘Adawi on Majmu‘ al-Amir at his statement: 'And the extent of talaq is realized upon the entry of the second [husband]', i.e., his seclusion with her, even if he denies taking pleasure with her, because seclusion is a presumption and stands in its place as in al-Tawdih. As for the fifth issue, the answer is that matters in which the Muslim community deputizes for the judge are many, among them the issue of the missing husband. For his wife must have one of two things: either she is content to remain with her missing husband, or she desires separation. If she desires it, she must raise her case to the judge, or the governor, or the water authority, and if none exists, then to the Muslim community from among the righteous of her town and neighbors. As for her observing the waiting period and marrying another man without raising her case to the judge, there is no one who says it is permissible because of the corruption involved. As for the sixth issue, the answer is that matters referred to the Muslim community must be in accordance with their madhhab, because talfiq is forbidden by consensus. And Allah, exalted, knows best. [Signed] Muhammad al-Tayyib ibn Ishaq al-Ansari al-Madani, servant of knowledge in the Badri Mosque. The answer from the righteous scholar al-Tunisi al-Maliki, teacher in the Sharqi Mosque in Medina. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, and blessings and peace be upon the Messenger of Allah and his family and companions and those who support him. To proceed: A question derived from the issue of the missing husband was presented to me, and it is this: (1) If the wife of the missing husband returns to the first husband after the second has entered, does the first renew the marriage or not? (2) Does he renew the dowry for her or not? (3) Is the waiting period obligatory for her from the second husband or not, and what is its amount? (4) Does she have the dowry from the second or not? (5) To whom is the lineage of her children from the second attributed? And (6) Does a valid seclusion that necessitates the waiting period and the like serve as actual consummation? In matters whose reference and consideration belong to the judge, and if he is absent or not considered, then the Muslim community – would that be a prohibited talfiq if the origin is according to the Hanafi school and it is intended to place the consideration with the Muslim community according to what is established with the Malikis under the mentioned condition? The answer, with the help of Allah, according to the Maliki school as established and recorded in their books used in judgments and fatwas: Regarding the first question, the return of her first husband after the second's entry does not require renewal of the marriage. Regarding the second, she has no new dowry. Regarding the third, the waiting period is obligatory, called istibra', which is three menstrual periods. Regarding the fourth, the full dowry is obligatory for her from the second due to the agreed-upon principle that it is completed by intercourse. Regarding the fifth, the lineage of her children from the second is attributed to him due to the principle: whenever the hadd punishment is waived, the child follows.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a fatwa from a Maliki scholar responding to six sub-questions arising from the classical issue of the missing husband (mafqud). The fatwa is given in the context of a Hanafi concern about talfiq (patchworking of madhhabs). The author first notes that matters where the Muslim community acts in place of a judge must be in accordance with their own madhhab, as talfiq is forbidden by consensus. The fatwa then proceeds with Maliki rulings: (1) If the wife of a missing husband remarries and the second husband consummates the marriage, then the first husband returns, the original marriage is not revived and there is no need to renew the nikah; (2) No new mahr is due from the first husband; (3) The wife must observe an istibra' waiting period of three menstrual cycles from the second husband; (4) She is entitled to the full mahr from the second husband because consummation completes it; (5) The children born from the second husband are attributed to him, based on the maxim 'whenever the hadd punishment is dropped, the child is attributed' (i.e., when there is no possibility of legal punishment for zina, the child is considered legitimate). The fatwa does not explicitly answer the sixth question about whether valid seclusion equals actual consummation in all respects, but the context implies that in Maliki law, valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) does indeed trigger the same consequences as actual intercourse regarding 'iddah and lineage.

Key Terms
المفقود (al-mafqud): A husband who has disappeared and whose location and status (alive/dead) are unknown.
التلفيق (al-talfiq): Combining rulings from multiple madhhabs within a single case to produce a ruling not recognized by any single school.
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): A waiting period (usually three menstrual cycles) to verify that the womb is empty of pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa, why must matters referred to the Muslim community be in accordance with their madhhab?
A) Because each community has its own local customs.
B) Because talfiq is forbidden by consensus.
C) Because the judge is absent, so they must use their own reasoning.
D) Because the Hanafi school requires it.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is forbidden by consensus; a mufti must issue a fatwa consistently within a single madhhab without mixing rulings from other schools.

Maliki Rulings on the Mafqud Wife's Remarriage: Sub-questions Answered
Maliki fatwa on specific sub-questions of the mafqud case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki answers to the six sub-questions of the mafqud case and apply the underlying principles (e.g., 'sqt al-hadd yalhaq al-walid').

Core Idea
The Maliki school upholds the original marriage upon the first husband's return, and children from the second husband are attributed to him.

This lesson unpacks the specific Maliki fatwa addressing six sub-questions arising from the mafqud case. The fatwa provides clear rulings on renewal of nikah, dowry, 'iddah, and lineage. Understanding these answers helps students see the practical consequences of the prohibition of talfiq and the internal consistency of a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six sub-questions
Read the passage to list the six questions: (1) renewal of nikah, (2) new mahr, (3) 'iddah from second, (4) mahr from second, (5) lineage of children, (6) valid seclusion as consummation.
The fatwa answers them in order.
2
Extract the Maliki ruling for each question
From the fatwa, note the answers: (1) no renewal, (2) no new mahr, (3) istibra' 3 hayd, (4) full mahr from second, (5) children attributed to second, (6) implied: valid seclusion equals consummation.
Use the source translation.
3
Understand the maxim for lineage
The fatwa cites 'wa kullama saqata al-hadd lahiqa al-walid' (whenever the hadd punishment is dropped, the child is attributed). This means that if the marriage is considered valid such that no hadd for zina applies, the child is legitimate.
This maxim is from the Maliki school.
4
Relate the rulings to the prohibition of talfiq
The fatwa's Maliki answers are consistent and avoid talfiq. The Hanafi concern was whether using Maliki community authorization while retaining Hanafi rules would be talfiq. The fatwa affirms that if you follow Maliki, do so completely.

Fatwa on Madhhab Conditions for Separation in Permanent Insanity
A fatwa query about which madhhab's conditions to apply for separation due to permanent insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih when choosing conditions from different madhhabs in a fatwa regarding permanent insanity.

Core Idea
When the cause is agreed but conditions differ, the mufti applies the school whose conditions are operative in his context.

This passage presents a real fatwa query: the cause of separation (permanent insanity) is unanimously accepted, but the Maliki school requires a one-year waiting period while the Hanafi school (following Imam Muhammad) mandates immediate separation. A mufti must decide which set of conditions to follow. This lesson trains you to identify the key factors that determine such a choice, including the authority of the transmitted opinion and the practical consequences for the community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed cause
First, confirm that the cause for separation (permanent insanity) is agreed upon by all schools. This is the starting point.
The question states 'al-amr alladhi yujibu al-tafriq bil-ittifaq' – the matter that obligates separation by agreement.
2
Extract the differing conditions
List the specific condition each school requires. Malikis: a one-year wait. Hanafis: no delay, immediate separation.
The text says 'inda al-malikiyyah yurjallu sahibuhu sanah' and 'akhadha sadatuna al-hanafiyyah bi-qawl Muhammad… la yu'ajjal bal yufarraq fi al-hal'.
3
Assess the authority of the Hanafi position
Determine the weight of the Hanafi view (Imam Muhammad's statement) within the school. Is it mufta bihi? Is it from Zahir al-Riwayah?
The passage indicates that the Hanafis adopted the statement of Muhammad al-Shaybani, implying it is a relied-upon position.
4
Consider the context of the community
Analyze whether the Muslim community is bound to follow a particular madhhab or can choose based on maslahah. The question asks whether they 'must observe Maliki conditions or be content with Hanafi conditions.'
This is a key iftaa consideration: the mufti must decide based on prevailing school in the community or other factors.
5
Formulate the fatwa response
Based on the analysis, determine which conditions to apply and justify the choice using Hanafi usul al-iftaa principles.
The passage ends with a request for a fatwa; the lesson does not provide the answer but trains the student to think through the process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) السوال الثالث الامر الذي يوجب التفريق بالاتفاق، ولكن كانت شرائطه مختلفا فيها مثلا اذا كان الجنون مطبقا فعند المالكية يرجل صاحبه سنة كماذا كان ذا اناقة واخذ ساداتنا الحنفية بقول محمد ان المجنون اذا كان مطبة الا يؤحل بل يفرق في الحمال كالجب فهل يحب على جماعة المسلمين أن يراعوا الشرائط المعتبرة عند المالكية اهم يجون الاكتفاء بالشرائط المرعية عند الحنفية افيضوا علينا متع الله الفتبين بطول بنائكم الفتوى من العلامة محمد بن على البيضاوي المالكى منع الله المقتبسين بعلومهم
(3) The third question: The matter that obligates separation by agreement, but its conditions are differed upon. For example, if madness is continuous, according to the Malikiyyah they wait for its [the person's] condition for a year, [and] according to our Hanafi masters they adopted the statement of Muhammad [al-Shaybani] that the permanently insane person is not given a delay, but rather separation occurs immediately like [؟]. So is it required for the community of Muslims to observe the conditions considered by the Malikiyyah, or can they be satisfied with the conditions followed by the Hanafiyyah? Expound for us—may Allah grant the muftis enjoyment through your lengthy bounties—with a fatwa from the scholar Muhammad ibn Ali al-Baydawi al-Maliki, may Allah benefit those who seek benefits from their knowledge.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents a fatwa question to a Maliki scholar: For a cause that unanimously requires separation (such as permanent insanity), but the conditions differ between the Maliki and Hanafi schools, which set of conditions should a Muslim community council follow? The Malikis require a one-year waiting period for the insane person, while the Hanafis (following Imam Muhammad) hold that immediate separation is necessary without any delay. The questioner is asking for a binding fatwa on this matter. The passage does not include the answer; it is a request for a fatwa from the specified scholar.

Key Terms
مطبق (muṭbiq): Continuous and permanent insanity (without lucid intervals).
شرائط (shara'iṭ): Conditions that must be fulfilled for the legal ruling to apply.
تفريق (tafrīq): Judicial separation or divorce between spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main issue in the third question?
A) Whether madness is a valid cause for separation.
B) Whether the community must follow Maliki or Hanafi conditions for separation due to permanent insanity.
C) Whether Muhammad al-Shaybani agreed with the Malikis.
D) Whether a wife can self-divorce.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must determine which madhhab's conditions to apply in a cross-madhhab dispute, considering the agreed cause, the authority of the opinions, and the context of the community.

Talfiq vs. Tattabu' al-Rukhas: Using Maliki Rulings in Hanafi Fatwa
Copy of a Maliki scholar's fatwa on missing husband and wife's self-divorce, with discussion of talfiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on talfiq to determine when a Hanafi council may issue a separation based on the Maliki school.

Core Idea
Talfiq across madhhabs is permissible, but following licenses (tattabu' al-rukhas) is forbidden, especially in family law.

This passage presents a Maliki fatwa outlining the wife's right to divorce after one month of a husband's disappearance, then addresses the permissibility of Hanafi judges adopting this ruling through talfiq. Understanding the distinction between valid talfiq and forbidden tattabu' al-rukhas is crucial for muftis navigating fiqh al-nawazil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maliki ruling on the wife's self-divorce
Extract the conditions: one-month wait, oath, witness, no maintenance from relative or stranger.
This ruling is context for the cross-madhab discussion.
2
Identify the rasm al-mufti principle
The passage states talfiq is permissible (al-sahih) but tattabu' al-rukhas is forbidden. Locate the qawida in the text.
The qawida governs when a Hanafi may use a Maliki ruling.
3
Apply the qawida to the scenario
Suppose a Hanafi community council rules by taqlid of the Maliki school to separate a couple. Determine if this is talfiq or tattabu' al-rukhas.
Talfiq here is permissible because they are adopting a legitimate school ruling wholesale, not picking and choosing licenses.
4
Distinguish talfiq from tattabu' al-rukhas
Talfiq: combining rulings from different madhhabs on the same issue without cherry-picking easy options. Tattabu' al-rukhas: following every license in each issue arbitrarily.
The passage emphasizes the prohibition in matters of al-furuj (lineage and private parts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رصورة ما كتبه العلامة في ضمت الجواب عن السؤال الأول) دقيل ذكر صور الاربع اذكر لكم مقدمة فيها مسائل ، منها تعريف المفقود وهو الذى انقطع خيره ممكن الكشف عنه ومنها أن كل من ليس له مال تنفق منه زوجة من اسيرا و مفتود با قسامه الاربعة الاتية نتكم حكم المعسر الغائب الذى لم يترك لزوجة نفقة فتأجل شهر او تحلف وتطلق نفسها كما في شرح التخنة للشيخ على بن عبد السلام التسولى بهذا الشهر الذي توجلد يكون بعد اتيانها صفية تشهد لها بان زوجها غاب عنها قبل البناء أو بعده بموضع كذا اولا يعلمون موضعه واليه غاب منذ كذا ولا يعلمونه ترك لها نفقة ولا كسوة ولا شيئا تمون به نفسها ولا ما تعدى فيه ولا انه أب اليها ولا يعت بشتى ورد عليها في علمهم إلى حين تاريخه كما في التسولى المذكور ثم انها كونها تطلق بعد ثبوت ما ذكر و اليمين اذالم ينتظر قریب او اجنبي بنفقتها والا فليس لها ان تطلق نفسها على المعتمد لون سبب الفراق وهو عدم النفقة قد زال كما في التسولي. المسئلة الثانية اعلم وقفنى الله واياك ان المالكية لا يرون الحكم على زوجين بالتفريق لان مذهبهم خلاف ذلك ولا يا مرون الحنفية بالحكم بالتفريق لان الأمر فى ذلك خلاف مذهبهم نعم اذا اراد جماعة الحنفية الحكم بذلك تقليد المالكية في حكم جماعة المسلمين فتكون المسئلة عندهم من باب التلفيق وهو جائز على الصحيح وينبنى عدم ارتكابه فى الفروج بخلان تتبع الرخص فلا يجوز كما يأتى ففى الشبر خيطى انه يمتنع تتبع رخص المذاهب
A copy of what the scholar wrote in the answer to the first question: He said: Mention the four forms [of missing persons]. I mention for you a preface containing issues, including the definition of the missing person: he is the one whose news is cut off but it is possible to investigate. And also that everyone who does not have wealth from which the wife can be maintained, [the wife] of a prisoner or a missing person according to his four divisions that follow, [so] the ruling of the insolent absent person who has not left maintenance for his wife: she waits one month or takes an oath and divorces herself as in Sharh al-Tuhfah by al-Shaykh Ali ibn Abd al-Salam al-Tusuli. With this month that has been determined, it is after she presents a witness statement that testifies for her that her husband was absent from her before or after consummation in such a place, and they do not know his location, and that he has been absent since such and such, and they do not know that he left for her maintenance or clothing or anything with which she can support herself, nor that he delegated [someone for that], nor that he ever came to her, nor that he sent anything to her in their knowledge up to the date of the statement—as in the aforementioned al-Tusuli. Then that she divorces herself after establishing what was mentioned and the oath, as long as no relative or stranger steps forward to provide her maintenance. Otherwise, she does not have the right to divorce herself on the relied-upon opinion, because the cause of separation—i.e., lack of maintenance—has been removed, as in al-Tusuli. The second issue: Know—may Allah grant me and you success—that the Malikiyyah do not see ruling for the separation of a couple because their madhhab is contrary to that, nor do they order the Hanafiyyah to rule for separation, because the matter is contrary to their madhhab. Yes, if a group of Hanafis want to rule by that, taqlid of the Malikiyyah in the ruling of the Muslim community, then the issue is from the category of talfiq, and it is permissible according to the correct opinion. It is built upon the prohibition of practicing it in matters of private parts/lineage, contrary to following licenses (tattabu' al-rukhas), which is not permissible, as will come. For in al-Shubra Khitayri, it is stated that it is forbidden to follow licenses of the schools.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a copy of a Maliki scholar's written response to the first question. It first defines a 'missing person' (mafqud) as someone whose whereabouts are unknown but searchable. It then discusses the ruling for a wife whose husband is absent and insolvent (no maintenance left). According to the Maliki school, after one month and upon swearing an oath, she may divorce herself if no one provides for her. Conditions for this self-divorce include witnesses to his absence and lack of support. If maintenance is provided by a relative or stranger, she cannot divorce herself. The second part addresses the earlier question: Malikis do not rule for separation because it's against their madhhab, nor do they order Hanafis to do so. However, if a Hanafi community council rules by taqlid of the Maliki school in their collective judgment, that is talfiq and is permissible on the correct view—provided it does not involve unrestricted license-following (tattabu' al-rukhas), which is forbidden in family law (al-furuj). The scholar cites al-Shubra Khitayri on this prohibition.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqūd): A person whose news is cut off but it is possible to investigate his whereabouts.
تتبع الرخص (tattabu' al-rukhaṣ): Following the licenses of various madhhabs in a single case arbitrarily, without valid reason.
تلفيق (talfīq): Adopting the ruling of another madhhab in its entirety for a specific case, without mixing elements from different schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida in the passage, when is talfiq not permissible?
A) When it is done in matters of worship (ibadat).
B) When it involves matters of private parts/lineage (al-furuj) without proper caution.
C) When it is done by a judge, not a mufti.
D) When the two madhhabs involved are Hanafi and Maliki.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is permissible when adopting a whole school's ruling, but tattabu' al-rukhas (following arbitrary licenses) is forbidden, especially in family law matters.

The Muslim Community as Judge for Dissolving Marriages of Missing Husbands
A query to Maliki scholars about the community acting as judge for dissolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which the Muslim community can substitute for a judge in dissolving a missing husband's marriage, and evaluate the procedural questions raised in the Hanafi-Maliki discourse.

Core Idea
The community can dissolve a marriage only when no judge exists and only for missing husbands — but the manner of judgment is disputed.

The problem of the missing husband's wife is a longstanding fiqh dilemma. Hanafis adopted a Maliki legal stratagem (hila) allowing the Muslim community to act as a judge to dissolve the marriage when no qualified judge is present. However, this hila raises procedural questions: does the community judge collectively or delegate? Is collective judgment valid? This lesson examines the conditions and the queries posed to Maliki scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core hila
What legal problem does this hila solve? It addresses the situation of a wife whose husband is missing and no judge is available to dissolve her marriage.
The hila is a temporary solution until a judge can be found.
2
State the condition for its application
When can the community substitute for a judge? Only when there is no judge (hakim) available, either in reality or figuratively.
'In reality' means no qualified judge exists; 'figuratively' may mean the judge is inaccessible or unfit.
3
Distinguish the scope
Which marital matters does this cover? Only dissolution of marriage ties (mukhasasat), not all judicial matters.
The community's authority is limited to this specific type of case.
4
Analyze the procedural questions
The query raises two main issues: (1) How should the community proceed? (a) collectively as a whole, or (b) delegate to a just scholar? (2) If collective, how is validity upheld given that the Maliki school requires individual judgment?
These questions were left to the Maliki scholars for clarification.
5
Recognize the inter-madhhab dimension
The query is directed to Maliki scholars because the hila originates from the Maliki school. Hanafis are seeking clarification before adopting it fully.
This shows cross-madhhab interaction in legal problem-solving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الاستفتاء بالمرة الخامسة
الحمد لله وكفى وسلام على عباده الذين اصطفى اما بعد فالمعروض على ساداتنا العلماء المالكية انه قد اختار بعض [؟]احنات الهند ما صرح به المالكية من ان جماعة المسلمين تقوم مقام الحاكم في فصل المخصصات عند عدم الحاكم حا او معنى ولكن وردت على ذلك اسئلة تكتبها اليكم والمأمول من جنابكوان تشرفونا بالجواب عنها مع الدليل توجروا عند الله الجليل
الاول - اعنى ول الاسئلة قد صرحوا ان زوجة المفقود ومثلها ترفع امرها الى جماعة المسلمين عند عدم الحاكم لكن لم نجد في كتبهم كيفية قضاء الجماعة هل تلى تلك الجماعة بإجمعها سماع القضية وفصلها ام تقرض امرها الى عالم عدل يقضى فيها.
الثاني وعلى الشق الاول اذا وليت الجماعة باجمعها [؟]شبهتات (الف) اذا ثبت عند المالكية ان تفرد القاضي في القضاء واجب والقضاء المشترك باطل فكيف يصح القضاء المشترك من الجماعة اليس هذا الحكم قضاء وان لم يكن قضاء فما ذا [؟]تشمونه رباء) هل يشترط اتفاق الجماعة على [؟]الحكوام لا وان لم يكن الاتفاق شرطا فكيف السبيل الى ترجيح رأى على رأى هل يرجح بالكثرة امر يمر عمر غيرها والذي نهنا ان الاتفاق على رأى شرط النفاذ الحكم من الجماعة وان لعد نجد هذا مصر حا لكن قناء على ما إذا حكم الخصمان رجلين اور جالا
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The fifth query. Praise be to Allah, and sufficient is He, and peace be upon His chosen servants. To proceed: Presented to our masters, the Maliki scholars: Some Hanafis of India have chosen what the Malikis have stated, that the Muslim community stands in place of the judge in dissolving marriage ties (mukhasasat) when there is no judge, either in reality or figuratively. But questions have arisen regarding that, which we write to you. We hope that you will honor us with answers along with evidence, and you will be rewarded by Allah the Mighty. First: Among the questions, they have stated that the wife of a missing person and the like take her matter to the Muslim community when there is no judge. But we did not find in their books the manner of the community's judgment: whether that community as a whole hears the case and decides it, or they delegate it to a just scholar who judges it. Second: Regarding the first possibility, if the community as a whole undertakes it, [؟] doubts arise: (a) If it is established in the Maliki school that the individual judicial authority is obligatory and collective judgment is void, then how can collective judgment by the community be valid? Is this not judgment? And if it is not judgment, then what do you call it? [؟] Is agreement of the community on the ruling required? If agreement is not a condition, then how is one opinion preferred over another? Is preference by majority? Or by something else? And our opinion here is that agreement on a ruling is a condition for the enforceability of the community's judgment, but we do not find this explicitly stated, except that it is based on the case where two men or more judge between the disputants...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is a query (istifta') addressed to Maliki scholars by some Hanafis of India. It concerns the legal stratagem (hila) of using the Muslim community as a substitute for a judge in dissolving marriages, particularly for the wife of a missing husband. The query raises two main issues: (1) How should the community proceed? Should all members hear the case or delegate to a just scholar? (2) If the community judges collectively, how can this be valid given the Maliki principle that individual judgment is obligatory and collective judgment void? The query also asks about the requirement of consensus and how to resolve disagreements. The text breaks off mid-sentence. This passage shows that the author was engaging with Maliki scholars to clarify the practical implementation of the hila.

Key Terms
جماعة المسلمين (jama'at al-muslimin): The body of Muslims that acts as a substitute for a judge in the absence of a qualified judge
المفقود (al-mafqud): A missing person whose whereabouts are unknown
فصل المخصصات (fasl al-mukhasasat): Dissolution of marriage ties (specifically for the wife of a missing person)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what is the primary condition for the Muslim community to act as a judge for dissolving the marriage of a missing husband's wife?
A) The husband must be missing for more than four years.
B) The community must include a Maliki scholar.
C) No qualified judge (hakim) is available.
D) The wife must have permission from her guardian.

Key Takeaway
The hila of community judgment for missing husbands is valid only if no judge exists and only for dissolution, but its procedural details require further clarification from Maliki scholars.
